Tayammum for Fear of Missing Funeral Prayer
Ruling on tayammum for fear of missing funeral prayer with refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when fear of missing a funeral prayer justifies tayammum according to Hanafi fiqh, identify the exception for the guardian, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on the guardian's eligibility.

Core Idea
Fear of missing a funeral prayer excuses tayammum because it has no substitute—but the guardian loses this excuse unless someone else leads.

The funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) is unique: if missed, it cannot be made up (qada). This non-substitutability forms the basis for allowing tayammum when one genuinely fears missing it. However, the person entitled to lead the prayer—the guardian (wali)—normally controls the timing, so he cannot claim this fear. This passage from Maraqi al-Falah and its commentary refines the ruling, addressing exceptions and a key dispute within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
Read the first part: fear of missing a funeral prayer is an excuse for tayammum, even for a junub. The basis: the funeral prayer has no substitute (لا خلف له). This is the core principle.
2
Locate the exception for the guardian
The passage states that the wali (guardian) does not fear missing it—therefore he cannot use this excuse. Understand who the wali is: the person entitled to lead (sultan, imam, etc.).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Hidayah declared the correct view restricts the guardian. But Zahir al-Riwayah allows tayammum for everyone because delaying the funeral is disliked (makruh). Al-Sarkhasi supported the latter. This is a legitimate difference.
4
Examine the ruling when another funeral arrives
If a second funeral arrives before the person can do wudu, he prays it with his first tayammum according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn). Imam Muhammad requires repetition. This affects practical fatwa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage indicates that the fatwa adopts the Sahibayn's view (no repetition) and the allowance of tayammum for all (Zahir al-Riwayah), though the correct view in al-Hidayah restricts the guardian. The latter is supported by al-Sarkhasi.
Mufta bihi: tayammum permitted for all (including guardian if someone else leads), no repetition for second funeral.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) من العذر (خوف فوت صلاة جنازة) ولو جنباً لأنها تفوت بلا خلف فإن كان يدرك تكبيرة منها توضأ، والولي لا يخاف الفوت، هو الصحيح فلا يتيمم وإذا حضرت جنازة أخرى قبل القدرة على الوضوء صلى عليها بتيممه للأولى عندهما وقال محمد عليه الإعادة كما لو قدر ثم عجز قوله : (ولو) جنباً) لأن صلاة الجنازة دعاء في الحقيقة وإنما أو جبنا لها التيمم لكونها مسماة بإسم الصلاة قاله السيد قوله : (لأنها تفوت بلا خلف هذا هو الأصل في هذا الباب وهو أن ما يفوت إلى خلف لا خوف فوته، وما لا خلف له له قوله : ( والولي) لا يخاف الفوت) المراد بالولي من حق التقدم كالسلطان، ونحوه لأنّ الولي إذا كان لا يجوز له التيمم، وهو مؤخر. فمن هو مقدم عليه أولى، فيجوز التيمم للولي عند وجود من هو مقدم عليه إتفاقاً لأنه يخاف الفوت إذ ليس له حق الإعادة حينئذ قوله : (هو الصحيح) صححه في الهداية، وظاهر الرواية جواز التيمم للكل لأن تأخير الجنازة مكروه وصححه السرخسي، فتأيد التصحيح الثاني بكونه ظاهر الرواية . قوله : (قبل القدرة على الوضوء أما بعد القدرة يعيده إتفاقاً . قوله : (أو خوف فوت صلاة عيد)
And from the excuses is the fear of missing a funeral prayer, even for a junub (impure person), because it passes without a substitute. If he can catch even one takbir of it, he performs wudu. The guardian (wali) does not fear missing it – this is the correct view – so he does not perform tayammum. And if another funeral arrives before he is able to perform wudu, he prays over it with his tayammum from the first one, according to them (the two companions). Muhammad said: Repetition is required upon him, just as if he was able and then became incapable. He said: 'Even if junub' – because the funeral prayer is essentially a supplication, and we only obligated tayammum for it because it is called a prayer, as al-Sayyid said. He said: 'Because it passes without a substitute' – this is the principle in this chapter: that which can be substituted is not feared for being missed, but that which has no substitute is feared. He said: 'The guardian does not fear missing it' – the guardian is the one who has the right to lead, like the sultan and the like. Because when the guardian is not allowed to perform tayammum, and he is delayed, then one who is ahead of him is more entitled. So tayammum is permissible for the guardian when there is someone ahead of him, unanimously, because he fears it will be missed, as he then has no right to repeat it. He said: 'This is the correct view' – it was declared correct in al-Hidayah, and the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) permits tayammum for everyone because delaying the funeral is disliked (makruh). Al-Sarkhasi declared it correct, so the second correction is supported because it is the apparent narration. He said: 'Before he is able to perform wudu' – but after he is able, he repeats it, by agreement. He said: 'Or fear of missing the Eid prayer.'
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage discusses tayammum due to fear of missing a funeral prayer. The base text states that this excuse permits tayammum even for a person in major impurity (junub), because the funeral prayer cannot be repeated (it has no substitute). However, if a person can catch at least one takbir of the funeral prayer with wudu, he must perform wudu. The guardian (the one entitled to lead the funeral prayer, like the sultan or imam) is not allowed to perform tayammum because he cannot fear missing it (since he can postpone or repeat it later), but this is the correct view; some say he can. The commentary explains that the funeral prayer is essentially a supplication, so tayammum is allowed for it despite its name being prayer. The key principle: if an act has a substitute (e.g., missed prayer can be made up later), then fear of missing it is not an excuse for tayammum. If it has no substitute, the fear is a valid excuse. The guardian does not fear missing it because he can have someone else lead it and he can still get the reward; but if there is someone ahead of him in sequence (like the ruler), the guardian can then fear missing it and thus perform tayammum by agreement. There is a dispute: al-Hidayah declared the correct view is that the guardian does not perform tayammum, but the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) allows tayammum for all because delaying the funeral is disliked. The passage ends with a brief mention of fear of missing Eid prayer, which serves as another excuse.

Key Terms
خوف فوت صلاة جنازة (khawf fawt salat janazah): Fear of missing the funeral prayer, an excuse permitting tayammum
ولي (wali): The guardian entitled to lead the funeral prayer (sultan, imam, or next of kin with precedence)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is the guardian (wali) permitted to perform tayammum for fear of missing a funeral prayer?
A) Never, because he can always delay the funeral
B) Only if he is in a state of janabah
C) When there is someone ahead of him who can lead the prayer
D) Always, because delaying the funeral is disliked

Key Takeaway
Fear of missing the funeral prayer is a valid excuse for tayammum because it has no substitute, but the guardian loses this excuse unless a more rightful person leads.

Tayammum for Funeral Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Wali
Intra-Hanafi dispute on tayammum for funeral prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for fear of missing funeral prayer and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the wali and repetition of tayammum.

Core Idea
The funeral prayer is irreplaceable — its loss justifies tayammum, but the wali's ability to delegate creates an intra-Hanafi dispute.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when can a person perform tayammum due to fear of missing the funeral prayer? The key principle is that acts lost without a substitute (like janazah) permit tayammum, while those with a substitute (like Zuhr for Jumu'ah) do not. The debate centers on the wali (the one with right to lead) and whether he truly fears loss, and what happens if a second funeral arrives.

Guided Path
1
State the general ruling on tayammum for funeral prayer
Identify that fear of missing the funeral prayer is a valid excuse for tayammum, even in janabah, because the prayer is lost without a substitute. Note the condition: if one can catch a single takbir with wudu, wudu is required.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on the wali
Recognize that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that the wali does not fear loss and thus should not perform tayammum, while Muhammad al-Shaybani argues he can fear loss if someone ahead is present.
The wali is one with priority to lead, like a ruler or imam.
3
Follow the proofs for each position
Analyze the principle 'what is lost without a substitute causes fear' and how it applies to the wali. Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf: the wali can delegate, so no fear. Muhammad: if someone ahead exists, the wali fears loss because he cannot repeat the prayer.
4
Analyse the second funeral scenario
Determine the ruling when a second funeral arrives before ability to perform wudu. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow praying with the same tayammum; Muhammad requires repetition (i'ada) if ability arises later.
This difference hinges on whether tayammum is considered valid for multiple prayers once performed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Note that al-Hidayah declares the restrictive view (no tayammum for wali) as sahih, but the apparent riwaya (zahir al-riwaya) permits it. Later fatwas often adopt the permissive view to avoid delaying the funeral.
Authority weight: restrictive = al-Hidayah; permissive = zahir al-riwaya supported by al-Sarakhsi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) من العذر (خوف فوت صلاة جنازة) ولو جنباً لأنها تفوت بلا خلف فإن كان يدرك تكبيرة منها توضأ، والولي لا يخاف الفوت، هو الصحيح فلا يتيمم وإذا حضرت جنازة أخرى قبل القدرة على الوضوء صلى عليها بتيممه للأولى عندهما وقال محمد عليه الإعادة كما لو قدر ثم عجز. قوله : (ولو) جنباً) لأن صلاة الجنازة دعاء في الحقيقة وإنما أوجبنا لها التيمم لكونها مسماة بإسم الصلاة قاله السيد. قوله : (لأنها تفوت بلا خلف) هذا هو الأصل في هذا الباب وهو أن ما يفوت إلى خلف لا خوف فوته، وما لا خلف له له. قوله : ( والولي) لا يخاف الفوت) المراد بالولي من حق التقدم كالسلطان، ونحوه لأن الولي إذا كان لا يجوز له التيمم، وهو مؤخر. فمن هو مقدم عليه أولى، فيجوز التيمم للولي عند وجود من هو مقدم عليه إتفاقاً لأنه يخاف الفوت إذ ليس له حق الإعادة حينئذ. قوله : (هو الصحيح) صححه في الهداية، وظاهر الرواية جواز التيمم للكل لأن تأخير الجنازة مكروه وصححه السرخسي، فتأيد التصحيح الثاني بكونه ظاهر الرواية . قوله : (قبل القدرة على الوضوء أما بعد القدرة يعيده إتفاقاً
(And) among the excuses (is fear of missing a funeral prayer) even if in a state of major impurity (janabah) because it is lost without a substitute. If he can catch one takbir of it with wudu, he should perform wudu. The wali (guardian) does not fear loss; this is the correct view, so he does not perform tayammum. If another funeral arrives before he is able to perform wudu, he prays over it with his tayammum from the first, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and Muhammad said: he must repeat it, just as if he had ability and then became incapable. His statement: (even if) in janabah because the funeral prayer is essentially a supplication, and we only obligated tayammum for it because it is named prayer, so said al-Sayyid. His statement: (because it is lost without a substitute) this is the principle in this chapter: whatever is lost to a substitute, there is no fear of its loss, and whatever has no substitute, there is fear. His statement: (the wali does not fear loss) the intended meaning of wali is one who has the right to precedence, like the sultan and similar, because if the wali is not permitted to do tayammum and he is delayed, then whoever is ahead of him is more entitled. So tayammum is permitted for the wali when there is someone ahead of him by agreement because he fears loss since he does not have the right to repeat then. His statement: (this is the correct view) he corrected it in al-Hidayah, but the apparent riwaya permits tayammum for all because delaying the funeral is disliked, and al-Sarakhsi corrected it, so the second correction is supported as it is the apparent riwaya. His statement: (before ability to perform wudu; but after ability he repeats it by agreement).
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding tayammum for fear of missing a funeral prayer. The base ruling states that fear of missing the funeral prayer (صلاة الجنازة) is a valid excuse for tayammum, even if one is in a state of major impurity (جنب). The rationale is that the funeral prayer is 'lost without a substitute' (تفوت بلا خلف), meaning if you miss it, there is no other prayer that can replace it. This is contrasted with other prayers like Fajr which can be made up (qada). The text then details: if a person can still catch at least one takbir of the funeral prayer by performing wudu, he must do wudu and not resort to tayammum. The 'wali' (ولي) - the person with priority to lead the prayer, such as the ruler or imam - is not considered to 'fear loss' because he can delegate or delay, so he should not do tayammum. This is the 'sahih' (correct) view according to al-Hidayah. However, the 'zahir al-riwaya' (apparent transmitted position) permits tayammum for all, including the wali, since delaying the funeral is makruh. The commentary by al-Sayyid explains that the funeral prayer is essentially a du'a (supplication) but was named prayer to necessitate tayammum. The principle is restated: any act that has a substitute (like Zuhr for Jumu'ah) does not cause fear of loss; any act without a substitute (like Janazah) does. The dispute continues: if a second funeral arrives before the person gains ability to perform wudu, does he use the same tayammum from the first? According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ('indahuma), he prays the second funeral with the same tayammum without repetition. But Muhammad al-Shaybani says he must repeat (i'ada) the tayammum if he later becomes able to do wudu (e.g., water becomes available). The commentary notes that if after the prayers he becomes capable of wudu, he does not need to repeat the funeral prayer by agreement; but Muhammad's view of i'ada applies only if he had ability and then lost it. The correct view for the wali is that he does not do tayammum because he can always find another to lead, but if someone ahead of him is present, he can do tayammum by consensus because he truly fears loss.

Key Terms
خلف (khalf): A substitute or replacement for an act of worship, e.g., Zuhr prayer is a substitute for Jumu'ah, qada for missed fard prayers.
ولي (wali): The person who has the primary right to lead the funeral prayer, such as the ruler or the local imam. In this context, the wali is contrasted with a regular person who has no one ahead of him.
إعادة (i'ada): Repetition of the tayammum or prayer due to a change in circumstances, such as gaining ability to use water after the initial tayammum.
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using pure earth, performed as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or its use is harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view in al-Hidayah, when is the wali (guardian) allowed to perform tayammum for a funeral prayer?
A) He is never allowed because he can always delegate.
B) He is allowed if there is someone ahead of him who can lead.
C) He is allowed only if he is in a state of janabah.
D) He is always allowed because delaying the funeral is makruh.

Key Takeaway
The funeral prayer's irreplaceability justifies tayammum, but the wali's ability to delegate creates a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute where the mufta bihi often favors the permissive view to avoid delay.

Tayammum for Non-Qada Prayers: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on tayammum when fear of missing janazah or eid prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on tayammum for fear of missing a non-qada prayer and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding Eid prayer.

Core Idea
Tayammum is permitted only for prayers lost forever without substitute; the Sahibayn differ on Eid.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi unpacks a critical exception: when a prayer cannot be made up, the Hanafi school allows tayammum even if water is present. The text grounds this in hadith and then dives into a foundational disagreement among the school's founders over whether Eid prayer truly qualifies. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to apply the principle of 'fawt la ila badal' and recognize where the mufta bihi position lies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its basis
The passage opens by stating that tayammum is allowed for janazah and Eid prayers because they are lost with no substitute. Identify the hadith of Ibn Abbas as the primary proof.
The hadith explicitly mentions janazah; Eid is analogized.
2
Distinguish non-qada prayers from those with substitute
List prayers that have no qada (janazah, Eid, eclipse) versus those that do (Friday, missed fard). Note that Friday has zuhr as a substitute, and missed fard can be made up.
This distinction is the key to the ruling.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on Eid
Contrast Imam Abu Hanifa's view (tayammum allowed even if part of Eid can be caught with wudu) with the Sahibayn's view (tayammum not allowed if any part can be caught).
The root cause: whether Eid prayer has a substitute (qada).
4
Analyze the reasoning behind the difference
Imam holds Eid has no qada; Sahibayn hold it can be performed individually. Also consider the imam's fear of corruption due to crowding.
The passage also discusses 'building' (bana') if hadath occurs during the prayer.
5
Apply the principle to other cases
The passage extends the ruling to eclipse prayers (kusuf/khusuf) by analogy and mentions that tayammum is allowed for acts not requiring purification, such as greeting or entering a mosque.
This shows the broader principle: necessity overrides normal rules.

Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage is a detailed intra-Hanafi legal discussion on when fear of missing a specific prayer justifies performing tayammum in place of wudu. It begins by stating the ruling: if one fears missing a funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) or the two Eid prayers due to lack of wudu, he may perform tayammum. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas: if a funeral prayer suddenly comes upon you and you fear missing it, pray upon it with tayammum. Similarly, Ibn Umar performed tayammum for a funeral. The author notes that funeral and Eid prayers are lost without substitute (la ila badal), meaning they cannot be made up later. Then it discusses 'building' (bana') upon tayammum: if an event (hadath) occurred during these prayers, one may build upon tayammum and continue. Fear of missing Friday prayer or the time is not an excuse because Friday has a substitute (zuhr prayer) and missed prayers can be made up. The commentary then explores the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The fundamental difference: Imam holds that Eid prayer, if missed or invalidated, is not qada (made up) — thus it is lost without substitute, justifying tayammum. The Sahibayn hold that Eid prayer can be performed individually after the congregation, so it is not completely lost. Hence, according to them, if a person could catch part of it by performing wudu, he should not do tayammum. However, if he already started tayammum, he may continue. The passage also extends the ruling to eclipse prayers (kusuf and khusuf), analogizing to Eid since they are also non-qada. Finally, tayammum is allowed for any act that does not require formal purification (tahara), such as sleeping, greeting, entering a mosque for one in a state of hadath — even if water is available, though this is a lenient view.

Key Terms
فوت (fawt): The loss of a prayer that cannot be made up later (e.g., janazah, eid, eclipse).
بدل (badal): A substitute prayer that can be performed later (qada) or alternative like zuhr for jumu'ah.
بناء (bana'): Continuing a prayer after tayammum upon the same intention, without restarting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because Eid prayer has no qada (substitute)
C) Because Eid prayer is not obligatory
D) Because the time is short

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits tayammum for any prayer that cannot be made up, with Imam Abu Hanifa extending this to Eid prayer despite the Sahibayn's objection.

The Substance for Tayammum: Purity and Earth Type
Definition and examples of permissible tayammum materials

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the substance used in tayammum and identify which materials are valid according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Tayammum is valid with any pure earth substance – dust, sand, stone, minerals – not only dust.

This lesson examines the third condition for the validity of tayammum: the substance must be pure (tahir) and belong to the 'genus of earth' (jins al-ard). The Hanafi school accepts a broad range of materials, distinguishing itself from other madhahib. We will explore the evidence from the Quran and the principles that guide the Hanafi interpretation, including the distinction between raw minerals and processed metals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and its proof
The third condition of tayammum is that the substance used must be pure and from the genus of earth. The proof is the Quranic verse 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban' (4:43).
The word 'sa'id' is key to the Hanafi expansion.
2
Define 'sa'id' and 'tayyib'
'Sa'id' means the face of the earth, encompassing all types of earth. 'Tayyib' means pure and purifying. The Hanafi interpretation sees 'tayyib' as requiring both purity and the ability to purify.
The author of the commentary clarifies that 'tayyib' here means pure, not just good.
3
List valid and invalid substances
Valid: dust, sand, smooth stone, clay, ochre, mineral stones (raw). Invalid: glass, wood, metals (cast), coral, substances that turn to ash or melt.
The general rule: anything that burns to ash or melts is not from the genus of earth.
4
Apply the general rule
Use the criterion: if a substance was originally from earth but transformed by fire or industry, it is invalid. Example: glass from sand is invalid; raw gold in a mine is valid.
Metals before smelting are valid because they are still in their mineral state.
5
Note intra-Hanafi differences and the mufta bihi
Abu Yusuf restricts to dust only; Abu Hanifa and Muhammad allow a broader range. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view.
Smooth stone is valid according to Abu Hanifa but Muhammad reportedly disagreed. The later Hanafi tarjih favors permissibility.

Source Text

Source pages p. 118

Commentary
This passage defines the third condition of tayammum: the substance used must be pure (tahir) and from the genus of earth (jins al-ard). The author explains that 'tayyib' in the Quranic verse means both clean and purifying. The substance must be inherently pure, meaning it has not been touched by impurity even if the impurity's trace has disappeared. It then enumerates what qualifies: dust, sand, smooth stone, clay, and various minerals are permissible according to the majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), though Abu Yusuf restricts to dust only. The passage provides a general rule: any substance that becomes ash when burned or melts is not permissible (e.g., wood, metals like gold, silver, copper, iron). However, exceptions are noted: metals in their raw mineral state are permissible because they are from the earth. The passage also discusses marginal cases: coral is not permissible because it is solidified plant, not earth; burnt clay without dung is permissible; grave dust is permissible unless impurity is certain; glass is not permissible even if made from sand because it is transformed. The proof is the Quranic verse (4:43) 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban', and the word 'sa'id' is interpreted as the face of the earth, including all its types. The commentary reconciles the generalization with the predominant interpretation as dust, noting that restricting the absolute by a solitary hadith or companion statement is not allowed.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): The face of the earth, including all types: dust, sand, stone, clay, etc.
طيب (tayyib): Pure and purifying (tahir wa mutahhir).
جنس الأرض (jins al-ard): The genus of earth: substances that are originally from the earth and do not transform into something else (like metal or ash).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid substance for tayammum according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) Pure dust
B) Smooth stone
C) Gold (cast)
D) Burnt clay without dung

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid with any pure substance from the genus of earth, including dust, sand, stone, and minerals, provided it does not burn to ash or melt.

Valid and Invalid Substances for Tayammum
Ruling on valid materials for tayammum with Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi general principle (dabit) to classify any substance as valid or invalid for tayammum and identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on minerals.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school permits tayammum on any natural earth surface—stones, sand, minerals—based on the general meaning of 'sa'id'.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the Hanafi ruling on which materials make tayammum valid. The common assumption is that only pure dust works, but the Hanafi school expands this to include smooth stone, sand, and even mineral substances—provided they are natural and not transformed by fire. The commentator also resolves an inner-school dispute between Abu Yusuf and the Sahibayn and provides a clear principle to test any material.

Guided Path
1
Identify the valid substances listed
Read the passage and list the substances explicitly mentioned as valid: dust, smooth stone, sand, orpiment, lime, ochre, kohl, sulfur, turquoise, agate, other mineral stones, mountain salt, burnt earth, burnt clay (without dung), and earth mixed with something else as long as earth dominates.
Burnt earth is valid only if ash does not dominate.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that the first three (dust, stone, sand) are agreed upon, but for minerals like orpiment, Abu Yusuf alone opposes. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) permit them. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn position.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Extract the general principle (dabit) for invalid substances
The commentator gives a rule: anything that turns to ash when burned or can be molded by fire (i.e., metals) is invalid. Examples: firewood, gold, silver, copper, iron. Note that gold and silver before casting (as ore) are valid.
This principle helps classify new materials.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
The proof is Quran 4:43 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban'. The word 'sa'id' is general for the face of the earth. The commentator cites 18:40 'sa'idan zalaq' (smooth stone) to show that 'sa'id' includes stone, not just dust. Thus the Hanafi school retains the general meaning.
The Shafi'i school interprets 'sa'id' specifically as dust.
5
Apply the principle to a new substance
Given a substance like 'plastic' (a petroleum product that melts), determine its validity: it is not natural earth, and if it melts by fire, it falls under the dabit and is invalid. For natural clay that is not burnt, it is valid.
Always check if the substance is originally earth and not transformed by fire.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهو (كالتراب) المنبث وغيره والحجر) الأملس (والرمل) عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف فيجوز عندهما بالزرنيخ والنورة والمغرة والكحل والكبريت والفيروزج والعقيق وسائر أحجار المعادن وبالملح الجبلي في الصحيح وبالأرض المحترقة والطين المحرق الذي ليس به سرقین قبله والأرض المحترقة إن لم يغلب عليها الرماد وبالتراب الغالب على مخالط من غير جنس الأرض لأنه (لا) يصح التيمم بنحو الحطب والفضة والذهب والنحاس والحديد وضابطه أن كل شيء يصير ) رماداً، أو ينطبع بالإحراق لا يجوز به التيمم والإجاز لقوله تعالى: فتيمموا صعيداً طيباً والصعيد اسم لوجه الأرض تراباً كان أو غيره وتفسيره بالتراب لكونه أغلب لقوله تعالى صعيداً زلقاً أي حجراً أملس
And it [is valid with] (like dust) that is scattered and other [dust], and (stone) that is smooth, and (sand) according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), contrary to Abu Yusuf. So according to them, it is permissible with orpiment, lime, ochre, kohl, sulfur, turquoise, agate, and all other mineral stones, and with mountain salt in the correct [view], and with burnt earth, and burnt clay that has no dung in it before burning, and with burnt earth provided ash does not dominate it, and with dust that is predominant over a mixture of something not of the same type as earth. Because (it is not valid to perform tayammum with like firewood, silver, gold, copper, and iron). The principle is: everything that turns into ash or becomes moldable by burning is not permissible for tayammum. And it is permitted due to His statement: 'so perform tayammum with pure earth' (4:43). And 'sa'id' is a name for the face of the earth, whether it be dust or otherwise. And its interpretation as dust is because it is more common, based on His statement: 'a slippery sa'id', meaning smooth stone.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the ruling on substances valid for tayammum. The matn states that tayammum is valid with dust, smooth stone, and sand. The commentator notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani) — the two — these and other mineral substances like orpiment, lime, ochre, etc., are valid; but Abu Yusuf alone holds they are not. The relied-upon (sahih) position is that mountain salt is permissible. Burnt earth and clay are valid as long as they are not mixed with impurity (like dung) and ash does not dominate. The general principle (dabit) is: anything that turns to ash by burning or can be molded by fire is invalid for tayammum — such as wood, metals like gold, silver, copper, iron. Gold and silver before crafting (as ore) are considered earth and thus valid. The proof is Quran 4:43: 'fa-tayammamu sa'idan tayyiban'. The word 'sa'id' literally means face of the earth, including stone and soil. Although some interpret it as dust (turab) due to common usage, the commentator argues against restricting it, citing another verse (18:40) where 'sa'id zalaq' means smooth stone, thereby proving 'sa'id' is general. Thus the Hanafi school permits tayammum on any natural surface of the earth.

Key Terms
صعيد (sa'id): The face of the earth, including soil, sand, stone, and minerals.
ضابط (dabit): General rule: anything that turns to ash or melts by fire is invalid for tayammum.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is valid on any natural earth surface that does not turn to ash or melt by fire, as supported by the general meaning of 'sa'id' in the Quran.

Conditions of Tayammum: Wiping Extent and Number of Strikes
Explanation of the fourth, fifth, and sixth conditions of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions of tayammum (covering the full face and hands to elbows, wiping with most of the hand, and two strikes), explain the relied-upon Hanafi position and its proof, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi differences on the extent of the hands.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires complete wiping of face and forearms to elbows, using most of the hand, with two strikes — the hadith defines the limits.

This lesson unpacks the fourth, fifth, and sixth conditions of tayammum as detailed in the Hanafi text. We will examine the requirement to cover every part of the face and forearms with dust, the obligation to wipe using most of the hand or an equivalent, and the necessity of performing two separate strikes. The passage also presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether the hands must be wiped to the elbows or only to the wrists, and clarifies the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position derived from the Prophet's ﷺ practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions
From the passage, list the fourth, fifth, and sixth conditions of tayammum. Note that each condition is explicitly numbered in the text.
The fourth condition is isti'ab al-mahal (covering the entire part). The fifth is using the whole or most of the hand. The sixth is performing two strikes.
2
Analyze the requirement of complete coverage
Understand that the relied-upon view demands wiping all skin and hair of the face (including area between sideburn and ear) and the hands to the elbows. Contrast the weak opinion that only most of the face suffices.
The text mentions removing the ring and passing fingers through the beard to ensure complete coverage.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on hand extent
Compare the zahir al-riwaya position (hands to elbows) with the narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad that Abu Hanifa said to the wrists. Determine why the former is mufta bihi.
The hadith explicitly states 'to the elbows,' so it takes precedence over qiyas to wudu.
4
Understand the fifth condition: using most of the hand
The wiping must be done with the entire hand or most of it, or something equivalent (like a substitute hand or moving the dust-affected body part). Wiping with only two fingers does not suffice unless repeated.
The source contrasts this with head wiping where a part suffices.
5
Verify the necessity of two strikes
The sixth condition requires two distinct strikes: one for the face and one for the forearms. The hadith and the Prophet's demonstration are cited as proof. Note that a single strike for both is invalid by Hanafi ruling.
This is a point of difference with the Shafi'i school, which allows one strike.

And it is said that wiping most of the face and hands is sufficient. And it was corrected, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is to the wrists, which is the face of the apparent transmission. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Tayammum is two strikes: one strike for the face and one strike for the forearms up to the elbows.' And similarly he did it, because he was asked: 'How should I wipe?' Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage details three conditions for tayammum. The fourth condition is isti'ab al-mahal: covering the entire part (face and hands to elbows) with wiping. The relied-upon (zahir al-riwaya) view is that wiping must cover all the skin and hair of the face, including the area between the sideburn and ear, and the hands including the fingers. This necessitates removing rings and khuff? and passing fingers through the beard. However, there is a weak view that wiping most (more than half) suffices. Another narration from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reports Abu Hanifa saying the hands are only to the wrists. The proof for the full extent is the hadith: 'Tayammum is two strokes: one for the face, one for the forearms to the elbows,' and the Prophet's actual demonstration. The fifth condition: the wiping must be done with the entire hand or most of it (or something equivalent like a substitute hand or moving the face through dust). Wiping with two fingers only does not suffice unless repeated to cover the area. The sixth condition: the act must consist of two strikes (not one). The palms (or their inner sides?) are used in striking. The text mentions striking with the inner palms, but other sources say both inner and outer. The purpose is to acquire enough dust for wiping.

Key Terms
استيعاب المحل (isti'ab al-mahal): Covering the entire area required to be wiped (face and hands to elbows) with the dust.
ضربتين (darbatayn): Two strikes of the hands on the ground, one for face and one for arms.

Requirement to Wipe Entire Face and Hands in Tayammum
Ruling on covering entire face and hands in tayammum with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi position on the extent of wiping in tayammum and identify the dalil (hadith) that supports it.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires wiping the entire face and hands to the elbows — the hadith of two strikes is the proof.

Tayammum, the dry ablution when water is unavailable, has specific requirements. This passage clarifies the obligatory extent of wiping: according to the relied-upon transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), one must wipe the entire face and both forearms up to the elbows. The proof is the Prophet's explicit statement and practice. While alternative views exist within the school, the mufta bihi demands complete coverage, ensuring tayammum's validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping in tayammum. The ruling is that it must cover the entire face and hands to the elbows. This is considered wajib based on the relied-upon transmission.
The alternative view (qīla) holds that most suffices, but it is not the mufta bihi.
2
Locate the dalil
The dalil is the hadith: 'Tayammum is two strikes: a strike for the face and a strike for the forearms to the elbows,' and the associated practice of the Prophet.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit mention of 'two strikes' and specifying the areas (face and forearms to elbows) indicates that wiping must cover those entire areas. The Prophet's demonstration confirms this.
The imperative nature of the action implies obligation (wujub).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Within the Hanafi school, there are variant views: one from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) that it is to the wrists, and another that wiping most of the face suffices.
These are not the relied-upon position.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The author (Al-Tahtawi) affirms that the Zahir al-Riwayah is the correct and fatwa-worthy view, supported by the hadith and practice.
The mufta bihi is complete covering.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استيعاب المحل) وهو الوجه واليدان إلى المرفقين (بالمسح) في ظاهر الرواية وهو الصحيح المفتى به فينزع الخاتم ويخلل الأصابع ويمسح جميع بشرة الوجه والشعر على الصحيح وما بين العذار والأذن إلحاقاً له بأصله وقيل يكفي مسح أكثر الوجه واليدين، . وصحح وروى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة : أنه إلى الرسغين وجه ظاهر الرواية قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «التيمم ضربتان ضربة للوجه وضربة للذراعين إلى المرفقين وكذا فعله عليه السلام لأنه سئل كيف أمسح فضرب بكفيه الأرض، ثم رفعهما لوجهه ثم ضرب ضربة فمسح ذراعيه باطنهما وظاهرهما حتى مسح بيديه المرفقين
Covering the place [i.e., the entire face and hands to the elbows] by wiping, according to the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), and it is the correct and fatwa-worthy view. So he removes the ring, interlaces the fingers, and wipes all the skin of the face and hair on the correct view, and [wipes] between the chin and ear, annexing it to its origin. It was said that wiping most of the face and hands suffices. And it was authenticated, and al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is to the wrists. The basis of the apparent transmission is the saying of the Prophet ﷺ: 'Tayammum is two strikes: a strike for the face and a strike for the forearms to the elbows.' Similarly, his action ﷺ, because he was asked, 'How do I wipe?' So he struck his palms on the ground, then raised them to his face, then struck a strike and wiped his forearms, their inner and outer, until he wiped his hands to the elbows.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the extent of wiping in tayammum. The author states that according to the Zahir al-Riwaya (the relied-upon transmission), it is mandatory to wipe the entire face and both hands up to the elbows. This necessitates removing any ring, interlaces fingers, and wiping all skin and hair. The alternative view (qīla) allows wiping most of the face and hands. The tarjīh (preference) is given to the Zahir al-Riwayah, supported by the hadith that tayammum consists of two strikes: one for the face and one for the forearms up to the elbows, and by the Prophet's demonstrated practice (fi‘l). The hadith is cited as the primary proof for the obligation of isti‘āb (covering the entire area).

Key Terms
استيعاب المحل (isti‘āb al-maḥall): Covering the entire area that must be wiped in tayammum (face and hands to elbows).
ظاهر الرواية (ẓāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent transmission from the six books of Imam Muhammad – the authoritative position of the Hanafi school.

Conditions of Tayammum: Fifth to Eighth
List and explanation of the fifth to eighth conditions of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fifth to eighth conditions of tayammum and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the two strikes.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires wiping most of the hand, two strikes (though not a pillar), purity at the time, and removal of barriers.

In this passage, the author lists four remaining conditions of tayammum, completing the prerequisites for this purification. Among them is a notable internal Hanafi debate: are the two strikes on the earth a required pillar or merely a customary means to obtain dust? Understanding these conditions ensures tayammum is performed correctly when water is unavailable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifth condition and its limits
The text states that one must wipe with the entire hand or most of it, or something equivalent. Wiping with only two fingers is insufficient unless repeated to cover the area. This contrasts with wiping the head where a part suffices.
The condition ensures full purification of the hands.
2
Analyze the sixth condition and the dispute
Tayammum must be performed with two strikes of the inner palms. The author then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: al-Isbijabi and Ibn al-Humam hold that the strike is not a rukn, while Shams al-A’imma considers it a rukn.
The dispute centers on whether the strikes are essential to the definition of tayammum.
3
Apply the seventh condition on purity
At the time of performing tayammum, one must be free from menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and minor impurity (hadath), just as for wudu.
This mirrors the conditions of wudu.
4
Recognize the eighth condition on barriers
Substances like wax or fat that prevent wiping on the skin must be removed, otherwise the wipe occurs on the substance, not the body.
Barriers invalidate the tayammum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(الخامس) من الشروط (أن يمسح بجميع اليد أو بأكثرها أو بما يقوم مقامه حتى لو مسح باصبعين لا يجوز) كما في الخلاصة (ولو كرر حتى استوعب بخلاف مسح الرأس كذا في السراج الوهاج عن الإيضاح (السادس) من الشروط أن يكون) التيمم (بضربتين بباطن (الكفين لما روبنا فإن نوى التيمم وأمر به غيره فيممه صح (ولو) كان الضربتان في مكان واحد على الأصح لعدم صيرورته مستعملاً لأن التيمم بما في اليد ويقوم مقام الضربتين إصابة التراب بجسده إذا مسحه بنية التيمم) حتى لو أحدث بعد الضرب أو إصابة التراب فمسحه يجوز على ما قاله الاسبيجابي كمن أحدث وفي كفيه ما يجوز به الطهارة وعلى ما اختاره شمس الأئمة لا يجوز لجعله الضرب ركناً كما لو أحدث بعد غسل عضو، وقال المحقق ابن الهمام: الذي يقتضيه النظر عدم اعتبار الضرب من مسمى التيمم شرعاً لأنّ المأمور به في الكتاب ليس إلا المسح وقوله : التيمم ضربتان خرج مخرج الغالب والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم (السابع) من الشروط انقطاع ما ينافيه حالة فعله من حيض أو نفاس أو حدث) كما هو شرط أصله (الثامن) منها (زوال) ما يمنع المسح على البشرة كشمع وشحم) لأنه يصير به المسح عليه لا على الجسد
(The fifth condition) is that one wipes with the entire hand or most of it or with something that serves as its substitute, so that if he wipes with two fingers it is not permissible, as in al-Khulasa. Even if he repeats until covering it entirely, unlike wiping the head, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj from al-Idah. (The sixth condition) is that tayammum should be with two strikes with the inner part of the palms, because we have narrated that if he intends tayammum and commands someone else to perform it, it is valid. Even if the two strikes are in one place, according to the most correct view, because it does not become used (musta‘mal). Because tayammum is by what is on the hand, and the two strikes can be replaced by dust reaching his body if he wipes it with the intention of tayammum. So if he has an event after striking or after dust reaching, and then wipes, it is permissible according to al-Isbijabi, like one who has an event while on his palms there is what purifies him. According to what Shams al-A’imma chose, it is not permissible because he considers the strike a pillar (rukn), as if he had an event after washing a limb. Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam said: what reason requires is that the strike is not considered part of the definition of tayammum legally, because what is commanded in the Book is only wiping, and his saying 'tayammum is two strikes' is indicative of the common case. And Allah knows best. (The seventh condition) is the cessation of what contradicts it at the time of action, such as menstrual bleeding, postpartum bleeding, or hadath, as is the condition for its origin. (The eighth) of them is the removal of what prevents wiping on the skin, such as wax or fat, because then the wiping is on it, not on the body.
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage enumerates four conditions of tayammum, from the fifth to the eighth, as counted in the text. The fifth condition: one must wipe with the entire hand or most of it or something equivalent (like another's hand). Wiping with only two fingers is not allowed unless one repeats until the whole area is covered—this is unlike wiping the head where a part suffices. The sixth condition: tayammum must be performed with two strikes of the inner palms. The author discusses a dispute: Is the strike a pillar? Al-Isbijabi holds that if one strikes or dust reaches and then he has an event (invalidator) before wiping, he may still wipe; Shams al-A’imma says not, because the strike is a rukn. Ibn al-Humam argues that the strike is not part of the definition of tayammum, as the Quran only mentions wiping (famsahu) and the hadith mentioning two strikes refers to the common practice. The seventh condition: the person performing tayammum must be free from menstrual bleeding, postpartum bleeding, and minor ritual impurity (hadath) at the time of action, just as in wudu. The eighth condition: any substance that prevents water from reaching the skin (like wax or fat) must be removed, otherwise the wiping occurs on the substance, not the skin itself.

Key Terms
ضربتان (ḍarbatān): Two strikes of the hands on the earth in tayammum, one for the face and one for the hands.
التيمم بما في اليد (al-tayammum bimā fī al-yad): The effect of tayammum is by the dust that sticks to the hand after striking, not the strike itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the sixth condition of tayammum?
A) Wiping with the entire hand
B) Performing two strikes with the inner palms
C) Removing wax and fat from the skin
D) Cessation of menstruation

Key Takeaway
The conditions of tayammum (fifth to eighth) require wiping most of the hand, two strikes (though not a pillar), purity at the time, and removal of barriers, with the dispute over strikes reflecting internal Hanafi legal development.

Tayammum: The Dispute Over Striking (Darb) as a Pillar
Hashiya commentary refining the ruling on tayammum pillars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the pillars of tayammum and explain why striking (darb) is not a pillar, using the Quranic evidence and the reasoning of Ibn al-Humam.

Core Idea
In tayammum, only wiping the face and hands is obligatory; striking the earth is a means, not a pillar.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the act of striking the earth (darb) is a pillar (rukn) of tayammum or merely a means to acquire dust. The matn of Maraqi al-Falah states the pillars as wiping the face and hands, omitting the strike. The hashya of al-Tahtawi reinforces this by citing Quranic evidence and the preferred view of later authorities. Understanding this distinction clarifies the scope of obligation in tayammum and its valid performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pillars of tayammum as stated in the matn
Read the text: 'وركناه مسح اليدين والوجه' – the two pillars are wiping the hands and the face. Notice that striking (darb) is not included.
The matn deliberately omits 'ضربتان' to indicate that striking is not a pillar.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi dispute
The commentary notes that Shams al-A'immah considered striking a pillar, while the majority (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, and later authorities like Ibn al-Humam) hold that it is not. Identify which view is mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi is that darb is not a rukn, as supported by Ibn al-Humam and al-Tahtawi.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse (4:43) commands 'famsahu' (wipe), not 'idribu' (strike). Ibn al-Humam argues that the command is only for wiping, and the hadith 'al-tayammum darbatan' describes the typical practice, not an essential requirement.
The imperative 'فامسحوا' is the operative text; it is qat'i in transmission and meaning.
4
Understand the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If darb is not a pillar, then tayammum performed with existing dust (without striking) is valid. If it were a pillar, such tayammum would be invalid. The mufta bihi view allows greater ease.
Example: a person with dusty hands from normal activity can perform tayammum without striking.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Scenario: A traveler has dust on his hands from a dusty surface. He wipes his face and arms without striking the earth. According to the mufta bihi, his tayammum is valid. Consider the opposite view of Shams al-A'immah for comparison.
Application to real life: this ruling is relevant for those in dusty environments or with limited mobility.

Book of Purity. And if he ordered someone else, so he performed tayammum for him, it is valid. (And if) the two wipes are in one place, the correct view is it is valid because it does not become used [water?]. Because tayammum is by what is on the hand, and striking the earth with his body when he wipes with the intention of tayammum takes the place of the two wipes. So if he had an event after the strike or hitting the earth and then wiped, it is permissible according to what al-Isbijabi said, like one who had an event and in his hands is what permits purification. And according to what Shams al-A'immah chose, it is not permissible because he made the strike a pillar, like if he had an event after washing a limb. Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi is a critical refinement of the matn of Maraqi al-Falah on tayammum. It opens with a ruling that if one person orders another to perform tayammum and does so for him, it is valid. Then it discusses a key dispute: whether the two wipes (darb) are a pillar (rukn) of tayammum. The matn states that performing both wipes in one place is valid, and the hashiya explains that the correct view does not consider the strike as a pillar; rather, the essence is wiping with the earth on the skin. Ibn al-Humam' argument is cited: the Qur'anic command is only 'wiping' (famsahu), and the phrase 'tayammum is two wipes' is a description of what usually happens, not a requirement. Then the passage enumerates the seventh and eighth conditions (cessation of invalidators and removal of barriers), the cause (intending an act that requires purification), and the eight conditions of obligation (referring to wudu). The pillars are stated as wiping the face and hands. Next, the seven sunan of tayammum are listed, including tasmiya, tartib, and muwalat, with a detailed description of the method from Abu Hanifa. Finally, there are additional rulings about using dust from animals or garments, and conditions for using dust from impure cloth. Throughout, the hashiya clarifies and refines the matn, emphasizing the Hanafi position while noting differences among later scholars.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Dry ablution as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
الضرب (al-darb): The act of striking the earth with the hands to pick up dust for wiping.
الركن (al-rukn): An integral part of an act of worship that invalidates it if omitted.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the pillars of tayammum are only wiping the face and the hands; striking the earth is a recommended act, not a requirement for validity.

The Seven Sunan of Tayammum
Lists and explains the seven recommended acts of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven sunan of tayammum and explain the practical details of each, including the rationale behind hand movements and finger separation.

Core Idea
Tayammum has seven recommended acts that perfect its performance and follow the Prophet's practice.

This passage from the matn lists the seven sunan (recommended acts) of tayammum, followed by a hashya that provides practical details from Imam Abu Hanifa's demonstration. Understanding these sunan helps you perform tayammum in the most complete manner, avoiding common mistakes like soiling the face with wet clay. Let's walk through each sunnah and its implementation.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the List
Commit the seven sunan to memory: tasmiyah, tartib, muwalat, iqbal wa idbar wa nafd, method of wiping arms (two strokes), tafrij al-asabi', and andab ta'khir al-tayammum.
2
Understand the Rationale
For each sunnah, note the reason: tasmiyah follows wudu; tartib and muwalat imitate the Prophet's action; hand movements prevent dust on the face; finger separation ensures thorough purification; delaying tayammum gives more chance to find water.
The hashya emphasises avoiding wet clay unless time is short.
3
Visualise the Method
Picture the two-stroke process: first stroke, wipe face; second stroke, wipe arms up to elbows including inner sides. Between strokes, shake and bring hands forward and back.
Imam Abu Hanifa demonstrated this to Abu Yusuf.
4
Apply in Practice
When performing tayammum, intentionally include each sunnah. For example, say 'Bismillah', separate fingers when striking, and shake hands before wiping.
If time is limited, performing the obligatory elements (two strokes) is sufficient; sunan are recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسنن التيمم سبعة التسمية في أوله كأصله (والترتيب) كما فعله النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (والموالاة) لحكاية فعله وإقبال اليدين بعد وضعهما في التراب وإدبارهما ونفضهما) اتقاء عن تلويث الوجه، والمثلة ولذا لا يتيمم بطين رطب حتى يجففه إلا إذا خاف خروج الوقت وبين الإمام الأعظم لما سأله أبو يوسف عن كيفيته بأن مال على الصعيد فأقبل بيديه، وأدبر ثم رفعهما ونفضهما ثم مسح وجهه ، ثم أعاد كفيه جميعا، فأقبل بهما وأدبر ثم رفعهما، ونفضهما ثم مسح بكل كف ذراع الأخرى وباطنها إلى المرفقين (وتفريج الأصابع حالة الضرب مبالغة في التطهير وندب تأخير التيمم
And the sunan of tayammum are seven: saying the basmalah at its beginning as in its origin, and order as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did, and continuity due to the narration of his action, and bringing the hands forward after placing them in the dust and moving them back and shaking them off, precaution against soiling the face and disfigurement, and therefore one should not perform tayammum with wet clay until it dries unless he fears the time will expire, and the Greatest Imam explained when Abu Yusuf asked him about its method: he leaned on the dust and brought his hands forward and back, then raised them and shook them, then wiped his face, then repeated his two palms together, bringing them forward and back, then raised them and shook them, then with each palm wiped the other forearm and its inner side up to the elbows, and separating the fingers during the strike as an exaggeration in purification, and recommending delaying tayammum.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage enumerates the seven sunan (recommended acts) of tayammum according to the Hanafi school. The first is pronouncing the basmalah at the start. The second is performing the actions in order (tartib) as the Prophet did. The third is continuity (muwalat) without significant pause. The fourth is bringing the hands forward after placing them in the earth, then moving them back, then shaking them off. This prevents dust from soiling the face. The fifth is the method of wiping the arms as demonstrated by Imam Abu Hanifa when Abu Yusuf asked: one leans on the pure earth, brings the hands forward and back, shakes them, wipes the face, then repeats for the arms up to the elbows, each palm wiping the opposite forearm including the inner side. The sixth is separating the fingers during the strike to ensure dust enters between them. The seventh is the recommendation to delay tayammum until near the end of the prayer time if one hopes to find water. This is a memorization anchor from the matn, with the hashya providing practical details.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Pronouncing 'Bismillah' at the start of tayammum.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Performing the actions of tayammum in a specific order: first strike, wipe face, second strike, wipe arms.
الموالاة (al-muwalat): Performing the actions consecutively without a significant gap.
إقبال اليدين وإدبارهما ونفضهما (iqbal al-yadayn wa idbaruhuma wa nafduhuma): Bringing the hands forward (away from body), then back (toward body), then shaking off excess dust.
تفريج الأصابع (tafrij al-asabi'): Separating the fingers when striking the earth to allow dust to reach between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Seven
C) Six
D) Eight

Key Takeaway
Tayammum has seven sunan that perfect its performance; while not obligatory, following them ensures completeness and adherence to the Prophet's practice.

Delaying Tayammum: Recommendation, Obligation, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delaying tayammum with legal reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between recommended and obligatory delays of tayammum, apply the rules for promised water and clothing/rope, and explain the basis of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The ruling on delaying tayammum depends on the type of promise and fear of time expiry—water promise binds, clothing/rope dispute hinges on how ability is established.

This lesson examines the conditions under which one should delay tayammum in hope of finding water. While delaying is generally recommended, it becomes obligatory when water is promised within a mile. A key intra-Hanafi difference arises regarding promises of clothing or a rope for drawing water. We will explore the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial ruling on delaying tayammum
Understand the baseline ruling: delaying tayammum for one who hopes to find water before the end of the recommended time is recommended (mandub) or binding (ḥatm) according to Abu Hanifa. The rationale is to perform with the more complete of the two purifications in the more complete time.
The story of Imam Abu Hanifa delaying Maghrib prayer illustrates this.
2
Understand the obligation to delay when promised water
If water is promised and is within a mile (approximately 300 steps), delaying tayammum becomes obligatory by agreement of all Hanafi imams. This is because the promise establishes apparent ability, and water is a necessity for wudu.
If water is beyond a mile or not promised, no delay is required.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on promised clothing/rope
Abu Hanifa holds that delay is obligatory only if one does not fear the prayer time will expire; if time is short, tayammum at the beginning is allowed. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say delay is obligatory even if time is feared to expire, by analogy to the promise of water. The basis of the dispute is whether ability for non-water items is established by mere offer (bazl) or requires ownership.
Abu Hanifa argues that accepting such charity causes humiliation (dhull), which the Law does not compel.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
According to the majority of reliable Hanafi works (e.g., al-Khaniyyah, al-Fath, Munyat al-Musalli), the relied-upon position is that delay is recommended (mandub) for promised clothing/rope, not obligatory. The text in al-Hashiya supports this, stating that the general principle is that delay is mandub.
Thus, in practice, one may pray at the beginning of the time with tayammum and not wait for such promises.

And from Abu Hanifa that it is binding for one who hopes to find water before the expiry of the recommended time, since there is no benefit in delay except performing with the more complete of the two purifications, as the Greatest Imam did in Maghrib prayer, opposing his teacher Hammad, and he (Hammad) approved him in it, and it was the first incident in which he opposed him, and their going out was to see off al-A'mash, may Allah have mercy on them. And it is obligatory to delay when promised water even if he fears missing the prayer, by agreement, if water is present or near, since there is no doubt about the permissibility of tayammum, and preventing delay due to time expiry while it is a mile away. I say: that is what the following principle requires. His saying: 'and they said delay is obligatory' – the basis of the dispute is whether ability regarding other than water is established through giving and permission. The Imam said: no, it is only established through ownership, or ownership of its substitute if it is sold. They said: it is established through them just as it is established through them by analogy to water. And they agreed that if one is told, 'I will pay for your Hajj,' he is not obliged to perform Hajj because ownership is considered, and here it is ability. Similarly, if the price of water is offered to him, he is not obliged to accept it because the wealth is not given as a gift, i.e., customarily, so he suffers humiliation by accepting it. Thus in Hashiyat al-Shalabi from Shaykh Yahya. His saying: 'and it is obligatory to seek water' – i.e., it is fard, explicitly stated by Qadikhan. And if he finds someone, he must ask; if he prays and did not ask and then is informed of water after that, he repeats; otherwise, no repetition, according to al-Zayla'i. And the meaning is one of the people, so it is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from the hashya discusses the ruling on delaying tayammum. It begins with the recommendation (nadb) to delay for one who hopes to find water before the end of the recommended prayer time. Imam Abu Hanifa considered it binding (hatm) for such a person. The reasoning is that the only benefit in delaying is performing with the more complete of the two purifications (tayammum vs wudu). This is illustrated by the story of Imam Abu Hanifa delaying Maghrib prayer to find water, opposing his teacher Hammad, who later approved. Then the hashya addresses the obligation to delay when one is promised water (by agreement of all Hanafi imams) provided the water is within a mile. If further, no delay is needed. A key intra-Hanafi dispute arises concerning promises of clothing (for a naked person) or a rope (for drawing water). Abu Hanifa says delay is obligatory only if the prayer time is not feared to expire; if one fears expiry, tayammum is done due to inability and kindness to the promiser. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say delay is obligatory even if expiry is feared, analogous to the promise of water. The basis of the dispute is whether ability for non-water items is established by a mere promise (bazl) or requires ownership. Finally, the passage states the obligation (fard) to seek water within a ghulwah (about 300 steps). If one prays without asking about water and later learns water was available, the prayer must be repeated. However, the last part is incomplete, indicating that one is not obliged to seek water from all people.

Key Terms
الحتم (al-hatm): A binding recommendation (stronger than nadb but not quite wajib).
الوعد بالماء (al-wa'd bi al-ma'): A promise by someone to provide water for wudu/tayammum.
الغلوة (al-ghulwah): A unit of distance, approximately 300 steps (about 150-200 meters).
القدرة (al-qudrah): Legal ability to perform an act, here ability to obtain water or its substitute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the distance one must seek water before performing tayammum?
A) One mile
B) Three hundred steps (ghulwah)
C) Two miles
D) Five hundred steps

Key Takeaway
The ruling on delaying tayammum depends on the type of promise and the proximity of water; a general hope makes it recommended, a promise of water within a mile makes it obligatory, and promises of other items generate a fiqh dispute.

The Recommended Delay of Tayammum Until Before Mustahabb Time Expires
Commentary on ruling of delaying tayammum before mustahabb time expiry

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why delaying tayammum until before the expiry of the preferred time is mustahabb and define the Hanafi concept of mustahabb time.

Core Idea
Delaying tayammum is recommended, not obligatory, to allow the chance to pray with water — the more complete purification.

This passage clarifies that performing tayammum early is valid, but delaying it until just before the expiry of the mustahabb time is mustahabb (recommended). The recommendation is based on the potential benefit of obtaining water and performing prayer with the complete purification. The commentator illustrates this with the incident where Imam Abu Hanifa differed from his teacher Hammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing tayammum before prayer. The ruling from the text is that delaying it until before the expiry of the mustahabb time is mustahabb, not wajib.
Mustahabb means recommended; failure to do so does not invalidate the prayer.
2
Understand the rationale
The only benefit of delaying is the possibility of performing prayer with water (the more complete purification). The text says, 'since there is no benefit in delaying except performing [prayer] with the more complete of the two purifications.'
If water is available, it must be used; tayammum is only a substitute.
3
Define the mustahabb time
According to the preferred view (as in al-Jawhara), the mustahabb time is the first half of the last portion of the prayer time. Some say it extends to the end of permissible time, but the first view is correct.
For Asr and Maghrib, special restrictions apply: do not delay Asr until sun changes, nor Maghrib from its earliest time.
4
Apply to specific prayers
For Asr, do not delay until the sun changes (i.e., after zenith). For Maghrib, do not delay from its earliest time, though a slight delay is allowed. For other prayers, delay is recommended within the mustahabb time.
The text implies that for Fajr, similar reasoning applies.
5
Reflect on the historical incident
Imam Abu Hanifa delayed tayammum for Maghrib, contrary to his teacher Hammad who prayed early. He later found water and prayed at the end of time, validating the recommendation.
This incident is the first recorded difference between Abu Hanifa and his teacher.

Source Text

Water: by overwhelming assumption (before the expiry of the preferred time, since there is no benefit in delaying except performing [prayer] with the more complete of the two purifications, as did the Great Imam in the Maghrib prayer, contrary to his teacher Hammad, and he deemed him correct in that. And it was the first incident in which he opposed him, and their leaving was to bid farewell to al-A'mash, may Allah have mercy on them. He said: (before the expiry of the preferred time) and it is the first half of the last portion of the time in a prayer whose delay is recommendable, as in al-Nahr, such that the performance falls within the preferred time, and it is said: until the end of the permissible time, and the first is the correct one as in al-Jawhara, and according to the first, one should not delay Asr until the sun changes, nor delay Maghrib from its earliest time, and it is said: there is no problem until shortly before the disappearance of the twilight, and al-Qahistani made it the saying of the majority. Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This is a commentary on the ruling regarding the time for tayammum. The matn states that it is permissible to perform tayammum based on overwhelming assumption of water absence before the expiry of the preferred time. The hashiya explains that delaying tayammum until the end of the mustahabb time is mustahabb, not wajib, because the only benefit is the possibility of performing prayer with water (the more complete purification). The commentator gives the example of Imam Abu Hanifa who delayed tayammum for Maghrib prayer contrary to his teacher Hammad, and later found water, proving the wisdom of delay. He also defines the 'mustahabb time' and notes differences of opinion.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Ritual purification with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is absent or harmful.
الطهارتان (al-taharatayn): The two purifications: the complete purification with water and the lesser purification with tayammum.
الوقت المستحب (al-waqt al-mustahabb): The desirable time for prayer: the first half of the latter portion of the prayer time (or until the end of permissible time, according to difference).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib.
B) It is mustahabb.
C) It is haram.
D) It is mubah.

Key Takeaway
Delaying tayammum until before the expiry of the preferred time is mustahabb, as it allows the chance to use water for the more complete purification.

Obligation to Delay Tayammum Due to Promise of Water or Clothing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on delaying tayammum when promised water or clothing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying tayammum when promised water or clothing, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the basis of ability.

Core Idea
Delay for water is obligatory by consensus; delay for clothing is mustahabb per the mufta bihi view of Abu Hanifa.

In this passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi, we explore a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when someone is promised water or clothing, does the obligation to delay tayammum apply? The text clarifies the agreed ruling for water and the differing positions of Abu Hanifa and his two students on clothing. This lesson will help you understand how the concept of 'ability' (qudra) is defined differently by each imam and how the later tarjih settled the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed ruling on water promise
Understand that by consensus, if water is promised and available within a mile, one must delay tayammum even if it means missing the prayer time.
This is the foundational case for the analogy.
2
Pinpoint the disputed issue: clothing promise
The dispute centers on whether ability is established by a mere offer (ibahah) or only by ownership (milk). Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn differ on this.
The same dispute applies to other items like a rope or bucket.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and its proof
Abu Hanifa holds that delay is not obligatory if one fears missing the prayer time, because ability is only by ownership. Accepting a clothing offer involves humiliation (mannah), which the Lawgiver does not require.
He argues the qiyas on water fails because water is freely given, clothing is not.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and its proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that delay is wajib even if one fears missing the time, by analogy with water: the promise outwardly establishes ability to obtain the item.
They consider the humiliation factor not preventing the obligation.
5
Identify the mufta bihi (operative view)
The majority of reliable works, as cited by the commentator, follow Abu Hanifa: delay for clothing is mustahabb, not wajib. This is the position relied upon for fatwa.
The commentator explicitly favors this view, calling it 'what the principle necessitates'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب التأخير بالوعد بالماء ولو خاف القضاء) اتفاقاً إذا كان الماء موجوداً أو قريباً إذ لا شك في جواز التيمم ومنع التأخير لخروج الوقت مع بعده ميلاً (ويجب التأخير) عند أبي حنيفة (بالوعد بالثوب) على العاري (أو السقاء) كحبل أو دلو (ما) لم يخف القضاء) فإن خافه تيمم لعجزه وللمنة بهما وقالا يجب التأخير ولو خاف القضاء كالوعد بالماء لظهور القدرة بوفاء الوعد ظاهراً قوله : (أي يلزم) فالوجوب بمعنى الافتراض كما في الذي بعده قوله : (إذا كان الماء موجوداً) أي عند الواعد، أو قريباً منه، دون ميل، أما إذا لم يوجد عنده، أو كان بعيداً منه ميلاً فأكثر، التأخير لأن الشارع أباح له التيمم حلبي، وهذه العبارة لم نرها لغيره. قوله: (ويجب التأخير عند أبي حنيفة تبع فيه صاحب البرهان، والذي في عامة المعتبرات كالخانية والفتح ومنية المصلى وشرحيهما والسراج، والبحر، وعزاه في الخلاصة إلى الأصل أن التأخير مندوب وعلى ذلك إن لم ينتظر، فصلى كذلك أول الوقت جاز قلت : وهو الذي يقتضيه التأصيل الآتي قوله : (وقالا يجب التأخير الخ مبنى الخلاف أن القدرة على ما سوى الماء هل تثبت بالبذل والإباحة. قال الإمام : لا وإنما تثبت بالملك، أو بملك بدله، إذا كان يباع، وقالا تثبت بها كما تثبت بهما قياساً على الماء وأجمعوا أنه لو قيل له أبحث لك مالي لتحج به، لا يجب عليه الحج لأن المعتبر فيه الملك وهنا القدرة وكذا لو عرض عليه ثمن الماء لا يجب عليه قبوله لأن المال ليس بمبذول أي عادة فيلحقه الذل بقبوله كذا في حاشية الشلبي عن الشيخ يحيى.
And it is obligatory to delay (if promised water) even if one fears missing the prayer time, by agreement, if the water is present or near, since there is no doubt about the permissibility of tayammum and prevention of delay due to expiry of time while it is more than a mile away. (And it is obligatory to delay) according to Abu Hanifa (if promised clothing) for the naked (or the rope) like a rope or a bucket (as long as) he does not fear missing the prayer time; if he fears it, he performs tayammum due to his inability and the humiliation that comes with them. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: it is obligatory to delay even if he fears missing the prayer time, like the promise of water, because ability appears through the fulfillment of the promise outwardly. He said: (that is, it is necessary) so wujub in the sense of fard, as in the following. He said: (if water is present) that is, with the person making the promise, or close, less than a mile; but if it is not with him, or is far away by a mile or more, then there is no delay because the Lawgiver has permitted tayammum (al-Halabi). And this expression we have not seen from others. He said: (it is obligatory to delay according to Abu Hanifa) he followed the author of al-Burhan in that, and what is in the majority of reliable works such as al-Khaniyya, al-Fath, Munyat al-Musalli and its commentaries, al-Siraj, al-Bahr, and attributed in al-Khulasa to the original that the delay is mustahabb, and on that if he did not wait and prayed at the beginning of the time, it is permissible. I say: and that is what the following principle necessitates. He said: (and they both said it is obligatory to delay etc.) the basis of the disagreement is: can ability over other than water be established by offer and permission? The Imam said: no, it is only established by ownership, or by ownership of its substitute if it can be sold. And they both said: it can be established by them (offer and permission) as it can be established by ownership, by analogy with water. And they all agreed that if one is told 'I will provide you with money to perform Hajj', he is not obliged to perform Hajj because the basis there is ownership, and here it is ability. Similarly, if the price of water is offered to him, he is not obliged to accept it, because wealth is not usually offered, so he would suffer humiliation by accepting it, as in Hashiyat al-Shalabi from Sheikh Yahya.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage deals with the obligation to delay tayammum when one is promised water or clothing. By agreement, if one is promised water and the water is present or near (within a mile), one must delay tayammum even if it means missing the prayer time. For clothing or other items (like a rope to draw water), Abu Hanifa holds that one must delay only if not fearing to miss the prayer; if he fears missing the time, he may perform tayammum because he is unable to obtain them without humiliation. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that one must delay even if fearing to miss the time, by analogy with the promise of water. The commentator explains the underlying principle: ability is established by ownership according to Abu Hanifa, but by offer and permission according to the Sahibayn. The hadiye clarifies that the relied-upon position is that delay is mustahabb, not obligatory, for clothing.

Key Terms
الوعد (al-wa'd): A promise made by someone to provide water or clothing.
المنة (al-mannah): The feeling of obligation or humiliation that comes from accepting a favor from someone.
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Permission or offer to use something without ownership.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, if a naked person is promised clothing during the prayer time, what is the ruling on delaying tayammum?
A) He must delay and wait for the clothing.
B) He may perform tayammum immediately.
C) He must delay only if the clothing is given within a mile.
D) He must combine tayammum and wait.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, one must delay tayammum for promised water by consensus, but for clothing the mufta bihi view is that delay is mustahabb, not obligatory.
