Obligation to Seek Water for Tayammum
Rulings and intra-Hanafi disputes on the obligation to seek water before tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make seeking water wajib before tayammum and explain how the apparent dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is reconciled in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Seeking water is wajib when there is a strong presumption of its presence and safety; in inhabited areas, it is always wajib.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi delves into the obligation to search for water before turning to tayammum. It not only defines when the obligation applies but also resolves an apparent internal Hanafi conflict, showing that the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two disciples are grounded in different presumptions about water availability. Understanding this refinement is key to applying the ruling correctly in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and basic obligation
State that seeking water (talab) is wajib (fard) before tayammum. Note that if one finds a person, he must ask; failure to ask and subsequent discovery of water invalidates the prayer.
The obligation is established in the matn and supported by Qadikhan.
2
Examine the conditions for the obligation
The obligation depends on a strong presumption (zann) of water's presence (e.g., seeing a bird, greenery, or receiving news) and safety from harm. The distance is a bowshot (300-400 steps). If water is presumed in multiple directions, seek from each direction.
The hadd al-qurb (proximity) is less than a mile; doubt does not trigger obligation.
3
Distinguish wilderness from inhabited areas
In the desert (mafazah), the obligation is conditional. In inhabited areas ('umran), seeking is always wajib because water is generally available; even without strong presumption, the prayer is invalid if water later appears.
The general (ghalib) is treated as certain in rulings.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Hidaya and some works narrate from Abu Hanifa that seeking is not obligatory because inability is certain and ability is presumed. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) oblige seeking because water is usually offered. Shams al-A'imma and al-Jassas reconcile: Abu Hanifa meant when one presumes refusal; otherwise he agrees.
The reconciliation hinges on the presumption of refusal or availability.
5
Apply the reconciled view
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that seeking is wajib when there is a strong presumption of presence and safety. This includes seeking tools (bucket, rope) if needed. The dispute is resolved in practice by the contextual reading.
The commentator concludes there is no real disagreement once the context is understood.

And it is obligatory to seek water (i.e., it is fard, as explicitly stated by Qadikhan). And if he finds someone, he must ask; so if he prayed without asking and later was informed of water, he must repeat, otherwise not (al-Zayla'i). And it refers to one of the people of that place, or someone who knows it. He said: (or his messenger) and it suffices if someone tells him without sending (as in Munyat al-Musalli). He said: (and it is three hundred steps etc.) as in al-Dhakhira and al-Mughrib, and what is in al-Tabyin is that it is the distance of an arrow shot, and that is consistent with al-Qamus. The definition of proximity is that he presumes the distance between him and water is less than a mile, mentioned by al-Sayyid. And if a just person informs him of the absence of water, even if he had a strong presumption of its existence, it is permissible for him to perform tayammum without disagreement, as in al-Halabi. The place of this issue is in the wilderness; but if he is near inhabited areas, he must seek absolutely by agreement, even if he performs tayammum and prays, then water appears, his prayer is invalid because inhabited areas are generally not empty of water, and the general is attached to the certain in rulings even if he is not strongly presuming (as in al-Bada'i and al-Halabi). He said: (his seeking) meaning by asking, and his saying: 'from those with him' means absolutely, and the restriction to his companion in some books follows custom (Hamawi from al-Jundi). And know that the transmission in this issue differs: from al-Hidaya and many books that seeking is not required at all in the saying of the Imam because inability is certain and ability is presumed, since water is among the most precious things in travel, so the apparent is non-offering. And they both (Sahibayn) said: he must seek, and it is not permissible for him to perform tayammum before that because water is usually offered. And Shams al-A'imma transmitted in his Mabsut that the requirement to seek is the saying of all apparently. al-Jassas said: there is no disagreement among them; the meaning of Abu Hanifa is no obligation when he strongly presumes refusal, and their meaning is when he presumes no refusal due to proven ability to water by permission unanimously. He said in al-Burhan: hence al-Kafi did not mention any disagreement. And if seeking water is obligatory apparently, then seeking a bucket and rope is obligatory, as in al-Nahr from al-Mi'raj. He said: (so there is no humiliation) in seeking it, and al-Hasan said: no.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation to seek water before resorting to tayammum. The matn establishes that seeking water is fard (obligatory) under certain conditions. The hashiya clarifies that one must ask those present, and if one fails to ask and later finds water, the prayer must be repeated. The distance to search is a bowshot (300-400 steps), but only if one has a strong presumption of water's presence based on signs (bird, greenery, news) and safety. If in inhabited areas, seeking is always obligatory. The commentator reconciles a reported difference: Abu Hanifa is said to not oblige seeking in some narrations, but the majority view—and the reconciled position—is that the obligation depends on presumption: if one presumes water will be refused, no seeking; if one presumes availability, seeking is wajib. The final ruling is that seeking water is obligatory on the apparent view, and includes seeking tools like a bucket and rope.

Key Terms
الطلب (al-talab): The act of seeking or asking for water.
الغلوة (al-ghalwah): A bowshot, approximately 300-400 steps (used as a measure for how far one must search).
الظن (al-zann): Overwhelming presumption or belief; in legal terms, strong probability that something is true.
المفازة (al-mafazah): A desert or unpopulated area (wilderness).
العمران (al-'umran): Inhabited areas (towns, villages)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a traveller is in a desert and sees a bird flying from a direction, indicating water, what is the ruling on seeking water?
A) Seeking is not obligatory because he is in a desert.
B) He must seek water in that direction up to a bowshot distance if safe.
C) He may perform tayammum without seeking.
D) He must seek in all four directions equally.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, seeking water before tayammum is wajib when there is a strong presumption of its presence and safety; in inhabited areas, it is always wajib. The apparent dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn is reconciled by the context of presumed refusal.

Seeking Water for Tayammum: Obligation, Distance, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains obligation to seek water, distance, and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which seeking water before tayammum becomes wajib, identify the required distance (400 steps), and explain the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
Seeking water is wajib when you strongly think it is near and safe; otherwise not.

Before a traveler can resort to tayammum, the Hanafi school requires that he first make a reasonable effort to find water. This lesson unpacks what that effort entails: when it is obligatory, how far to search, and what signs justify a presumption of water. You will also explore a subtle difference of opinion within the Hanafi school itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'seeking water' (talab al-ma). The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) under certain conditions. Note: it is not a condition for the validity of tayammum, but a prerequisite before performing it.
Wajib here means the act is required; omitting it without reason makes the subsequent tayammum invalid.
2
Understand the role of strong presumption (zann)
Zann (strong presumption) is the key factor. If you have a strong thought that water is near (based on birds, greenery, news, etc.) and it is safe, you must seek. If you do not have such zann, or you fear an enemy, seeking is not required.
This is based on the Hanafi principle that zann suffices for action in practical matters (furūʿ).
3
Learn the distance to seek
Seeking must be done up to a distance of four hundred steps (or about one bowshot = ghalwa) in the direction you think water is located. This distance is considered reasonable for a traveler.
Various estimations: 400 steps, 300 cubits, or one bowshot. The most correct is the extent that does not harm oneself or companions.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Imam Abu Hanifa held that seeking is not obligatory even with zann because water is scarce in travel, so ability is doubtful. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held it is obligatory because water is customarily given. The text reconciles: Abu Hanifa meant when one strongly thinks he will be refused; the companions meant when he thinks he will be given.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the school; both views are based on valid usul.
5
Recognize the relied-upon position (mufta bihi)
The preferred opinion for fatwa is that seeking is obligatory, as stated by Shams al-A'imma in al-Mabsut and supported by al-Jassas. This is followed by the majority of later Hanafi scholars.
If a person is near habitation, seeking is absolutely obligatory by agreement.

But the two companions said: seeking is necessary, and tayammum is not permissible before it because water is customarily given. Shams al-A'imma in his Mabsut reported that the necessity of seeking is the saying of all apparently. Al-Jassas said there is no disagreement among them; so the meaning of Abu Hanifa is non-obligation when he strongly thinks refusal, and their meaning is when he thinks non-refusal due to the establishment of ability to water by permission by agreement. He said in al-Burhan: for this reason, no disagreement was reported in al-Kafi. When seeking water is necessary apparently, then seeking the bucket and rope is necessary.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage discusses the obligation to seek water before performing tayammum. The author explains that if a traveler thinks water is near (based on signs like birds, greenery, or news) and it is safe, he must seek it up to four hundred steps in that direction. If he does not think it is near or fears an enemy, he does not have to seek. The passage also details the distances: an arrow shot (ghalwa), three hundred cubits, or four hundred steps. There is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: Imam Abu Hanifa held that seeking is not obligatory because water is scarce in travel, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) held it is obligatory because water is customarily given. The relied-upon view is that of the two companions when one has a strong expectation of finding water. The passage also clarifies that if one is near habitated areas, seeking is absolutely obligatory.

Key Terms
ظن (zann): Strong presumption or belief, sufficient to act upon in practical matters (furūʿ).
غلوة (ghalwa): A bowshot distance approximately 300–400 cubits or steps.
طلب (talab): The act of seeking water before tayammum; includes asking people or looking physically.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum distance a traveler must seek water in the direction he thinks it is located?
A) One mile
B) Four hundred steps
C) Two bowshots
D) Five hundred cubits

Key Takeaway
Seeking water before tayammum is wajib only when you have a strong presumption of finding it and it is safe; the preferred Hanafi position follows the two companions that seeking is obligatory.

Conditions for Obligation to Buy Water for Tayammum
States when a person must buy water for tayammum and conditions for obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions that obligate a traveler to purchase water for tayammum and apply them to determine when purchase is not required.

Core Idea
You must buy water only at a fair price, with surplus money, not needed for essentials.

When water is for sale, is a traveler obliged to buy it? The answer depends on three conditions that balance legal duty and financial hardship. This passage from the Hanafi works outlines exactly when purchase becomes wajib and when it drops.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purchasing water for tayammum. The ruling is wajib under certain conditions.
The ruling applies when water is available for sale.
2
List the three conditions
The text states three conditions: (a) price is fair (no ghabn fahish), (b) buyer has the money with him, (c) money is surplus to his immediate needs (expenses and transport cost).
These are shurut for wujub.
3
Define ghabn fahish
Understand the two definitions: (1) what does not fall under valuation of experts, (2) half the value. The preferred definition is the first as more lenient.
The definition affects the threshold of fairness.
4
Apply negation
If any condition fails, purchase is not obligatory. E.g., excessive price, no money, or money needed for essentials.
The text explicitly lists cases where purchase is not required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مثله لزمه شراؤه به وبزيادة يسيرة لا بغبن فاحش وهو ما لا يدخل تحت تقويم المقومين وقيل شطر القيمة ( إن كان الثمن (معه) وكان فاضلاً عن نفقته وأجرة حمله فهذه شروط ثلاثة للزوم الشراء، فلا يلزم الشراء لو طلب الغبن الفاحش أو طلب ثمن المثل، وليس معه فلا يستدين الماء، أو احتاجه لنفقته
Similarly, he is obliged to buy it with it and with a slight increase, not with excessive fraud, which is what does not fall under the valuation of appraisers. And it was said half the value. (If he has the price with him) and it is surplus to his expenses and the hire of carrying it; these are three conditions for the obligation of purchase. So purchase is not obligatory if he demands excessive fraud, or demands the fair price and does not have it, so he does not borrow for water, or he needs it for his expenses.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage explains when a traveler must purchase water for wudu or tayammum. The general rule is that if water is available for sale, one must buy it if he has the means. Three conditions must be met: (1) the seller asks only a fair price or a slight increase, not excessive fraud (ghabn fahish); (2) the traveler has the price with him; (3) the money is surplus to his immediate needs (expenses and transport costs). If any condition is missing—e.g., the seller asks an exorbitant price, or the buyer does not have the money, or he needs it for essentials—then purchase is not obligatory. He is not required to borrow money to buy water. The definition of ghabn fahish is that which is not within the valuation of experts; some say it is half the value. The text emphasizes that the school's position is based on protecting wealth from waste.

Key Terms
غبن فاحش (ghabn fahish): Excessive fraud in price that is not within normal valuation of experts; some define as half the value.
ثمن المثل (thaman al-mithl): The fair market price for the item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The seller demands a fair price or slight increase
B) The buyer has the price with him
C) The buyer is in a desert
D) The price is surplus to his necessary expenses

Key Takeaway
Purchase of water for tayammum is obligatory only when three conditions are jointly met: fair price, available funds, and surplus to essential needs.

Multiple Prayers with One Tayammum
Ruling that one tayammum suffices for multiple prayers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that one tayammum suffices for unlimited prayers and explain the evidence, the intra-Hanafi precaution, and the practical difference from the Shafi'i school.

Core Idea
One tayammum suffices for unlimited prayers until water is found.

What happens if you perform tayammum for Fajr and then want to pray Dhuhr? Does your tayammum expire after that first prayer? In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling that one valid tayammum can be used for any number of prayers — both obligatory and supererogatory — as long as water remains unavailable. The ruling is supported by a clear hadith and contrasted with the Shafi'i position, leading to a recommended precaution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing multiple prayers using a single tayammum. Determine the hukm: is it permissible, recommended, or obligatory? The Hanafi school rules it permissible (mubah).
The text begins with ويجوز (and it is permissible).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two proofs: the Quranic command (implied) and the hadith: 'Soil is a purifier for the Muslim, even up to ten years, as long as he does not find water.' Identify this as a hadith ahad.
The hadith is narrated by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'even up to ten years' indicates that tayammum remains valid indefinitely as long as water is not found. There is no expiration by prayer count or time.
The dalala is zanni but clear in its implication.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that tayammum only permits one fard prayer. The Hanafi school thus recommends repeating tayammum for each fard as a precaution (khurūjan min al-khilāf).
This is an example of legitimate ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the literal meaning of the hadith and the principle that tayammum is a complete substitute for wudu (badal mutlaq). The fatwa is to follow the Hanafi view, but the precaution is also valid.
The text says 'الأولى إعادته لكل فرض' (it is better to repeat it).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجوز أن يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من الفرائض) كالوضوء للأمر به ولقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : التراب طهور المسلم ولو إلى عشر حجيج ما لم يجد الماء والأولى إعادته لكل فرض خروجاً من خلاف الشافعي (و) يصلي بالتيمم الواحد ما شاء من (النوافل) اتفاقاً (وصح تقديمه على الوقت لأنه شرط فيسبق المشروط، والإرادة سبب وقد حصلت ولو كان أكثر البدن جريحاً تيمم والكثرة تعتبر من حيث عدد الأعضاء
And it is permissible to pray with one tayammum as many obligatory prayers as he wishes, like wudu, because of the command and because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Soil is a purifier for the Muslim, even up to ten years, as long as he does not find water.' And it is better to repeat it for each obligatory prayer to exit from the disagreement of al-Shafi'i. And he may pray with one tayammum as many supererogatory prayers as he wishes by agreement. And it is valid to perform tayammum before the time because it is a condition, so the condition precedes the conditioned, and intention is a cause and it has occurred. And if most of the body is wounded, he performs tayammum, and the majority is considered in terms of the number of limbs.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage establishes that one valid tayammum can be used for multiple prayers, both fard (obligatory) and nafil (supererogatory). The proof is the Quranic command 'if you do not find water, then perform tayammum' (Q 4:43, 5:6) and the hadith 'Soil is a purifier for the Muslim, even up to ten years, as long as he does not find water' (narrated by Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, etc.). The Hanafi ruling is that tayammum is a complete substitute for wudu, so it lifts impurity (hadath) absolutely until water is found. This differs from Imam al-Shafi'i, who holds that tayammum only allows one fard prayer. Therefore, the Hanafi school recommends repeating tayammum for each fard to avoid the disagreement. It is also agreed that one tayammum suffices for multiple nafil prayers. Tayammum before the time (e.g., before the prayer enters) is valid because tayammum is a condition (shart) like wudu, and the condition can precede the conditioned. The intention (niyyah) must be present. Finally, if most of the body is wounded, one performs tayammum, and 'most' is determined by the number of limbs covered by wounds.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution with pure soil as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
بدلية (badaliyyah): The substitution relationship between water and soil; according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the substitution is between water and soil with equal purity; according to Muhammad al-Shaybani (in another view), it is between tayammum and wudu, with wudu being superior.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many obligatory (fard) prayers can one perform with a single tayammum according to the Hanafi school?
A) Only one
B) Two
C) As many as he wishes
D) Only three

Key Takeaway
One tayammum is valid for any number of prayers until water is found; repeating it for each fard is recommended to avoid Shafi'i disagreement.

Tayammum when Wounded: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Refinement
Ruling with proof (implicit), expanded by hashiya

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tayammum when body parts are wounded, identify the condition (majority wounded) that triggers tayammum, and explain why combining ghusl and tayammum is invalid.

Core Idea
Tayammum substitutes for water when majority of a limb is wounded; the substitute cannot combine with the original.

When water is harmful due to wounds, tayammum becomes obligatory. But how do we determine when a wound triggers tayammum vs. partial washing? The Hanafi school has nuanced positions based on the majority of the limb or body affected. This lesson unpacks the key ruling and the critical reasoning behind it, as refined by the hashiya tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with tayammum when wounds prevent washing. The ruling is that tayammum is wajib when water is harmful or unavailable.
This is a conditional ruling – tayammum is not the default.
2
Locate the condition (majority wounded)
The text states that if the majority of a limb or half the body is wounded, tayammum is performed. If the majority is healthy, wash the healthy parts and wipe the wounded.
The condition is quantitative: majority of the limb/body, not merely presence of a wound.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi authorities consider each limb separately (majority of each limb), while others consider the body as a whole. In ghusl, the majority is by area according to the mukhtar view.
This difference affects whether one performs tayammum or partial washing.
4
Apply the no-combination principle
The text clearly states that one cannot combine ghusl and tayammum for the same purification, because a substitute (badal) cannot be combined with the original (mubdal). This is a key usul principle.
Analogies from other areas of fiqh (e.g., amputation and compensation) illustrate this rule.
5
Understand the hashiya refinement
The hashiya (al-Tahtawi) clarifies ambiguous terms, resolves conflicting statements, and sometimes prefers a more precautionary view (washing healthy and wiping wounded).
This shows how later scholars carefully refine and choose the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في المختار فإذا كان بالرأس والوجه واليدين جراحة، ولو قلت وليس بالرجلين جراحة تيمم ومنهم من اعتبرها في نفس كل عضو فإن كان أكثر كل عضو منها جريحاً تيمم وإلا فلا (أو) كان (نصفه) أي البدن ( جريحاً (تيمم في الأصح ، ولو جنباً لأن أحداً لم يقل بغسل بين كل جدريتين ( وإن كان أكثره صحيحاً غسله أي الصحيح (ومسح الجريح) بمروره على الجسد وإن لم يستطع فعلى خرقة وإن ضره تركه وإذا كانت الجراحة قليلة ببطنه أو ظهره ويضره الماء صار كغالب الجراحة حكماً للضرورة (ولا) يصح أن (يجمع بين الغسل والتيمم) إذ لا نظير له في الشرع للجمع بين البدل والمبدل والجمع بين التيمم وسؤر الحمار لأداء الفرض بأحدهما لا بهما كما لا يجتمع قطع وضمان وحد ومهر ووصية وميراث إلى غير ذلك من المعدودات هنا . مهمة نظمها ابن الشحنة بقوله ويسقط مسح الرأس عمن برأسه من الداء ما إن بله يتضرر وبه أفتى قارى الهداية قلت وكذا يسقط غسله في الجنابة والحيض والنفاس للمساواة في العذر ( وينقضه) أي التيمم (ناقض الوضوء لأن ناقض الأصل ناقض لخلفه، إلا به قاله في الشرح قوله : ( ولو كان أكثر البدن الأولى للمصنف حذف البدن ويقول ولو كان الأكثر من الأعضاء أو النصف منها جريحاً تيمم ليكون كلامه متناولاً للطهارة الصغرى والكبرى قاله السيد قوله : ( والكثرة الخ) لا يخفى أن هذا الخلاف إنما هو في الوضوء وأما في الغسل فالظاهر اعتبار الكثرة من حيث المساحة كما في البحر قوله: (تيمم في الأصح) وقيل يغسل الصحيح ويمسح الجريح وصححه في المحيط والخانية. قال في البحر، ولا يخفى أنه أحوط فكان أولى. قال المؤلف في حاشية الدرر والحاصل أن التصحيح اختلف قوله: (لأن أحداً إلخ) قد يقال ان الغسل سقط هنا للحرج أو لأنه يضر ما حاذاه من الجدري قوله: (بمروره) أي الماء يعني ،بلته، والأولى أن يقول بإمراره قوله : (فعلى خرقة) في كلام الحلبي ما يفيد أنه يشدها عند إرادة المسح إن لم تكن مشدودة قوله : صار كغالب الجراحة) أي فيتيمم ولو قيل انه يمسح الأعلى ويغسل الأسفل، لكان حسناً قال في الشرح : ولم أر من تكلم عليه قوله : (ويسقط مسح الرأس الخ) وظاهره انه لا يؤمر بالمسح على الخرقة بخلاف الغسل كما تقدم، وسيأتي أنه أحد قولين قوله : (ما إن بله أي قدر وقوله من الداء بيان مقدم على مبينه والضمير في بله يرجع إلى ما المفسر بقدر والكلام فيه حذف أي أن بل محل هذا القدر من الداء يتضرر قوله : (وكذا يسقط غسله) أي وينتقل الحكم لمسحه فإن ضره مسح على الخرقة ضره تركه كما تقدم فتأمل قلت وسيأتي ما يفيده قوله: (ناقض الوضوء) لو قال ناقض الأصل ليعم الغسل والوضوء لكان أحسن وأجاب الحموي بأن المراد بالوضوء الطهارة أعم من أن تكون عن حدث أو جنابة بطريق استعمال الخاص في العام مجازاً ذكره السيد .
In al-Mukhtar: If there is a wound on the head, face, and hands, and it is said there is no wound on the feet, he performs tayammum. Some consider each limb individually: if the majority of each limb is wounded, then tayammum; otherwise no. Or if half of the body is wounded, he performs tayammum in the more correct view, even if in a state of janabah, because no one said to wash between each smallpox scab. If the majority of the body is healthy, he washes the healthy part and wipes the wounded part by passing water over the body. If unable, then (he wipes) over a cloth. If it harms him, he leaves it. If the wound is small on his stomach or back and water harms him, it becomes like the majority of the wound due to necessity. It is not valid to combine ghusl and tayammum, as there is no parallel in the law for combining a substitute and the substituted. Combining tayammum and the leftover water of a donkey (as a substitute) is for performing the obligation by one of them, not by both, just as one cannot combine amputation and compensation, or fixed punishment and dowry, or bequest and inheritance, and so on. An important point: Ibn al-Shihnah versified it saying: 'The wiping of the head is dropped for one on whose head there is a disease such that if wetted he is harmed; and the reciter of al-Hidayah gave fatwa accordingly.' I said: Likewise, washing is dropped in janabah, menstruation, and postnatal bleeding due to equality in excuse. It (tayammum) is nullified by the nullifier of wudu, because the nullifier of the original nullifies its substitute, except as stated in the Sharh. His saying: (If most of the body is healthy) – it would have been better for the author to omit 'the body' and say: 'if most of the limbs or half of them are wounded, he performs tayammum' so that his statement includes both minor and major purification, as said by al-Sayyid. His saying: (the majority etc.) – it is clear that this difference is regarding wudu; as for ghusl, the apparent view is consideration of majority by area, as in al-Bahr. His saying: (he performs tayammum in the more correct view) – it is said: he washes the healthy and wipes the wounded, and this was corrected in al-Muhit and al-Khaniyyah. He said in al-Bahr: it is more precautionary and thus more appropriate. The author said in Hashiyat al-Durar: the gist is that the correction differs. His saying: (because no one said) – it may be said that washing is dropped here due to hardship or because it harms the area opposite the smallpox. His saying: (by passing) i.e., the water meaning wetting it; it is better to say 'by passing it'. His saying: (upon a cloth) – in the speech of al-Halabi it indicates that he ties it when intending to wipe if it is not already tied. His saying: (becomes like the majority of the wound) i.e., he performs tayammum; and if it were said that he wipes the upper and washes the lower, it would be good. He said in al-Sharh: I have not seen anyone discuss it. His saying: (The wiping of the head is dropped etc.) – its apparent meaning is that he is not commanded to wipe over the cloth unlike washing as stated earlier; it will come that it is one of two opinions. His saying: (what if wetted) i.e., amount, and his saying (of disease) is an explanation preceding the explained; the pronoun in 'wetted' refers to 'what' interpreted as 'amount', and there is ellipsis meaning: if wetted, this amount of disease harms him. His saying: (and likewise washing is dropped) i.e., and the ruling transfers to wiping; if wiping harms him, he wipes over a cloth; if that harms him too, he leaves it as stated earlier. Ponder. I said: It will come what benefits it. His saying: (the nullifier of wudu) – if he had said 'the nullifier of the original' to include ghusl and wudu, it would be better. Al-Hamawi answered that what is meant by wudu is purification generally, whether from minor or major impurity, by way of using the specific for the general metaphorically, as mentioned by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (though the proof is implied) from the hashya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah concerning tayammum when wounds are present. The author begins by stating the ruling in al-Mukhtar: if wounds are on the head, face, and hands but not the feet, one performs tayammum. There is a difference of opinion: some consider each limb individually, so if the majority of each limb is wounded, tayammum is performed; otherwise no. Another view: if half the body is wounded, tayammum is performed in the more correct view, even in janabah, because no one requires washing between each smallpox scab. If the majority is healthy, one washes the healthy parts and wipes the wounded parts, either by passing water over the body or over a cloth if necessary; if water causes harm, wiping is omitted. If a small wound on the stomach or back is harmed by water, it is treated like a widespread wound due to necessity. Combining ghusl (full ablution) and tayammum is invalid, as it would combine a substitute with the original. The author then quotes a poetic summary by Ibn al-Shihnah regarding the dropping of head wiping when wetting would harm, and extends this to dropping ghusl in cases of janabah, etc. The hashya then comments on each phrase of the matn, clarifying the reasoning, discussing differences (e.g., in ghusl vs wudu, the majority is by area), and noting that the most precautionary view is to wash the healthy and wipe the wounded. It also distinguishes between types of nullifiers and the proper terminology. The overall legal weight is from the mukhtar (chosen) view and later fatawa, though some positions are from earlier authorities like al-Muhit.

Key Terms
تيمم (tayammum): Dry ablution using earth as a substitute for wudu/ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.
جراحة (jirahah): A wound that makes washing harmful or painful, affecting the obligation of wudu/ghusl.
بدل (badal): Substitute; tayammum is a substitute (badal) for water-based purification.
أكثر (akthar): Majority; the condition that triggers tayammum in case of wounds (majority of limb or half of body).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more correct view (al-ashah) in the Hanafi school, if half of a person's body is wounded, what must they do?
A) Wash the healthy half and wipe the wounded half
B) Perform tayammum, even if in a state of janabah
C) Combine ghusl and tayammum
D) Wait until the wounds heal

Key Takeaway
When the majority of a limb or half the body is wounded, tayammum becomes wajib and cannot be combined with water-based purification; the substitute suffices for the entire obligation.

What Nullifies Tayammum? The Removal of the Excuse and Ability to Use Water
Ruling on nullifiers of tayammum with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two main nullifiers of tayammum and explain why the true nullifier is the original hadath, citing the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Tayammum is nullified by removal of the excuse or ability to use water; the original hadath remains the true nullifier.

In this lesson, we examine the conditions that invalidate tayammum according to the Hanafi school. The matn from Nur al-Idah and its hashya clarify that tayammum is not permanent: it is tied to the ongoing excuse. The passage also explains the underlying principle that the true nullifier is the original impurity (hadath), which tayammum only temporarily suspends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the explicit nullifiers
Read the text: removal of excuse (enemy, illness, cold) and ability to use water are the stated nullifiers.
These are conditions that end the permissibility of tayammum.
2
Understand the condition of partial water use
If water runs out during wudu, tayammum is invalidated because the purity of earth ends.
This is based on the hadith's condition: 'as long as he does not find water'.
3
Recognize the change of excuse
If one excuse ends and another begins, the first tayammum is nullified and a new one is needed.
The causes are different, so a new tayammum is required.
4
Trace the proof from hadith
The hadith 'earth is a purifier as long as no water is found' shows tayammum ends when water is available.
The hadith is cited as the primary evidence (dalil).
5
Identify the true nullifier
The hashya teaches that the true nullifier is the original hadath, not the removal of excuse per se.
Tayammum only suspends the ruling of impurity; when the excuse ends, the original hadath is reactivated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينقضه زوال العذر المبيح له كذهاب العدو والمرض والبرد ووجود الآلة وقد شمل هذا قوله (و) ينقضه القدرة على استعمال الماء الكافي ولو مرة مرة فلو ثلث الغسل وفنى الماء قبل إكمال الوضوء بطل تيممه في المختار لانتهاء طهورية التراب بالحديث (ومقطوع اليدين والرجلين إذا كان بوجهه جراحة يصلي بغير طهارة ولا يعيد) وهو الأصح وقال بعضهم سقطت عنه الصلاة ويمسح الأشل وجهه وذراعيه بالأرض ولا يترك الصلاة ويمسح الا قطع ما بقي من الفروض كغسله ويسقطان بتجاوز القطع محل الفرض . قوله : ( وينقضه زوال العذر المبيح) فلو تيمم لعذر فزال فمرض مرضاً يبيحه انتقض الأول ويتيمم للثاني لتغاير الأسباب واعلم أن الناقض في الحقيقة الحدث السابق. قوله: (بالحديث) أي بدلالة الحديث، وهو قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : التراب طهور المسلم ولو إلى عشر حجج ما لم يجد الماء اه قوله : ( ومقطوع اليدين الخ) لم يتكلم على الرأس لأن أكثر الأعضاء جريح، والوظيفة حينئذ التيمم، ولكنه سقط لفقد آلته وهي اليدان قاله في حاشية الدر قوله: (ويمسح الأشل الخ) أما على رواية الاكتفاء بأكثر الأعضاء في التيمم فظاهر، وأما على الأخرى فللضرورة والاحتياط في العيادة، ولعل هذا عند عدم القدرة على استعمال الماء قوله: (ويمسح الأقطع الخ) اعتباراً للجزء بالكل، قاله في الشرح والمراد ان ذلك في التيمم، وقوله كغسله أي في التطهير بالماء.
It (tayammum) is nullified by the removal of the excuse that permitted it, such as the departure of an enemy, illness, cold, and the presence of a means (water). And included in this is his saying: (and) it is nullified by the ability to use sufficient water, even if only once, so that if one washes (with water) partially and the water runs out before completing wudu, his tayammum is invalidated in al-Mukhtar, because the purity of earth ends with the hadith. (And one whose hands and feet are cut off, and if there is a wound on his face, he prays without purification and does not repeat) and that is the most correct. Some said prayer is dropped for him, but he wipes his face and arms (the unstruck ones?) on the earth and does not abandon prayer, and he wipes except what remains of the obligatory parts like washing, and both (tayammum? washing?) are dropped if the cut exceeds the site of obligation. His saying: (it is nullified by the removal of the excuse that permits it) – if he performs tayammum for an excuse and then it ceases, then he becomes ill with an illness that permits tayammum, the first tayammum is nullified and he performs tayammum for the second due to the difference of causes. Know that the true nullifier is the previous hadath (impurity). His saying: (by the hadith) i.e., by the indication of the hadith, which is his saying (peace be upon him): 'The earth is a purifier for the Muslim even for ten years, as long as he does not find water.' His saying: (and one whose hands and feet are cut off) – he did not speak about the head because the majority of limbs are wounded, and in that case the duty is tayammum, but it is dropped due to the lack of its instrument, namely the hands, as said in Hashiyat al-Durr. His saying: (and he wipes the flabby/stump) – as for the narration of sufficing with the majority of limbs in tayammum, it is apparent; as for the other narration, it is due to necessity and precaution in worship, and perhaps this is when unable to use water. His saying: (and he wipes the amputated) – considering the part as the whole, said in al-Sharh. The meaning is that this is in tayammum, and his saying 'like his washing' means in purification with water.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage deals with what nullifies tayammum and a special case where a person is both lacking limbs and has a face wound. The matn states that tayammum is nullified by the removal of the excuse (like enemy, illness, cold) and by the ability to use water. The hashya explains that if the excuse changes (one illness ends and another begins), a new tayammum is required. The true nullifier is the original hadath (state of impurity) that tayammum temporarily removed. The hadith 'the earth is a purifier even for ten years if no water is found' is cited as proof. Then a unique case: if one has no hands and feet and has a face wound, he prays without any purification (neither wudu nor tayammum) and does not repeat. The hashya clarifies that the head is not discussed because the majority of limbs are wounded, but tayammum is normally required yet dropped here due to lack of hands (the instrument for striking the earth). The hashya also discusses the option of wiping the face and arms on the ground (like a partial tayammum) as a precaution. The legal weight comes from the mukhtar and the hadith, with some ikhtilaf among scholars.

Key Terms
ناقض (naqid): What nullifies tayammum: either directly (like hadath) or through removal of the excuse.
آلة (alah): Instrument; the hands are the instrument for tayammum (striking the earth).
مقطوع اليدين والرجلين (maqtu' al-yadayn wa al-rijlayn): One whose hands and feet are amputated; a specific legal case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the true nullifier of tayammum?
A) Removal of the excuse
B) Ability to use water
C) The original hadath
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is nullified by removal of the excuse or ability to use water, but the ultimate nullifier is the original state of impurity.

The Amputee with a Face Wound: Tayammum Dropped and Prayer Without Purification
Ruling on a person without limbs and with a face wound.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling for a person without hands and feet who has a face wound, and evaluate the intra-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
When no limbs remain to perform tayammum and a wound prevents washing, purification is dropped entirely and prayer is valid without repeat.

This lesson addresses an extraordinary case: a person who has lost both hands and feet and also has a wound on the face. Since tayammum requires striking the earth with hands – the instrument – and that instrument is absent, and washing the face is impossible due to the wound, the Hanafi school rules that purification is completely waived. The hashya explains the reasoning and notes a minority view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the special case
Read the text: a person with no hands and no feet, and a wound on the face.
The case combines two obstacles: loss of limbs for tayammum and inability to wash the face for wudu.
2
Understand why tayammum is normally required but dropped
Tayammum uses hands to strike the earth; without hands, the act is impossible. Hence tayammum is dropped.
The instrument (alah) is missing, so the obligation falls away.
3
State the correct ruling
He prays without any purification (neither wudu nor tayammum) and does not repeat the prayer.
This is the most correct (al-ahh) position according to al-Tahtawi.
4
Examine the minority views
Some scholars said prayer is dropped entirely; others said he should wipe his face and arms (stumps) on the earth as a precaution.
The hashya discusses these as weaker opinions.
5
Explain the reasoning
The obligation of purification is tied to ability. Since both wudu and tayammum are impossible, the obligation is lifted. The hadith's condition 'if you find water' implies a general principle of ability.
This is based on the principle of 'la taklif illa bi al-wus' (no obligation beyond capacity).

Source Text

Definition and Conditions of Wiping over Khuffs
Opening of the chapter on wiping over khuffs with definition and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the khuff, list its conditions for valid wiping, explain the basis in Sunnah, and identify when wiping becomes obligatory.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a proven Sunnah concession lightening washing, but it has strict conditions.

Wiping over khuffs is a well-established concession (rukhsah) in the Hanafi school, but its validity depends on precise conditions. This lesson unpacks the opening passage of the chapter from the hashya of al-Tahtawi, clarifying the definition of the khuff, its basis in the Sunnah, the cause and conditions, and the ruling. We will also see how the concession can become obligatory in certain circumstances, such as when washing would cause hardship or missing a prayer time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its basis
Recognize that wiping over khuffs is established by the Sunnah (both sayings and actions of the Prophet). The text refutes those who claim it is from the Quran, emphasizing its mutawatir transmission.
Basis: Sunnah qat'iyyah, not subject to debate.
2
Define the khuff and its cause
State the definition: the khuff is a covering that reaches above the ankles. The cause (sabab) for the concession is simply wearing the khuff in a state of purity.
Khuff is derived from 'khiffah' (lightness) as it lightens the obligation.
3
List the conditions for valid wiping
The khuff must: (1) cover the ankles (site of washing), (2) be durable enough to walk a mile, (3) not be torn in a way that prevents wiping, (4) be worn in a state of wudu, and (5) the duration of wiping (24h resident, 72h traveler) must not have expired.
These conditions ensure the khuff serves as a proper substitute for washing.
4
Understand the ruling and its obligatory cases
The default ruling is permissibility (ibahah) and a reward for following Sunnah. However, al-Tahtawi quotes al-Bahr: wiping becomes obligatory (wajib) if washing would cause hardship, such as insufficient water, missing the prayer time, or missing standing at Arafah. This is a special feature of this ummah.
Ruling has two aspects: worldly (salah valid) and otherworldly (thawab).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب المسح على الخفين ثبت بالسنة قولاً وفعلاً والخف الساتر للكعبين مأخوذ من الخفة لأن الحكم به خف من الغسل إلى المسح وسببه لبس الخف وشرطه كونه ساتراً محل الفرض صالحاً للمسح مع بقاء المدة وحكمه حل الصلاة به في مدته، وركنه مسح القدر المفروض وصفته أنه شرع رخصة وكيفيته الابتداء من أصابع القدم خطوطاً بأصابع اليد إلى الساق (صح) أي جاز قوله : (ثبت بالسنة رد لمن قال انه ثبت بالكتاب على قراءة الجر. قال في البحر : وينبغي أن يجب في صور منها لو غسل رجليه لا يكفيه الماء، ولو مسح بكفيه فإنه يلزمه المسح ومنها لو غسل يفوته الوقت، أو الوقوف بعرفة فإنه . يمسح لزوماً، وهو من خصائص هذه الأمة اهـ قوله : (صالحاً للمسح بأن يمكن متابعة المشي فيه فرسخاً وأن لا يكون مخروقاً بخرق مانع قوله : ( وحكمه حل الصلاة (الخ هذا الحكم الدنيوي، وأما حكمه الأخروي فهو الثواب إن قصد فعل السنة قوله : (وصفته أنه شرع رخصة) اختلف هل هو من
Chapter on wiping over the khuffs. It is established by the Sunnah in word and deed. The khuff is that which covers the ankles, derived from lightness because the ruling thereby lightens the obligation from washing to wiping. Its cause is wearing the khuff. Its condition is that it covers the site of the obligation, is suitable for wiping, with the duration (of the wipe) remaining. Its ruling is that it permits prayer (with it) during its period. Its pillar is wiping the obligatory amount. Its description is that it is legislated as a concession. Its manner is to begin from the toes with lines using the fingers of the hand up to the leg. (Sahih) i.e., it is permissible. His saying: (established by the Sunnah) is a refutation of those who said it is established by the Book upon the reading of jar (a grammatical issue). He said in al-Bahr: it becomes obligatory in cases, including: if he washes his feet, water is insufficient for him; if he wipes with his palms, then wiping becomes incumbent upon him; and if washing would cause him to miss the time or standing at Arafah, then he wipes necessarily, and this is a specificity of this ummah. His saying: (suitable for wiping) means that one can continue walking in them for a mile and that they are not torn with a tear that prevents (wiping). His saying: (and its ruling is the permissibility of prayer) – this is a worldly ruling; as for the otherworldly ruling, it is reward if he intends to perform the Sunnah. His saying: (and its description is that it is legislated as a concession) – there is disagreement whether it is...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on wiping over khuffs (leather socks). It defines the khuff, its basis in Sunnah (refuting those who claim it is from the Quran), and outlines its cause (wearing the khuff), condition (covering the ankles, intact, suitable for walking), ruling (permitting prayer), pillar (wiping the required area), description (a concession), and manner (wiping from toes up to leg). The hashya then expands: it becomes obligatory in certain situations to wipe, such as when water is insufficient for washing, or when washing would cause missing the prayer time or standing at Arafat, and this is a special dispensation for this ummah. The condition of being 'suitable' means the khuff must be durable (for a mile walk) and not have a hole that prevents wiping. The ruling is divided into worldly (permissibility of prayer) and otherworldly (reward for following Sunnah). The passage cuts off during a discussion on the nature of the concession, but the provided text is a complete introduction.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock that covers the ankles, worn for wiping during wudu instead of washing the feet.
رخصة (rukhsah): A concession from the original obligation (washing feet) due to ease.
مسح (mash): Wiping; passing wet fingers over the surface of the khuff.

Ruling on Wiping over Khuffs and Material Conditions
Establishes permissibility and details material requirements for khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs, identify the three categories of khuff material, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute over non-leather khuffs.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is a confirmed sunnah based on mutawatir hadith, provided the khuffs are thick enough to prevent water seepage.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on wiping over khuffs (masah 'ala al-khuffayn). The permissibility is established by widespread hadith reports, making it a sunnah mu'akkadah. However, the material of the khuff must meet specific conditions of thickness and durability. The lesson also covers the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding non-leather materials and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the act is wiping over khuffs for minor impurity. The hukm level is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), not fard or wajib. Denial after proof may lead to disbelief.
Reward is greater for washing feet (azimah), but wiping is a valid license.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is mutawatir hadith reports from over seventy Companions, including the ten promised Paradise. The text cites al-Hasan al-Basri: seventy men saw the Prophet wipe over khuffs.
The hadith is qat'i al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (interpretation yields sunnah, not fard).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The widespread practice of the Prophet (SAW) and Companions demonstrates permissibility. The absence of an explicit command indicates it is not obligatory but a recommended license.
The Hanafi usul principle: al-amr yufidu al-wujub, but here the evidence is action not command.
4
Analyse the conditions for khuffs
Three categories exist: (1) thin without soles – no wiping by consensus; (2) thick with soles – wiping allowed by consensus; (3) thick without soles – disputed. The relied-upon position allows wiping on thick non-leather material that stays on the leg without tying.
Boots (jurmooq) with openings are permissible if openings are covered.
5
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa initially required leather; Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed thick non-leather. Imam returned to their view before his death, and the fatwa is on this view.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة المسح على الخفين في الطهارة من (الحدث الأصغر ) لما ورد فيه من الأخبار المستفيضة، فيخشى على منكره الكفر وإذا اعتقد جوازه وتكلف قلعه يثاب بالعزيمة لأن الغسل أشق والمسافر إذا تيمم لجنابة، ثم أحدث حدثاً أصغر ووجد ماء كافياً لأعضاء الوضوء يلزمه قلع الخف، وغسل رجليه ولا له مسحه للجنابة (للرجال والنساء) سفراً وحضر الحاجة يصح وبدونها لإطلاق النصوص الشامل للنساء ولو كانا) أي الخفان متخذين (من شيء ثخين رخصة الإسقاط أي المسقطة للعزيمة كقصر الصلاة للمسافر، أو من قبيل رخصة الترفيه بمعنى التخفيف دفعاً للحرج مع بقاء العزيمة كفطر المسافر جري عن الأول بعضهم، وعلى الثاني أكثر الأصوليين قوله : (صح المسح على الخفين (الخ) الصحة في العيادات كونها توجب تفريغ الذمة وهو المقصود الدنيوي، ويلزمه الثواب عند القبول وهو المقصود الأخروي والوجوب كون الفعل لو أتى به يثاب ولو تركه يعاقب، ويتبعه تفريغ الذمة اهـ من الشرح ملخصاً قوله: (من الحدث الأصغر) أما الجنابة ونحوها لا يصح فيها المسح لورود النص بذلك ولأن الرخصة للحرج فيما يتكرر ولا حرج في الجنابة ونحوها لعدم التكرار وصوّر حافظ الدين في الكافي صورة مسح الجنب تقريباً للمتعلم بأن توضأ ولبس جوربين مجلدين، ثم أجنب ليس له أن يشدهما ويغسل سائر جسده مضطجعاً يعني أو ما دار جلية على شيء مرتفع، ويمسح عليه اهـ من الشرح ملخصاً قوله : لما ورد فيه من الأخبار المستفيضة) حتى الحفاظ : إن عنهم فقد صح رجوعهم ، قال جمع من الله خبر المسح متواتر كما في فتح الباري، وقال الحسن البصري: حدثني سبعون رجلاً من أصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنهم رأوه يمسح على الخفين كما في البدائع، وذكر الحافظ في فتح الباري عن بعضهم أنه روى المسح أكثر من الثمانين منهم العشرة المبشرون رضي الله تعالى اهـ. وما روي عن الصحابة كابن عباس وأبي هريرة، وعائشة رضي عنهم من إنكاره إلى جوازه كما في النهاية وغيرها قوله : يثاب بالعزيمة الأولى أن يقول كان أفضل لأن الخلاف في الأفضلية بدليل التعليل لا في حصول الثواب، وما ذكره هو ما عليه الجمهور، وقالوا: إلا أن يكون بحضرة منكره، فالمسح أفضل ترغيماً له، وقال أبو الحسن الرستني من أصحابنا المسح أفضل مطلقاً، وهو أصح الروايتين عن أحمد لنفي التهمة تزول بالمسح أحياناً . قوله : (والمسافر الخ خص المسافر لأن الغالب في السفر عدم الماء، وإلا فالمدار على عدم الماء. قوله : (للجنابة) أي لأن الجنابة سرت إلى القدم وهو علة لقوله لا يصح قوله : (لا) طلاق النصوص الخ ولأن الخطاب الوارد لأحدهما يكون وارداً في حق الآخر ما لم ينص على التخصيص. قوله من شيء ثخين) اعلم أن المسئلة على ثلاثة وجوه إن كانا رقيقين غير منعلين لا يجوز المسح عليهما إتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين منعلين جاز إتفاقاً، وإن كانا ثخينين غير منعلين فهو محل الإختلاف كما في الخانية، وفي شرح الزاهدي للكتاب يجوز المسح على الجرموق المشقوق على ظهر القدم، وله أزرار عن نفسه قلنا [؟] هي غير الجلد) كلبد وجوخ وكرباس يستمسك على الساق من غير شد لا يشف الماء وهو قولهما وإليه رجع الإمام وعليه الفتوى لأنه في معنى المتخذ من الجلد (سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد) ويقال له جورب منعل بوضع الجلد أسفله كالنعل للقدم وإذا جعل أعلاه وأسفله يقال له مجلد (أو (لا) جلد بهما أصلاً وهو الثخين
Book of Purity. Wiping over khuffs in purification from (minor impurity) due to the widespread reports about it; so disbelief is feared for its denier. If one believes in its permissibility and burdens himself to remove them (to wash), he is rewarded for the 'azimah because washing is more strenuous. The traveler who performs tayammum for janabah, then has minor impurity and finds water sufficient for the limbs of wudu—he must remove the khuff and wash his feet, and he may not wipe over it (the khuff) due to janabah. (For men and women) traveling and residing: it is valid out of need and without it, due to the general texts that include women. 'And if they (the two khuffs) are made of something thick' — a license of exemption, i.e., one that abrogates the 'azimah, like shortening prayer for the traveler, or of a license of relaxation meaning alleviation to remove hardship while the 'azimah remains, like breaking fast for the traveler. Some lean towards the first, and most usul scholars towards the second. His saying: (Wiping over khuffs is valid) — validity in acts of worship means it causes the discharge of liability, which is the worldly purpose, and reward follows upon acceptance, which is the otherworldly purpose. Obligation means if one performs the act he is rewarded, and if he abandons it he is punished, and discharge of liability follows it. End summary from the sharh. His saying: (from minor impurity) — as for janabah and the like, wiping is not valid in them, due to the text to that effect, and because the license is for hardship in what is repetitive; there is no hardship in janabah and the like due to lack of repetition. Hafiz al-Din in al-Kafi depicted the case of a junub person for the learner: that he performed wudu and wore two lined socks, then became junub; he may not tighten them and he washes the rest of his body lying down, meaning or whatever part touches something elevated, and wipes over them. End summary from sharh. His saying: (due to the widespread reports about it) — even the memorizers of hadith: indeed they retracted their denial. A group said: the hadith of wiping is mutawatir as in Fath al-Bari. Al-Hasan al-Basri said: seventy men from the Companions of the Messenger of God (SAW) informed me that they saw him wiping over khuffs, as in al-Bada'i'. Al-Hafiz in Fath al-Bari mentioned from some that more than eighty narrated wiping, among them the ten promised Paradise. And what is reported from the Companions like Ibn 'Abbas, Abu Hurayra, and 'A'isha (R) of their denial is interpreted as turning to its permissibility as in al-Nihaya and others. His saying: (he is rewarded for the 'azimah) — it would be better to say it is more virtuous because the difference is in superiority by evidence of the reasoning, not in obtaining reward. What he mentioned is what the majority hold. They said: unless he is in the presence of a denier, then wiping is better to annoy him. Abu al-Hasan al-Rustini from our companions said: wiping is absolutely better, and it is the more correct of the two narrations from Ahmad, to remove suspicion, which is removed by wiping sometimes. His saying: (the traveler) — he specified the traveler because most often travel lacks water; otherwise the criterion is lack of water. His saying: (due to janabah) — i.e., because janabah reaches the foot, and it is the cause for his saying it is not valid. His saying: (no) — due to the generality of texts etc., and because the address to one of them applies to the other unless specification is explicitly indicated. His saying: (from something thick) — know that the case has three aspects: if they are thin without soles, wiping on them is not permissible by consensus; if they are thick with soles, wiping is permissible by consensus; if they are thick without soles, that is the point of disagreement as in al-Khaniyya. In Sharh al-Zahidi for the book: it is permissible to wipe over the boot that is split on the top of the foot and has buttons. 'From himself we said' [?] it is (other than leather) like felt, broadcloth, and cotton that stay on the shin without tying, does not let water seep through, and that is their (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad's) view, and the Imam returned to it, and on it is the fatwa, because it is akin to leather. (Whether it has a leather sole) — it is called a sock with a sole by placing leather underneath like a sole for the foot. And if its top and bottom are made of leather, it is called lined. (Or not) — i.e., no leather at all, and that is the thick type.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi discusses the ruling on wiping over khuffs (leather socks) in the Hanafi school. The ruling is that wiping over khuffs is permissible for minor impurity (hadath asghar) based on numerous mutawatir hadiths. Denial of this ruling after its establishment is dangerous and may lead to disbelief. However, if one chooses to remove the khuffs and wash the feet instead, they receive the reward for performing the 'azimah (the more strenuous act). The license (rukhsa) of wiping does not replace the 'azimah but alleviates hardship. The text then addresses a specific case: a traveler who performed tayammum due to janabah (major impurity) and then had minor impurity; he must remove his khuffs and wash his feet because the khuffs were not put on in a state of purity for minor impurity. The ruling applies to both men and women, whether traveling or at home, whether out of need or not, because the general evidence includes all. The material of the khuff must be thick (thakhin) such that water does not seep through. Three categories exist: thin without soles (no wiping by consensus), thick with soles (wiping allowed by consensus), and thick without soles (disputed; the relied-upon position is that wiping is allowed, as Imam Abu Hanifa returned to the view of the Sahibayn). The text also mentions that boots (jurmooq) with openings on the top of the foot are permissible as long as the openings are covered. The return of Imam Abu Hanifa to the permissibility of wiping on thick non-leather material is noted, and the fatwa is on this view.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A covering for the foot made of thick material (leather or other) that prevents water seepage, worn to allow wiping during wudu.
ثخين (thakhīn): Thick material that does not allow water to pass through to the foot.
منعل (muna''al): A khuff or sock that has a sole made of leather or other material attached at the bottom.
جرموق (jurmūq): A type of boot that covers the leg, often split on the top of the foot and fastened with buttons or laces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is true about wiping over khuffs in the Hanafi school?
A) It is only allowed for travelers.
B) It is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
C) It requires khuffs made of leather.
D) It invalidates wudu if the khuffs are thin.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over khuffs is a sunnah license valid for both men and women in all circumstances, provided the khuffs are thick enough to prevent water seepage and were worn after wudu.

Taharah — Purification

8 min
First Condition for Wiping over Khuffs: Complete Purity of Feet
Explains the first of seven conditions: khuffs must be worn after the feet are fully purified.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the first condition for wiping over khuffs (wearing after complete purity) and apply it to cases with splints and incomplete wudu.

Core Idea
Khuffs must be worn after the feet are purified — actual wash or equivalent.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession in wudu, but it has strict conditions. The first and most important is that the khuffs be put on after the feet have been fully purified. This lesson explores what 'complete purity' means, including special cases like splints and wudu that is finished after wearing.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its condition
The act in question is wearing khuffs for the purpose of later wiping over them. The condition is that this wearing must occur after the feet have been completely purified.
The condition is about the moment of wearing, not the state of wudu in general.
2
Understand 'complete purity' – actual vs. virtual
Complete purity normally means washing the feet with water. However, if a splint (jabira) is present, wiping over the splint during wudu is legally equivalent to washing. Wearing the khuff over a splint that has been wiped satisfies the condition.
The text explicitly says 'because wiping over a splint is like washing (al-ghusl).'
3
Analyze the exception for incomplete wudu
If a person washes their feet, then wears khuffs before completing the rest of wudu, the condition is still met as long as wudu is completed before any nullifier (nāqiḍ) occurs.
This shows that the condition focuses on the feet's purity at the time of wearing, not the overall wudu state.
4
Consider the excused person (ma'dhur)
If an excused person (e.g., with chronic urine dribbling) wears khuffs when their excuse is not active (i.e., a moment of purity), their valid wiping period is the same as a non-excused person.
The khuff acts as a barrier to prevent hadath from reaching the foot, but it does not remove hadath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويشترط لجواز المسح على الخفين سبعة شرائط الأول) منها لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين ولو حكماً كجبيرة بالرجلين أو بإحداهما مسحها ولبس الخف خفه لأن مسح الجبيرة كالغسل (ولو) كان اللبس (قبل كمال الوضوء إذا أتمه) أي الوضوء قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء) لوجود الشرط والخف مانع سراية الحدث لا رافع وإذا توضأ المعذور ولبس مع انقطاع عذره فمدته مثل غير
And for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs, seven conditions are required: The first is wearing them after washing the two feet, even if virtually, like a splint on the two feet or one of them—he wipes over it and wears the khuff over it, because wiping over a splint is like washing. And if the wearing is before completing wudu, when he completes it (the wudu) before a nullifier of wudu occurs, the condition is present. And the khuff prevents the transmission of the hadath, it does not remove it. And if an excused person performs wudu and wears (khuffs) when his excuse ceases, then his period (for wiping) is like that of one without an excuse.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage outlines the first of seven conditions for wiping over khuffs: the khuffs must be worn after the feet are purified. The condition is satisfied if the feet are washed directly or if a splint (jabira) is present. In the case of a splint, wiping over the splint is equivalent to washing, so wearing the khuff over it is valid. If a person begins wudu, wears the khuffs before completing it, and then completes the wudu without any nullifying act, the wearing is considered to have occurred after purity, and wiping is allowed. The khuff acts as a barrier that prevents the hadath from reaching the foot; it does not remove the hadath but only blocks its contagion. Finally, an excused person (e.g., one with chronic incontinence) who wears khuffs after wudu when the excuse is not active has a wiping period like that of a non-excused person, i.e., the duration is based on the normal time limit.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīrah): A splint or bandage used to set a broken bone; wiping over it in wudu is treated as washing.
معذور (ma‘dhūr): A person with a chronic excuse (e.g., constant urine dribbling) that prevents complete purity.
ناقض (nāqiḍ): Anything that nullifies wudu, such as passing wind or blood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has a splint on his foot and wipes over it during wudu, then wears a khuff, is the khuff considered worn after purity?
A) No, because a splint is not a full washing.
B) Yes, because wiping over a splint is like washing in terms of purity.
C) Only if the splint covers the entire foot.
D) Only if the khuff is also made of leather.

Key Takeaway
The first condition for wiping over khuffs is that they be worn after the feet are completely purified—either by washing or by an equivalent, such as wiping over a splint.

The First Condition for Wiping over Khuffs
Explains first condition and sub-rulings including material, jabeera, and ma'dhur

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for wiping over khuffs, explain the ruling on non-leather materials, and apply the condition to cases involving splints and chronic excuses.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs requires wearing them after washing feet—even legally via a splint—and the khuff must be waterproof.

The permissibility of wiping over khuffs (leather socks) is a well-known concession in wudu. However, it is subject to conditions. This passage focuses on the first and most fundamental condition: the khuffs must be worn after the feet have been washed during wudu. The text also clarifies what constitutes a valid khuff, including the Hanafi position on non-leather materials, and addresses special cases like splints and the person with a chronic excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first condition
The text states: 'الشرط الأول لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين' – the first condition is wearing them after washing the feet. Understand that this means the feet must be ritually pure (tahir) at the moment of wearing.
The condition is about timing, not about the khuff itself.
2
Understand the material of the khuff
The text expands on what material is acceptable. Although Quran and hadith originally refer to leather, the Hanafi school extends permission to thick non-leather materials that prevent water seepage, based on the hadith of wiping over socks. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, which Imam Abu Hanifa returned to.
The key is that the material must be waterproof and stay on without tying.
3
Apply the condition when wearing before complete wudu
The text allows wearing the khuffs before finishing wudu, as long as the wudu is completed before any nullifier occurs. This is because the khuff prevents hadath from reaching the foot, but does not remove it.
The khuff is a barrier (mani'), not a remover (rafi').
4
Apply the condition to a splint (jabeera)
If a person has a splint on the foot, wiping over the splint counts as washing the foot. Therefore, wearing the khuff after that is valid – it is as if the foot was washed legally.
The ruling on jabeera is based on necessity; wiping over it suffices for wudu.
5
Apply the condition to the excused person (ma'dhur)
For a ma'dhur (e.g., someone with incontinence), his wudu remains valid only within the prayer time. If he wears khuffs while his excuse is present, his wiping period is limited to that time; he cannot wipe after the time ends because that would imply the khuff removes hadath.
Different ruling if he wears them while not excused: then his period is normal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير الجلد) كلبد وجوخ وكرباس يستمسك على الساق من غير شد لا يشف الماء وهو قولهما وإليه رجع الإمام وعليه الفتوى لأنه في معنى المتخذ من الجلد (سواء كان لهما نعل من جلد) ويقال له جورب منعل بوضع الجلد أسفله كالنعل للقدم وإذا جعل أعلاه وأسفله يقال له مجلد (أو (لا) جلد بهما أصلاً وهو الثخين ويشترط لجواز المسح على الخفين سبعة شرائط الأول) منها لبسهما بعد غسل الرجلين ولو حكماً كجبيرة بالرجلين أو بإحداهما مسحها ولبس الخف خفه لأن مسح الجبيرة كالغسل (ولو) كان اللبس (قبل كمال الوضوء إذا أتمه) أي الوضوء قبل حصول ناقض للوضوء) لوجود الشرط والخف مانع سراية الحدث لا رافع وإذا توضأ المعذور ولبس مع انقطاع عذره فمدته مثل غير المعذور وإلا تقيد بوقته فلا يمسح بعده قوله : (فلا يمسح يمسح لأن وضوء المعذور يبطل بخروج الوقت، لظهور الحدث السابق، فلو جاز المسح بعد ذلك لكان الخف رافعاً للحدث لا مانعاً اهـ من الشرح
Other than leather) such as felt, broadcloth, and thick cotton that stays on the shin without tying, not allowing water to seep through - this is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and the Imam (Abu Hanifa) returned to it, and the fatwa is upon it, because it is in the meaning of what is taken from leather. (Whether they have a sole of leather) and it is called a 'mun'al sock' by placing leather at the bottom like a sole for the foot; if its top and bottom are made of leather, it is called 'mujallad'. (Or) no leather at all - this is thick (material). Seven conditions are prescribed for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs: the first) is wearing them after washing the feet, even legally like a splint on the feet or on one foot when one wipes over it and wears the khuff, because wiping over a splint is like washing. (Even if) the wearing was (before completion of wudu, when he completes) the wudu before the occurrence of a nullifier of wudu, because the condition exists, and the khuff prevents the transmission of hadath (ritual impurity), it does not remove it. When a person with an excuse performs wudu and wears (the khuffs) while his excuse ceases, his period (of wiping) is like that of one without an excuse; otherwise it is restricted to his time, so he does not wipe after it. He said: ('He does not wipe') - because the wudu of the excused person becomes invalid with the exit of time, due to the manifestation of the previous hadath; if wiping were permissible after that, the khuff would be removing the hadath, not preventing it. End from the Sharh.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the first condition for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs (leather socks). The text first clarifies what constitutes a valid khuff for wiping: it is a covering that stays on the shin without tying and does not allow water to seep through to the foot. The relied-upon position (fatwa) is that wiping is allowed on khuffs made of thick non-leather materials like felt, broadcloth, or cotton, as long as they meet the waterproof criterion. This is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (qawlahuma), and Imam Abu Hanifa returned to this view before his death. The condition then states that the khuffs must be worn after washing the feet, meaning after completing the wudu of the feet. Even if one has a splint (jabeera) on the foot, wiping over the splint counts as washing, so wearing the khuff after that is valid. If one wears the khuffs before completing wudu (e.g., after washing the first foot but before washing the second), it is still valid provided the wudu is completed before any hadath (ritual impurity) occurs. The khuff acts as a barrier preventing hadath from reaching the feet; it does not remove hadath. For a person with a chronic excuse (ma'dhur), if he performs wudu and wears the khuffs while his excuse is not present, his wiping period is like that of a normal person (24 hours for resident, 3 days for traveler). If his excuse is still present, his wiping is limited to the time (i.e., only until the end of that prayer time). The commentary explains that the excused person's wudu breaks with the exit of the prayer time, so he cannot wipe after that because it would imply the khuff removes hadath, which it does not.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A covering worn on the foot, traditionally leather, but extended in this text to thick non-leather materials that prevent water seepage.
جبيرة (jabeera): A splint or bandage applied to a wound or fracture; wiping over it counts as washing the limb for wudu.
معذور (ma'dhur): A person with a chronic excuse (e.g., incontinence) that constantly breaks wudu; his wudu is valid only for the time of a prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person wears khuffs after washing only one foot, then completes wudu before any hadath occurs?
A) Wiping is not valid because the feet were not washed completely before wearing.
B) Wiping is valid because he completed wudu before hadath.
C) Wiping is valid only if he removed the khuffs and rewore them after full wudu.
D) Wiping is invalid because the khuff was worn on a foot that had not been washed.

Key Takeaway
The first condition for wiping over khuffs is wearing them after the feet are washed, with the khuff acting as a barrier, not a remover of impurity.
