Conditions 2-4: Covering Ankles, Walking Ability, and No Large Holes
Details conditions 2-4 for khuff wiping with commentary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the second, third, and fourth conditions for valid wiping over khuffs and apply them to determine validity in given scenarios.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs requires covering ankles, ability to walk, and no large holes.

In this lesson, we continue the conditions for wiping over khuffs. We already know the khuff must be worn after wudu. Now we examine three more: covering the ankles, being able to walk normally, and being free from large holes. These conditions ensure that wiping is a genuine travel concession, not an ordinary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second condition: covering ankles
The khuff must cover both ankle bones from the sides. It is not required to cover them from above; a short khuff is fine. If the khuff does not cover naturally but is extended with thick material, wiping is valid.
The Hanafi madhhab differs from the Samarkand school on this.
2
Identify the third condition: ability to walk continuously
The khuff must allow normal walking for at least one farsakh (approx 5.5 km). If made of rigid materials like glass, wood, or iron that prevent walking, the concession is lost.
Some definitions include covering travel distance.
3
Identify the fourth condition: no large holes
The khuff must be free of holes that expose the foot. The threshold is the size of three of the smallest toes of the foot. Holes are measured during walking, not at rest. A hole that admits a needle is the smallest considered.
There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether to measure by hand fingers or foot toes.
4
Apply the dispute: measurement by foot toes vs. hand fingers
The relied-upon view uses the smallest toes of the foot. If toes are exposed, the actual exposed area is considered; exposing the big toe with its neighbor does not harm if their area equals three small toes.
This affects validity in borderline cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) الشرط الثاني سترهما) أي الخفين (للكعبين) من الجوانب، فلا يضر نظر الكعبين من أعلى خف قصير الساق والذي لا يغطي الكعبين إذا خيط به ثخين كجوخ يصح المسح عليه (و) الشرط الثالث إمكان متابعة المشي فيهما) أي الخفين فتنعدم الرخصة لانعدام شرطها وهو متابعة المشي (فلا يجوز) المسح (علی خف) صنع (من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد لما قلنا (و) الشرط (الرابع خلو كل منهما) أي الخفين عن خرق قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع القدم) لأنه محل المشي، واختلف في اعتبارها مضمومة أو مفرجة فإذا انكشفت الأصابع اعتبر ذاتها فلا يضر كشف الإبهام مع جاره وإن بلغ قدر ثلاث هي أصغرها على الأصح، والخرق طولاً يدخل فيه ثلاث أصابع ولا يرى شيء من القدم عند المشي لصلابته لا يمنع، ولا يضم ما دون ثلاثة من رجل المثله من الأخرى، وأقل خرق يجمع هو ما يدخل فيه مسلة ولا يعتبر ما دونه
قوله : (والذي لا يغطي الكعبين) وذلك كالزر بول، وهو في عرف أهل الشام ما يسمى مركوباً في عرف أهل مصر كما في : الأخيار وقولهم في سب الرقيق زربون تحريف قوله : (إذا خيط به ثخين) التشميل بالثخين هو المذهب خلافاً لما عليه أهل سمرقند من جواز المسح إذا ستر الكعبين باللفافة. قوله : (إمكان متابعة المشي) أي المعتاد فرسخاً فأكثر كما في حاشية الهداية، أو المراد قطع مسافة السفر كما في المحيط كذا في القهستاني وبالأول جزم في الدرر. قوله: (من أصغر أصابع القدم) وفي رواية الحسن يعتبر قدرها من أصابع اليد واختاره الرازي إعتباراً بالمسح اهـ وتعتبر الثلاثة أصابع في أي موضع كان بعد أن يكون أسفل من الكعبين وهو ظاهر إطلاق المتون، واختاره السرخسي، والكمال ولو تحت القدم أو في العقب وقيل الخرق تحت القدم لا يمنع ما لم يبلغ أكثر القدم، وقيل إن كان يخرج أقل من نصف العقب لا يمنع، وإلا منع قوله: (لا يمنع) والمانع هو المنفرج الذي يرى ما تحته من الرجل، أو المنضم الذي ينفرج عند المشي فالعبرة بإنفراجه حالة المشي دون حالة الوضع كما في الحلبي قوله: (ولا يضم ما دون ثلاثة) بخلاف النجاسة المتفرقة في خفيه أو ثوبه أو مكانه أو بدنه أو في المجموع، وبخلاف إنكشاف العورة فإنهما يجمعان قوله : (وأقل خرق يجمع الخ) هذا هو المشهور في المذهب، وذكر في خزانة الفتاوي والتوشيح عن أبي يوسف أنه لا تجمع الخروق سواء كانت في خف، أو خفين وارتضاه الكمال وقواه ابن أمير حاج واستظهره في البحر ورده النهر فليراجعها من رامها. قوله : (ولا يعتبر ما دونه) إلحاقاً له بموضع الخرز.
(And) the second condition: that they (the khuffs) cover the ankles from the sides; it does not harm if the ankles are seen from the top of a short-legged khuff. If one does not cover the ankles but a thick material like broadcloth is sewn to it, wiping over it is valid. (And) the third condition: the possibility of continuous walking in them (the khuffs); the concession is absent due to the absence of its condition, which is continuous walking. So wiping over a khuff made of glass, wood, or iron is not permissible, due to what we have said. (And) the fourth condition: each of them (the khuffs) is free from a hole of the size of three small toes of the foot, because it is the place of walking. There is a difference of opinion whether the three are considered together or separated. When the toes are uncovered, the actual toes are considered; exposure of the big toe with its neighbor does not harm even if it reaches the size of three (small toes) – this is the most correct view. A hole lengthwise through which three toes can enter but nothing of the foot is seen during walking due to stiffness does not prevent (wiping). What is less than three from one foot is not combined with the other. The smallest hole that is combined is one that admits a needle; what is less is not considered. He said: ('And that which does not cover the ankles') – that is like a zarbul (short boot), which in the custom of the people of Syria is called 'markub' in the custom of the people of Egypt, as in al-Akhyar, and their expression in insulting slaves 'zarbun' is a distortion. He said: ('If a thick material is sewn to it') – covering with thick material is the madhhab, contrary to the view of the people of Samarkand who permit wiping if the ankles are covered by wrapping. He said: ('Possibility of continuous walking') – meaning normal walking for a farsakh or more, as in Hashiyat al-Hidaya; or it means covering the distance of travel, as in al-Muhit and al-Qahastani; the first is affirmed in al-Durar. He said: ('From the smallest toes of the foot') – and in the narration of al-Hasan, the measure is taken from the fingers of the hand, and al-Razi chose this, based on wiping. The three toes are considered in any location as long as it is below the ankles; this is the apparent meaning of the texts, and al-Sarakhsi and al-Kamal chose this, even if under the foot or the heel. It was said that a hole under the foot does not prevent unless it reaches most of the foot; it was said that if less than half of the heel is exposed, it does not prevent, otherwise it prevents. He said: ('Does not prevent') – the preventer is the open hole through which the foot is seen, or the closed hole that opens during walking; the criterion is its opening during walking, not during rest, as in al-Halabi. He said: ('What is less than three is not combined') – unlike scattered impurity on his khuffs, garment, place, body, or in total, and unlike exposure of the private parts, which are combined. He said: ('The smallest hole that is combined, etc.') – this is the well-known view in the madhhab, and it is mentioned in Khizanat al-Fatawa and al-Tawshih from Abu Yusuf that holes are not combined, whether in one khuff or both, and al-Kamal approved and strengthened it, and Ibn Amir Hajj supported it, and it was preferred in al-Bahr, but al-Nahr rejected it; so consult those who desire. He said: ('What is less is not considered') – by including it with the place of stitching.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage details the second, third, and fourth conditions for the permissibility of wiping over khuffs, along with explanatory commentary. The second condition: the khuff must cover the ankles from the sides. It is not required that the ankle be covered from above; a short-legged khuff is acceptable if the ankles are visible from above. If the khuff does not naturally cover the ankles, but a thick material like broadcloth is sewn to extend it, wiping is valid. This is the madhhab position, contrary to the Samarkand school who permitted wiping if the ankles are covered by wrapping. The third condition: the khuff must allow continuous walking. If made of materials like glass, wood, or iron that impede normal walking, the concession of wiping is not granted. The walking ability is defined as being able to walk normally for at least one farsakh (about 5.5 km) or to cover travel distance. The fourth condition is the most detailed: the khuff must be free from holes that expose the foot. The measure is the size of three of the smallest toes of the foot. There is a dispute whether the three toes are considered together (mangdumma) or separately (mufarrija). The correct view (al-ashah) is that if the toes are exposed, the actual toes are considered; exposing the big toe with its neighbor does not harm even if that area equals the size of three small toes. A hole lengthwise through which three toes can fit but the foot is not visible during walking due to stiffness does not prevent wiping. Holes from different feet are not combined. The smallest hole that is considered is one that admits a needle; smaller holes are ignored. The commentary further explains that a hole is considered preventer if the foot is visible through it, or if a closed hole opens during walking; the criterion is the state during walking, not at rest. Unlike scattered impurity, holes are not combined from both khuffs, according to the well-known view and the choice of Abu Yusuf, though there is disagreement.

Key Terms
كعب (ka'b): The ankle bone (malleolus) on each side of the foot; the khuff must cover both ankles.
فرسخ (farsakh): A unit of distance, approximately 5.5 km or 3 miles; used to define normal walking ability.
مسلة (misalla): A needle; the smallest hole size that is considered for combining holes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a khuff that has a hole large enough to admit one small toe but is in a stiff material such that the foot is not visible during walking?
A) Wiping is invalid because the hole is present.
B) Wiping is valid because the hole does not meet the three-toe threshold.
C) Wiping is valid because the foot is not visible during walking due to stiffness.
D) Wiping is invalid unless the hole is patched.

Key Takeaway
The validity of wiping over khuffs depends on the khuff covering the ankles, being walkable, and having no hole larger than three small toes.

Seven Conditions for Wiping over Khuffayn
Lists and explains seven preconditions for valid masah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the seven conditions for valid masah over khuffayn and apply them to determine the validity of wiping in specific scenarios.

Core Idea
A khuff must cover the ankle, allow walking, be sturdy, waterproof, and free from large holes.

This lesson examines the seven preconditions (shurut) that must be satisfied for wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) to be valid in the Hanafi school. These conditions ensure that the concession of masah is properly applied; if any condition is missing, the wiping becomes invalid and the feet must be washed. Tahtawi's commentary expands on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, offering detailed measurements and exceptions for each condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify each of the seven conditions
Read through the Arabic text and note each condition as listed: covering the ankles, ability for continuous walking, freedom from large holes, staying on without tying, waterproofness, and having sufficient front foot length.
The first condition (wearing after complete wudu) is not mentioned here but is assumed from the broader fiqh context.
2
Understand the rationale behind each condition
For each condition, consider why it matters for the validity of masah. For example, the walking condition ensures that the khuff is actually worn for travel, not just for show.
The concession of masah is tied to the difficulty of removing the khuff, so conditions reflect genuine need.
3
Analyze the measurement standards
Note the precise measurements: a hole of three smallest toes (joined) invalidates; the front part of the foot must be at least three smallest fingers of the hand. Recognize that these measurements are based on the place of wiping (front of foot) and walking.
There is an intra-Hanafi difference regarding whether to use toes or fingers; the relied-upon view uses the smallest toes of the foot.
4
Apply the conditions to real cases
Use the conditions to test whether a given khuff permits masah. For instance, a thick, waterproof snow boot that covers the ankles and has no holes larger than three toes is valid.
Conditions are cumulative; all must be satisfied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشرط الثاني سترهما للكعبين من الجوانب، فلا يضر نظر الكعبين من أعلى خف قصير الساق والذي لا يغطي الكعبين إذا خيط به ثخين كجوخ يصح المسح عليه. والشرط الثالث إمكان متابعة المشي فيهما فتنعدم الرخصة لانعدام شرطها وهو متابعة المشي فلا يجوز المسح على خف من زجاج أو خشب أو حديد. والشرط الرابع خلو كل منهما عن خرق قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع القدم لأنه محل المشي، واختلف في اعتبارها مضمومة أو مفرجة فإذا انكشفت الأصابع اعتبر ذاتها فلا يضر كشف الإبهام مع جاره وإن بلغ قدر ثلاث هي أصغرها على الأصح، والخرق طولاً يدخل فيه ثلاث أصابع ولا يرى شيء من القدم عند المشي لصلابته لا يمنع، ولا يضم ما دون ثلاثة من رجل المثله من الأخرى، وأقل خرق يجمع هو ما يدخل فيه مسلة ولا يعتبر ما دونه. والشرط الخامس استمساكهما على الرجلين من غير شد لثخانته إذ الرقيق لا يصلح لقطع المسافة. والشرط السادس منعهما وصول الماء إلى الجسد فلا يشفان الماء. والشرط السابع أن يبقى بكل رجل من مقدم القدم قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد ليوجد المقدار المفروض من محل المسح فإذا قطعت رجل فوق الكعب جاز وإن بقي من دون الكعب أقل من ثلاث أصابع لا يمسح لإفتراض غسل الباقي، وهو لا يجمع مع مسح خف الصحيحة. فلو كان فاقداً مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه ولو كان عقب القدم موجوداً لأنه ليس محلاً لفرض المسح، ويفترض غسله.
And the second condition is that they cover the ankles from the sides, so it does not harm if the ankles are seen from above a short-legged khuff, and that which does not cover the ankles if thick material like broadcloth is sewn to it, wiping on it is valid. And the third condition is the possibility of continuous walking in them, so the concession is absent because its condition is absent, which is continuous walking, so wiping is not permissible on a khuff made of glass, wood, or iron. And the fourth condition is that each of them be free from a hole of the size of three of the smallest toes of the foot because it is the place of walking, and there is a difference of opinion regarding considering them as joined together or separated, so if the toes are uncovered, their essence is considered, so the uncovering of the thumb together with its neighbor does not harm even if it reaches the measure of three, they are the smallest according to the most correct view, and a hole lengthwise that admits three toes and nothing of the foot is seen when walking due to its hardness does not prevent, and the sum of less than three from the foot of the like of the other foot is not added, and the least hole that combines is that which admits a needle and less than that is not considered. And the fifth condition is that they stay on the feet without tying due to their thickness, because a thin one is not suitable for covering the distance. And the sixth condition is that they prevent water from reaching the body, so they do not allow water to seep through. And the seventh condition is that there remain on each foot from the front part of the foot the measure of three of the smallest fingers of the hand, so that the obligatory amount of the place of wiping may be found. So if a foot is cut above the ankle, it is permissible, but if what remains below the ankle is less than three fingers, he does not wipe because the washing of the remaining part is obligatory, and it is not combined with the wiping of the healthy khuff. So if he lacks the front part of his foot, he does not wipe on his khuff, even if the heel of the foot exists, because it is not a place for the obligatory wiping, and its washing is obligatory.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the seven preconditions (shurut) for the validity of wiping over leather socks (khuffayn) in the Hanafi school. The author follows the matn of Maraqi al-Falah, providing expansions and clarifications. The first condition (not mentioned here) is likely that the khuff is worn after complete ablution. The second condition requires the khuff to cover the entire foot up to the ankles, including the sides. A short-sleeved khuff that does not cover the ankles can be made valid by sewing thick cloth to it. The third condition requires that the khuff allow normal walking; thus khuffs made of glass, wood, or iron are invalid because they impede walking. The fourth condition concerns holes: a hole of the size of three of the smallest toes renders the khuff invalid for wiping. The toes are measured when joined, not spread. The hole must be large enough to expose the foot during walking; a hole that does not show the foot due to the khuff's stiffness does not prevent wiping. Small holes from different khuffs are not added together. The fifth condition requires the khuff to stay on the feet without tying, meaning it must be thick enough to remain on by itself. The sixth condition requires the khuff to be waterproof. The seventh condition deals with the foot itself: the front part of the foot (where wiping is performed) must be at least three small fingers long. If the front part is missing, wiping is not valid, even if the heel exists.

Key Terms
خف (khuff): A leather sock or boot that covers the foot up to the ankles, worn for the purpose of wiping during ablution.
مسح (masah): Wiping: passing wet hands over the khuff instead of washing the feet during wudu, a concession.
شرط (shart): Condition: a prerequisite for the validity of the act; if missing, the act is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tahtawi, what is the minimum size of a hole in the khuff that invalidates wiping?
A) The size of a needle
B) The size of three of the smallest toes of the foot
C) The size of three fingers of the hand
D) The size of a dirham

Key Takeaway
The seven conditions for masah are cumulative; missing any one requires washing the feet instead of wiping.

Obligatory Amount of Wiping: Three Fingers
Specifies the fard extent of wiping and its details

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the obligatory amount of wiping over the khuff and explain why three fingers is the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Wiping three fingers is obligatory; the rest is sunnah.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the minimum obligatory amount for wiping over the khuff. The Hanafi school holds that only three fingers of the hand need to be wiped, based on the principle that the hand is the instrument and three is its majority. The text also addresses a practical detail: the water used for wiping becomes musta'mal and cannot be reused.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Find the exact obligatory amount stated: three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand.
The text says 'وفرض المسح قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد'.
2
Understand the evidence
The reasoning: the hand is the tool of wiping, and three is the majority of the fingers (analogy to tayammum).
The evidence is qiyas khafi (hidden analogy).
3
Distinguish the two aspects of obligation
The obligation is doctrinal (i'tiqadi) regarding the essence of wiping, and practical ('amali) regarding the amount.
This means the act itself is fard, and the specified minimum quantity is also fard.
4
Apply the rule about used water
If you wipe multiple times, you must renew water because the first wipe makes the moisture musta'mal (used).
Analogous to moisture remaining after wiping the head – cannot be used again.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some earlier Hanafis considered the entire foot, but the school settled on three fingers as the mufta bihi.
Al-Tahtawi states 'hua al-ashah' (this is the most correct).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرض المسح قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد وهو الأصح لأنها آلة المسح، والثلاث أكثرها، وبه قال. الفرض اعتقادي من حيث أصل المسح، وعملي من حيث المقدار. وإنما اشترط تجديد الماء في الأخيرة لأنه بالرفع الأول صار البلل مستعملاً، فلا يمسح به ثانياً. وأيضاً البلة فيه إنما بقيت بعد مسح، فلا يجوز بها المسح كالمسح ببلة بقيت بعد الرأس.
And the obligatory amount of wiping is the measure of three fingers from the smallest fingers of the hand, and this is the most correct, because they are the tool of wiping, and three is the most of them, and thus it is said. The obligation is doctrinal regarding the essence of wiping, and practical regarding the amount. And he stipulated renewing the water at the last (wipe) because with the first lift the wetness becomes used, so one should not wipe with it a second time. Also, the moisture on it remains only after wiping, so wiping with it is not permissible, like wiping with moisture remaining after (wiping) the head.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage explains the obligatory minimum amount of wiping over the khuff. The relied-upon view (al-ashah) is that it is three fingers of the hand (the smallest ones), because the hand is the instrument of wiping and three is the majority of it. The obligation is twofold: in principle (i'tiqadi) the act of wiping is fard, but in practice ('amali) the amount is fard. The text also addresses a subtle point: if one wipes multiple times, water must be renewed each time because the moisture becomes used (musta'mal) after the first wipe and cannot be reused. This is analogous to the moisture remaining after wiping the head.

Key Terms
فرض المسح (fard al-masah): The obligatory part of wiping: the minimum extent of the khuff that must be wiped, which is three fingers of the hand.
مستعمل (musta'mal): Used water: water that has been used for ritual purification and cannot be reused for the same purpose.
بلة (ballah): Moisture: the residual wetness on the hand or khuff after wiping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The entire top of the khuff
B) Half of the khuff
C) Three fingers of the smallest finger of the hand
D) One finger

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires wiping three fingers; the rest is sunnah.

Three Conditions for Wiping over Khuffs
States three conditions for the validity of wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for wiping over khuffs and determine whether a given khuff meets them.

Core Idea
Wiping on khuffs requires them to be thick, waterproof, and have at least three finger-widths front intact.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession in purification, but it is only valid if the khuffs meet specific conditions. This lesson covers the fifth, sixth, and seventh conditions from the Hanafi text: the khuff must stay on without tying, prevent water from reaching the foot, and have a minimum front portion. Understanding these ensures your wiping is valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
List the three conditions: istimsak (self-fastening), man' al-wusul (impermeability), and baqa' muqaddam al-qadam (minimum front part intact).
2
Understand each condition's rationale
Reflect on why each condition is necessary—thickness for coverage, impermeability for proper wiping, and the front part being the site of wiping.
3
Apply to edge cases
Consider cases like amputation above/below the ankle, or a torn front part—decide if wiping is allowed based on the conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرط الخامس استمساكهما على الرجلين من غير شد لثخانته إذ الرقيق لا يصلح لقطع المسافة (و) الشرط السادس منعهما وصول الماء إلى الجسد فلا يشفان الماء (و) الشرط السابع أن يبقى بكل رجل من مقدم القدم قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد ليوجد المقدار المفروض من محل المسح فإذا قطعت رجل فوق الكعب جاز وإن بقي من دون الكعب أقل من ثلاث أصابع لا يمسح لافتراض غسل الباقي، وهو لا يجمع مع مسح خف الصحيحة فلو كان فاقداً مقدم قدمه لا يمسح على خفه ولو كان عقب القدم موجوداً لأنه ليس محلاً لفرض المسح، ويفترض غسله
The fifth condition: they (the khuffs) stay on the feet without tying because of their thickness, since a thin one is not suitable for covering the distance. And the sixth condition: they prevent water from reaching the body, so they do not let water seep through. And the seventh condition: there remains on each foot from the front of the foot a measure of three fingers from the smallest finger of the hand, so that the prescribed amount from the place of wiping exists. If the foot is cut above the ankle, wiping is permissible; if less than three fingers remain below the ankle, he does not wipe, because washing what remains is obligatory, and it cannot be combined with wiping the khuff of a healthy foot. So if one lacks the front of his foot, he does not wipe over his khuff, even if the heel exists, because it is not a place for prescribed wiping, and washing it is obligatory.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from the matn lists three conditions for the khuff to be valid for wiping. The fifth condition requires the khuff to be thick enough to stay on the feet without needing to be tied. The sixth requires it to be impermeable, not allowing water to reach the foot. The seventh requires that at least three fingers' width of the front part of the khuff remain intact, as the obligatory wipe is on that front portion. If the foot is amputated above the ankle, wiping is valid on the remaining part; if less than three fingers remain, the foot must be washed. For a person missing the front part entirely, washing the heel is obligatory, and no wipe is allowed.

Key Terms
استمساك (istimsāk): The khuff staying on the feet without external tying, due to its own thickness.
مقدم القدم (muqaddam al-qadam): The front part of the foot, including the toes and the area up to the ankle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum amount that must remain from the front part of a khuff for wiping to be valid?
A) One finger from the smallest finger
B) Two fingers from the smallest finger
C) Three fingers from the smallest finger
D) Four fingers from the smallest finger

Key Takeaway
The validity of wiping over khuffs depends on three conditions: thickness, impermeability, and an intact front portion of at least three fingers.

Duration of Wiping for Resident and Traveler
Duration and start time for wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the duration of wiping over khuffs for a resident and traveler, determine the start time of the period, and apply the rules when residency or travel status changes.

Core Idea
The wiping period begins at the first hadath after wearing khuffs on tahr, not at the time of wearing.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession that allows one to pass wet fingers over the khuffs instead of washing the feet in wudu. This concession, however, is limited in time. The Prophet ﷺ specified distinct durations for residents and travelers. In this lesson, we examine those durations, the correct starting point of the counting, and the effect of changing one's status during the period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over khuffs during wudu. The ruling per the Hanafi school is that it is permissible (mubah) but with a prescribed time limit that must be observed.
The act itself is a rukhsah (concession); failing to observe the limit invalidates the wipe.
2
Locate the dalil
The Prophet ﷺ specified the durations in a hadith: the resident wipes one day and night, the traveler three days and nights.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice; it provides the basis for the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative wording of the hadith indicates obligation (wujub) to adhere to the prescribed time. The limit is explicit and binding.
The phrase 'كما روي التوقيت' indicates the hadith as the source.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on start time
There is a disagreement on when the period begins. The Hanafi position is that it begins from the first hadath (breaking of wudu) after wearing the khuffs on tahr. Alternative views start from the time of wearing or from the time of first wiping.
Each view has different practical consequences for how much time one effectively has.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The correct view in the Hanafi school is from the hadath because the need for wiping only arises after purity is broken. This is supported by the principle that the condition (tahr) is fulfilled at wearing, but the ruling (muddah) only becomes operative after hadath.
This view is mufta bihi and adopted in the relied-upon texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويمسح المقيم يوماً وليلة ويمسح المسافر ثلاثة أيام بلياليها كما روي التوقيت عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وابتداء المدة للمقيم والمسافر من وقت الحدث الحاصل بعد لبس الخفين على طهر هو الصحيح سراية الحدث وما قبله طهارة غسل وقيل من وقت اللبس وقيل من وقت المسح وإن مسح مقيم ثم سافر قبل تمام مدته أتم مدة المسافر لأن العبرة لآخر الوقت كالصلاة وإن أقام المسافر بعدما مسح يوماً وليلة نزع خفيه لأن رخصة السفر لا تبقى دون يوم وليلة يتم يوماً وليلة لأنهما مدة المقيم
The resident wipes one day and night, and the traveler wipes three days with their nights, as the timing was related from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him. The beginning of the period for the resident and traveler is from the time of the hadath that occurs after wearing the two khuffs upon tahr, this is the correct view; the hadath spreads, and whatever is before it is purity of washing. It is said: from the time of wearing, and it is said: from the time of wiping. If a resident wipes then travels before completing his period, he completes the period of a traveler, because consideration is given to the last part of the time, like prayer. If a traveler resides after having wiped a day and night, he removes his two khuffs, because the concession of travel does not remain without a day and night; he completes a day and night, because that is the period of a resident.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage provides the duration for wiping over khuffs: a resident wipes for one day and one night, a traveler for three days and nights, based on the prophetic hadith. The start time is the first hadath (breaking of wudu) after wearing the khuffs on a state of tahr (ritual purity with water). There are alternative views, but the correct view is from the hadath. If a resident starts the period then travels before finishing, he continues as a traveler for the remainder of the three days, because the end of the period determines the duration. If a traveler after wiping one day and night takes up residence, he must remove his khuffs and wash his feet, as the traveler's concession is not retained without at least a day and night of travel; if he had wiped less than a day and night when he resided, he completes the period of a resident (one day and night).

Key Terms
ابتداء المدة (ibtidā' al-muddah): The start time of the wiping period, which is from the first hadath after wearing the khuffs on tahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He continues as a traveler for three days
B) He removes his khuffs and washes
C) He continues for one more day and night
D) He continues for the remainder of the day

Key Takeaway
The wiping period begins with the first hadath after wearing khuffs on tahr, and its duration depends on residency or travel status.

Obligatory Amount of Wipe for Khuff
Specifies the obligatory quantity and performance of the wipe.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligatory amount of the wipe for khuff, identify the correct place, and distinguish between wajib and sunnah actions.

Core Idea
Three fingers from the smallest finger is the minimum obligatory wipe; method follows the Prophet's demonstration.

In the Hanafi school, wiping over the khuff (leather socks) is a concession that replaces washing the feet in wudu. However, not any wipe suffices—there is a specified obligatory amount and a prescribed method. This lesson clarifies the minimum required wipe and the sunnah manner of performing it, based on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory amount
Read the first sentence: the obligatory amount is 'three fingers from the smallest finger of the hand'. Note that it is the smallest finger, not the index or thumb, and it refers to the width of the fingers placed together.
The three fingers represent both width and length of the wipe area.
2
Locate the place of wiping
The text specifies 'the outer (top) of the front of each foot once'. Excluded are the sole, heel, sides, and leg. Wiping any place other than the top front is invalid.
Some mistakenly wipe the sides; this is not valid.
3
Understand the sunnah method
The sunnah includes spreading the fingers apart, starting from the toes towards the shin (below the ankle). The hadith of the Prophet (SAW) is cited: he poked a man washing his khuffs and demonstrated the correct way.
Starting from the shin or wiping widthwise violates the sunnah, though the minimum wajib may still be fulfilled.
4
Distinguish between wajib and sunnah
The obligatory (wajib) is the wipe of three fingers on the top front once. The sunnah includes the spread fingers, starting from toes, and wiping the full front. Omission of sunnah does not invalidate the wipe.
Sunnah actions increase reward but are not required for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفرض المسح قدر ثلاث أصابع من أصغر أصابع اليد و الأصح لأنها آلة المسح، والثلاث أكثرها وبه وردت السنة، فإن ابتل قدرها ولو بخرقة أو صب جاز والأصبع يذكر ويؤنث ومحل المسح على ظاهر مقدم كل رجل مرة واحدة فلا يصح على باطن القدم ولا عقبه وجوانبه وساقه ولا يسن تكراره وسننه مد الأصابع مفرجة يبدأ من رؤس أصابع القدم إلى الساق لأن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مر برجل يتوضأ وهو يغسل خفيه فنخسه بيده وقال إنما أمرنا بالمسح هكذا وأراه من مقدم الخفين إلى أصل الساق مرة وفرج بين أصابعه فإن بدأ من الساق أو مسح عرضاً خالف السنة
The obligatory (amount) of the wipe is the measure of three fingers from the smallest finger of the hand, and the most correct (view) is because it is the tool of wiping, and three is the most of it, and upon that the Sunnah came. If its measure becomes wet, even by a cloth or by pouring, it is permissible. The word 'finger' is both masculine and feminine. The place of wiping is on the outer (top) of the front of each foot once; it is not valid on the sole, nor on the heel, nor the sides, nor the leg. Its repetition is not sunnah. Its sunnah is to spread the fingers apart, starting from the tips of the toes to the shin, because the Messenger of Allah passed by a man performing wudu who was washing his two khuffs, and he poked him with his hand and said, 'We were commanded to wipe like this,' and he showed him from the front of the two khuffs to the base of the shin once, and he separated his fingers. If he starts from the shin or wipes widthwise, he opposes the sunnah.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage from the matn explains the obligatory amount of the wipe on the khuff: three fingers from the smallest finger of the hand. The correct view is that this is the minimum obligatory amount. The wipe must be done on the top front of each foot once. It cannot be on the sole, heel, sides, or leg. Repeating the wipe is not sunnah. The sunnah method is to spread the fingers apart, starting from the toes upward to the shin (below the ankle), as demonstrated by the Prophet (saw) when he poked a man washing his khuffs and showed him the correct way. Doing otherwise, like starting from the shin or wiping crosswise, violates the sunnah.

Key Terms
فرض المسح (farḍ al-mash): The obligatory amount of the wipe, which is the measure of three fingers from the smallest finger.
محل المسح (maḥall al-mash): The place of wiping: the top front portion of each foot, not the sole, heel, sides, or leg.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Method and Sunnah of Wiping over Khuffs
Explanation of the sunnah method for wiping over khuffs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for wiping over khuffs, identify the sunnah acts, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i/Maliki view.

Core Idea
One wipe on the upper front of the khuff is fard; spreading the fingers is sunnah; the bottom is not wiped in Hanafi fiqh.

This lesson explains the correct method for wiping over khuffs (leather socks) during wudu. We will learn the obligatory (fard) and sunnah actions, the evidence from the Prophet's practice, and how the Hanafi school differs from others on wiping the sole of the khuff.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that wiping over khuffs is a substitute for washing the feet. The fard is one wipe on the outer front of each foot, from toes to shin.
The fard is minimal; sunnah adds details.
2
Locate the dalil
The passage cites a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) corrected a man washing his khuffs, showing the method of wiping.
Hadith is from al-Tabarani, considered ahad with zanni thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action and statement 'We have been commanded to wipe like this' establish that wiping, not washing, is the sunnah, and the demonstration indicates the method (upper front only).
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub (the command implies obligation).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (Maliki, Shafi'i, Zahiri) recommend wiping both top and bottom; the Hanafi school restricts to the top only, unless the sole is impure.
Imam Ali's quote: 'If religion were by opinion, the bottom would be more deserving.'
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is based on the apparent act of the Prophet and the principle that tashabbuh (likeness to revelation) overrides qiyas. The mufta bihi is one wipe on the upper front.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah from the six books.

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal commentary on the method and sunnah of wiping over khuffs during wudu. It begins by stating that when the khuff becomes wet, wiping is sufficient. The author clarifies that the word 'finger' (isba') is used in both masculine and feminine forms. The obligatory (fard) wiping is once on the outer part of the front of each foot; wiping on the sole, heel, sides, or shin is not valid. Repeating the wipe is not sunnah. The sunnah acts include spreading the fingers and starting from the toes up to the shin. The hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) is cited: he saw a man washing his khuffs and corrected him by showing that the command is to wipe, not wash. The commentary then addresses various details: if the khuff is made of material that absorbs water, wiping is valid even if the water penetrates; the permissibility of wiping on the upper part only is a distinct Hanafi position, while other schools like Maliki and Shafi'i recommend wiping both top and bottom unless the bottom is impure. A condition is mentioned: the khuff must be on the foot; if part of the khuff is empty, wiping there is invalid. The famous statement of Imam Ali is quoted: 'If religion were by opinion, the bottom of the khuff would be more deserving,' emphasizing that legal rulings are based on revelation, not human reasoning. Imam Abu Hanifa's hypothetical opinions about urination and mani illustrate the danger of relying solely on analogy. The passage concludes with a discussion of the hadith's authenticity, noting a variant narration where the Prophet kicked the man with his foot.

Key Terms
مسح (mash): Wiping the hand over the khuff as a substitute for washing the feet in wudu.
خف (khuff): Leather sock worn over the foot, which may be wiped instead of washing when worn in a state of purity.
سنة (sunnah): Here, the recommended method of wiping; not obligatory but following the Prophet's practice.

Four Nullifiers of Wiping over Khuffs
Enumeration and detailed explanation of the four nullifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and explain the four nullifiers of wiping over khuffs, and apply them to determine when wiping is invalidated.

Core Idea
Wiping over khuffs is nullified by four things: wudu-breaker, removal, water entry, and time expiry.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession that substitutes washing the feet in wudu. But this concession is not absolute; it can be nullified by four specific events or conditions. Understanding these nullifiers is essential for maintaining valid purification and avoiding invalid prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four nullifiers
List the four things that nullify the wiping: 1) anything that breaks wudu, 2) removing the khuff (or most of the foot exiting), 3) water entering and wetting most of the foot, 4) expiry of the time limit (1 day for resident, 3 for traveler).
The first nullifier is logical: wiping is a substitute, so when the original purification is broken, the substitute follows.
2
Understand the principle behind removal
When the khuff is removed, the previous state of hadath (impurity) transmits to the foot, making washing necessary. If one khuff is removed, the other must also be removed and both feet washed.
Partial removal: if most of the foot exits, it counts as removal.
3
Analyze the dispute on water entry
This nullifier is based on the view that wiping is a concession of ease (rukhsat tafrih), meaning the original washing is still valid. On the opposing view (rukhsat isqat), water entry does not nullify wiping because the foot remains pure under the khuff.
The majority of later Hanafis favor the first view.
4
Grasp the nature of time expiry
Time expiry is not an action but a legal limit. The nullification is metaphorical; the actual nullifier is the hadath that was suspended and reappears when the time ends.
If the period expires during prayer, the prayer is invalidated and tayammum may be required.
5
Apply the nullifiers to scenarios
Given a scenario, decide whether wiping is nullified and what the person must do. Consider which nullifier applies and any differences of opinion if relevant.
Use the relied-upon (mufta bihi) positions for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينقض مسح الخف) أحد (أربعة أشياء) أولها (كل شيء ينقض الوضوء) لأنه بدل فينقضه ناقض الأصل وقد علمته (و) الثاني (نزع خف) لسراية الحدث السابق إلى القدم وهو الناقض في الحقيقة، وإضافة النقض إلى النزع مجاز وينزع خف يلزم قلع الآخر لسراية الحدث ولزوم غسلهما (ولو) كان النزع (بخروج أكثر القدم إلى ساق الخف) في الصحيح لمفارقة محل المسح مكانه وللأكثر حكم الكل في الصحيح (و) الثالث (إصابة الماء أكثر إحدى القدمين في الخف على الصحيح كما لو ابتل جميع القدم فيجب قلع الخف وغسلهما تحرزاً عن الجمع بين الغسل والمسح ولو تكلف فغسل رجليه من غير نزع الخف أجزأه عن الغسل فلا تبطل طهارته بانقضاء المدة (و) الرابع (مضي المدة) للمقيم والمسافر وإضافة النقض مجاز هنا والناقض حقيقة الحدث السابق بظهوره الآن فإن تمت، وهو في الصلاة بطلت ويتيمم لفقد الماء (إن لم يخف ذهاب رجله) أو قوله: (مجاز) لغوي، أو عقلي من الإسناد إلى السبب قوله : (ولزوم غسلهما) أي الرجلين المعلومين من المقام، وهو عطف على السراية قوله : ( بخروج أكثر القدم القدم ما يطأ عليه الإنسان من الرسغ إلى ما دونه وعبر أولا بالنزع ثم بالخروج للإشعار بعدم الفرق بين خروجه بنفسه وبين الإخراج كما في التبيين وعن محمد : إن بقي من القدم في الخف ما يجوز المسح عليه لا ينتقض وإلا إنتقض قال في الكافي وعليه أكثر المشايخ ونحوه في شرح العلامة مسكين وفي البحر عن النصاب وهو الصحيح، وفي الكافي وإن كان صدر القدم في موضعه، والعقب يخرج، ويدخل لم يبطل مسحه . قوله : (في الصحيح مقابله رواية محمد المسابقة وقد علمت تصحيحها . قوله : ( والثالث إصابة الماء أكثر إحدى القدمين في الخف) هذا بناء على أن المسح رخصة ترفيه تكون العزيمة معها مشروعة وجرى عليه الزيلعي ونقله عن عامة الكتب وقواه البرهان الحلبي والفاضل نوح أفندي في حواشي الدرر ، وأما على القول بأنه رخصة إسقاط فلا ينتقض المسح ولا يعتبر ذلك غسلاً لأن استتار القدم بالخف يمنع سراية الحدث إلى الرجل بالإجماع فتبقى الرجل على طهارتها، ويحل الحدث بالخف، ويزول بالمسح فلا يقع هذا الغسل معتبراً لكونه لم يزل به حدث لكونه في غير محله حتى لو نزع خفه ، أو تمت المدة وهو غير محدث لزمه غسل رجليه ثانياً . قال في السراج وهو الأظهر وإليه جنح الكمال : والحاصل أن في هذا الفرع إختلافاً، ولذا لم يعدوه في المتون من النواقض قوله : (ولو تكلف الخ) مما يجري على الخلاف السابق. قوله : (بإنقضاء المدة) أي التي أولها الحدث الذي قبل هذا الغسل بعد اللبس على وضوء تام وتعتبر المدة من حدث بعد هذا الغسل فتدبر . قوله : (الحدث السابق بظهوره الآن لأن الشارع جعل إرتفاعه مقيداً بمدة فإذا تمت حل كما في التيمم أفاده في النهر . قوله : (بطلت ويتيمم) قال الزيلعي : هو الأشبه وقيل : يمضي على صلاته قال في السراج وهو الأصح لأنه لو قطعها وهو عاجز عن غسل رجليه يتيمم، ولاحظ للرجلين في التيمم لكن يلزم على هذا أداء الصلاة بوضوء غير تام لسراية الحدث إلى القدمين حينئذ لأن . عدم سراية الحدث، ولا يجوز أداء الصلاة إلا بتيمم عند فقد الماء كما لو بقي في أعضائه لمعة، ولم الماء لا يمنع
And the wiping of the khuff is nullified by one of four things: first, anything that nullifies wudu, because it is a substitute, so the nullifier of the original nullifies it, as you have known. Second, removing the khuff, due to the transmission of the previous hadath to the foot, which is the actual nullifier, and adding the nullification to the removal is metaphorical. If one khuff is removed, the other must also be removed due to the transmission of hadath and the obligation to wash both. If the removal is by the exit of most of the foot to the shin of the khuff, in the sahih position, because the place of wiping is separated from its place, and the majority has the ruling of the whole in the sahih. Third, water reaching more than half of one foot inside the khuff, in the sahih, as if the entire foot becomes wet. Then it is obligatory to remove the khuff and wash both feet to avoid combining washing and wiping. If he forces himself and washes his feet without removing the khuff, it suffices for washing, so his purification is not invalidated by the expiry of the period. Fourth, the expiry of the period for the resident and the traveler. Adding nullification here is metaphorical; the actual nullifier is the previous hadath appearing now. If it is completed and he is in prayer, the prayer is invalidated and he performs tayammum due to lack of water, if he does not fear losing his foot. Or his statement: ('metaphorical') linguistically or rationally as attribution to the cause. His statement: ('and the obligation to wash both') i.e., the two feet known from the context, and it is coordinate to the transmission. His statement: ('by the exit of most of the foot') the foot is what a person treads on from the ankle to below. He first expressed 'removal' then 'exit' to indicate no difference between exiting by itself and being taken out, as in al-Tabyin. From Muhammad: If there remains in the khuff what is permissible to wipe, it is not nullified; otherwise it is nullified. He said in al-Kafi: upon it are most of the mashayikh, and similar in Sharh al-Allamah Miskin, and in al-Bahr from al-Nisab: it is the sahih. In al-Kafi: If the forefront of the foot is in its place and the heel emerges and enters, his wiping is not invalidated. His statement: ('in the sahih') its opposite is the narration of Muhammad al-Musabaqah, and you have known its correction. His statement: ('and the third: water reaching more than half of one foot in the khuff') this is based on the view that wiping is a concession of ease (rukhsat tafrih) where the original ruling is still permitted. Al-Zayla'i followed this and transmitted it from most books, and al-Burhan al-Halabi and al-Fadil Nuh Afandi in Hawashi al-Durar strengthened it. But on the view that it is a concession of abrogation (rukhsat isqat), the wiping is not nullified and that is not considered washing because the concealment of the foot by the khuff prevents the transmission of hadath to the foot by consensus, so the foot remains in its purification, and the hadath is attached to the khuff and is removed by wiping. So this washing is not considered because it did not remove a hadath, being in an improper place. Even if he removes his khuff or the period expires while he is not in a state of hadath, he must wash his feet again. He said in al-Siraj: it is the more apparent, and al-Kamal inclined to it. In short, there is a difference of opinion on this branch, which is why they did not count it among the nullifiers in the matn. His statement: ('and if he forces himself') etc. follows the previous difference. His statement: ('by the expiry of the period') i.e., whose beginning is the hadath before this washing after wearing on complete wudu, and the period is considered from the hadath after this washing, so ponder. His statement: ('the previous hadath appearing now' because the Lawgiver made its removal restricted to a period, so when it is completed, it is allowed as in tayammum, as benefited from al-Nahr. His statement: ('it is invalidated and he does tayammum) al-Zayla'i said: it is the more appropriate. It was said: he continues his prayer. He said in al-Siraj: it is the most correct because if he cuts it while unable to wash his feet, he does tayammum, and there is no share for the feet in tayammum, but this necessitates performing the prayer with incomplete wudu due to the transmission of hadath to the feet then, because... the absence of transmission of hadath, and it is not permissible to perform the prayer except with tayammum when water is absent, as if there remained on his limbs a spot, and water does not prevent.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage details the four nullifiers of wiping over khuffs. First, anything that breaks wudu also nullifies the wiping because wiping is a substitute for washing; if the original purification is broken, the substitute follows. Second, removing the khuff (even partially, if most of the foot emerges) nullifies the wiping, and both feet must be washed. The key is the transmission of the state of hadath to the foot once the khuff is removed. Third, if water enters the khuff and wets more than half of one foot, the wiping is nullified. This is based on the view that wiping is a 'concession of ease' (rukhsat tafrih), meaning the original ruling of washing remains valid alongside the license. If the water entry occurs, the washing is actual and the wiping ceases. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars (like al-Kamal) consider wiping a 'concession of abrogation' (rukhsat isqat), meaning the washing is no longer required; on this view, water entry does not nullify the wiping because the foot remains pure due to the barrier of the khuff. The author notes that most later scholars (mutakhkhirin) favor the former view. Fourth, the expiry of the time limit for wiping: one day for residents, three days for travelers. The nullification is metaphorical; the actual nullifier is the hadath that was suspended and now reappears. If the period expires during prayer, the prayer is invalidated and one must perform tayammum if water is unavailable. The commentary also discusses the definition of the foot (from ankle to toes), the effect of partial exit, and the opinions of Muhammad al-Shaybani and others. The absence of this fourth nullifier in some matn texts is noted due to the difference of opinion.

Key Terms
نقض (naqd): Nullification or invalidation of the legal ruling of wiping, meaning that the substitute (wiping) ceases to be effective and the original washing becomes necessary.
سراية الحدث (sirayat al-hadath): The transmission of the state of ritual impurity from the khuff to the foot when the khuff is removed or the barrier is broken.
رخصة (rukhsah): A legal concession that permits an exceptional ruling under certain conditions, here the permission to wipe instead of wash.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the four nullifiers of wiping over khuffs according to this passage?
A) Removing the khuff
B) Washing the feet with water while wearing the khuff
C) The expiry of one day for a resident
D) Sleeping

Key Takeaway
The four nullifiers of khuff wiping are: wudu-breaker, removal, water entry (in the majority view), and time expiry; understanding these ensures valid purification.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

Nullification of Wiping by Removal of Khuff: The Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Explains the first nullifier of wiping over khuffs with a critical refinement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nullification of wiping upon removal of the khuff, identify the condition of most of the foot emerging, and distinguish the mufta bihi position from alternative views.

Core Idea
Removal of the khuff nullifies wiping only when most of the foot emerges, per the relied-upon view.

Wiping over khuffs is a concession that allows one to combine purification without washing the feet. However, once the khuff is removed, the concession may be nullified. This lesson unpacks the precise condition for nullification: the emergence of most of the foot, as clarified by later Hanafi scholars. We will also explore an important intra-Hanafi difference of opinion that refines the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Default Ruling
State the act: wiping over khuffs (al-mash ala al-khuffayn). Its default condition is that it remains valid as long as the khuff is intact and not removed. Removal triggers a potential nullification.
The nullification is not due to the removal itself but because the hadath (ritual impurity) now reaches the foot.
2
Understand the Condition for Nullification
The matn states that removal of one khuff necessitates removing the other and washing both feet. The commentary specifies that this occurs 'by the exit of most of the foot up to the shaft of the khuff.' This is the relied-upon condition: most of the foot (al-akthar) must emerge.
The foot is defined from the ankle downwards (al-qadam ma yata'u 'alayhi al-insan min al-rusgh ila ma dunahu).
3
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Muhammad ibn al-Hasan holds that nullification depends on whether enough of the foot remains inside to permit wiping (about three fingers' width). If enough remains, wiping remains valid; otherwise it is nullified. The majority of later mashayikh adopt Muhammad's view.
This is a refinement from the Zahir al-Riwayah position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) which considered any removal with most of the foot emerging as nullifying, without the exception for partial remaining.
4
Determine the Mufta Bihi Position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that if most of the foot emerges, wiping is nullified; if most remains (i.e., at least the part that allows wiping remains inside), it is not nullified. This is confirmed by al-Kafi, al-Bahr, and al-Nisab.
This position gives more flexibility and is considered the correct view in later Hanafi fatwa.
5
Apply to the Heel-Only Emergence Scenario
A specific scenario: if only the heel emerges but the front part of the foot remains in place, the wiping is not nullified. This is consistent with Muhammad's view because enough of the foot remains for valid wiping.
This illustrates the practical application of the refined condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينزع خف يلزم قلع الآخر لسراية الحدث ولزوم غسلهما (ولو) كان النزع (بخروج أكثر القدم إلى ساق الخف) في الصحيح لمفارقة محل المسح مكانه وللأكثر حكم الكل في الصحيح قوله: (مجاز) لغوي، أو عقلي من الإسناد إلى السبب قوله : (ولزوم غسلهما) أي الرجلين المعلومين من المقام، وهو عطف على السراية قوله : ( بخروج أكثر القدم القدم ما يطأ عليه الإنسان من الرسغ إلى ما دونه وعبر أولا بالنزع ثم بالخروج للإشعار بعدم الفرق بين خروجه بنفسه وبين الإخراج كما في التبيين وعن محمد : إن بقي من القدم في الخف ما يجوز المسح عليه لا ينتقض وإلا إنتقض قال في الكافي وعليه أكثر المشايخ ونحوه في شرح العلامة مسكين وفي البحر عن النصاب وهو الصحيح، وفي الكافي وإن كان صدر القدم في موضعه، والعقب يخرج، ويدخل لم يبطل مسحه .
And if one removes a khuff, it necessitates removing the other because of the transmission of the hadath and the obligation to wash both feet, even if the removal (occurs) by the exit of most of the foot up to the shaft of the khuff, according to the correct view, because the place of wiping has been left, and what is most has the ruling of the whole, according to the correct view. His statement: '(metaphor)' is linguistic or rational, attributing to the cause. His statement: 'and the obligation to wash both feet' means the two feet known from the context, and it is coordinated with 'transmission'. His statement: 'by the exit of most of the foot' – the foot is what one steps on from the ankle downwards. He first expressed it as removal then as exit to indicate no difference between exiting by itself or by extraction, as in al-Tabyin. And from Muhammad: if there remains in the khuff of the foot what makes wiping permissible, it is not nullified; otherwise it is nullified. He said in al-Kafi: upon this are most mashayikh, and similar in Sharh al-Allama Miskin, and in al-Bahr from al-Nisab, and it is the correct view. And in al-Kafi: if the front part of the foot is in its place and the heel comes out and enters, his wiping is not nullified.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from the Hashiya discusses the first nullifier of wiping over khuffs: the removal of the khuff causing most of the foot to emerge. The matn states that removing one khuff necessitates removing the other and washing both feet, because the hadath (ritual impurity) that was confined by the wiping now spreads to the feet. The commentary explains key points: the word 'majāz' (metaphor) refers to the attribution of nullification to the removal, which is metaphorical; the actual nullifier is the underlying hadath. The definition of 'qadam' (foot) is given as from the ankle downwards. It clarifies that there is no difference between the foot coming out by itself or being pulled out. It then presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani holds that as long as enough of the foot remains inside to permit wiping (i.e., an amount equal to the minimum for wiping, which is three fingers), the wiping is not nullified. If what remains is less than that, it is nullified. The majority of later scholars (mashayikh) adopt Muhammad's view, as reported in al-Kafi, al-Bahr, and other works. Another scenario: if the front part of the foot remains in place and only the heel emerges and re-enters, the wiping remains valid. This lesson is a critical refinement of the ruling from the matn, clarifying the extent of emergence that nullifies wiping according to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
نزع الخف (naza' al-khuff): Removal of the leather sock (khuff) worn over the foot for wiping.
القدم (al-qadam): The foot from the ankle (rusgh) downwards, including the heel and toes.
سراية الحدث (sarayat al-hadath): The transmission of ritual impurity from the khuff to the foot once the foot is exposed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what happens if most of the foot remains inside the khuff after removing it?
A) The wiping is nullified because the khuff was removed.
B) The wiping remains valid.
C) It is recommended to remove the other khuff too.
D) The wudu becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The nullification of wiping upon removal of a khuff depends on the emergence of most of the foot; if most remains, the wiping continues, in accordance with the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Does Water Under the Khuff Nullify Wiping?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on a nullifier of khuff wiping

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on water reaching the foot under the khuff and explain why the isqat view is considered more apparent.

Core Idea
Water reaching the foot does not nullify wiping if wiping is a concession that abrogates washing.

You may have heard that if water gets inside your khuff, you must remove it and wash your feet. But is that always true? The Hanafi school has a well-known dispute on this point, rooted in how we understand the concession (rukhsah) for wiping over khuffs. This lesson unpacks the two views and shows why many later scholars prefer the position that wiping remains valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
The matn gives one view: water reaching most of the foot nullifies wiping (tafrih view). The commentary introduces another view: it does not nullify (isqat view). Identify which is presented as 'as-sahih' and which as 'azhar'.
2
Understand the basis: nature of rukhsah
The tafrih view treats wiping as a concession that does not abrogate the original duty (washing), so washing remains valid. The isqat view treats wiping as a full replacement, so washing under the khuff is not considered a valid act of purification.
The term 'rukhsat tafrih' vs 'rukhsat isqat' is key.
3
Trace the hadath and the role of the khuff
On the isqat view, hadath attaches to the khuff, not the foot. The khuff prevents transmission of hadath to the foot by consensus. Thus, water on the foot does not affect the hadath, and wiping remains valid. On the tafrih view, the hadath is on the foot, so washing is still needed.
This consensus (ijma') on the khuff preventing transmission is a strong proof.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
If you follow the tafrih view, you must remove the khuff and wash if water gets in. If you follow the isqat view, you may continue without any action. This affects daily practice, especially for those wearing khuffs for extended periods.
Many texts omit this from the list of nullifiers due to the ikhtilaf.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
Al-Siraj and al-Kamal considered the isqat view 'azhar' (more apparent). However, the matn labels the tafrih view as 'as-sahih'. The issue remains unresolved, and fatwa may vary. Be aware of both views.
The commentary says 'wa huwa al-azhar' – a signal of preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) الثالث (إصابة الماء أكثر إحدى القدمين في الخف على الصحيح كما لو ابتل جميع القدم فيجب قلع الخف وغسلهما تحرزاً عن الجمع بين الغسل والمسح ولو تكلف فغسل رجليه من غير نزع الخف أجزأه عن الغسل فلا تبطل طهارته بانقضاء المدة قوله : (والثالث إصابة الماء أكثر إحدى القدمين في الخف) هذا بناء على أن المسح رخصة ترفيه تكون العزيمة معها مشروعة وجرى عليه الزيلعي ونقله عن عامة الكتب وقواه البرهان الحلبي والفاضل نوح أفندي في حواشي الدرر ، وأما على القول بأنه رخصة إسقاط فلا ينتقض المسح ولا يعتبر ذلك غسلاً لأن استتار القدم بالخف يمنع سراية الحدث إلى الرجل بالإجماع فتبقى الرجل على طهارتها، ويحل الحدث بالخف، ويزول بالمسح فلا يقع هذا الغسل معتبراً لكونه لم يزل به حدث لكونه في غير محله حتى لو نزع خفه ، أو تمت المدة وهو غير محدث لزمه غسل رجليه ثانياً . قال في السراج وهو الأظهر وإليه جنح الكمال : والحاصل أن في هذا الفرع إختلافاً، ولذا لم يعدوه في المتون من النواقض قوله : (ولو تكلف الخ) مما يجري على الخلاف السابق.
And the third (nullifier) is the water reaching most of one of the feet in the khuff, according to the correct view, just as if the entire foot gets wet; then it is obligatory to remove the khuff and wash both feet, as a precaution against combining washing and wiping. And if one takes the trouble and washes his feet without removing the khuff, it suffices him for the washing, so his purification is not nullified by the expiration of the period. His statement: 'And the third is water reaching most of one of the feet in the khuff' – this is based on the view that wiping is a concession for ease (rukhsat tafrih), with which the original ruling (washing) remains permissible. Al-Zayla'i followed this and transmitted it from most books, and it was strengthened by Burhan al-Halabi and Fadil Nuh Afandi in the margins of al-Durar. As for the view that it is a concession of abrogation (rukhsat isqat), then wiping is not nullified and that water is not considered a washing, because the covering of the foot by the khuff prevents the transmission of hadath to the foot by consensus, so the foot remains in its state of purity, and the hadath attaches to the khuff and is removed by wiping. Thus this washing is not considered because it did not remove a hadath, being out of its place, such that if he removes his khuff or the period expires while he is not in a state of hadath, he must wash his feet a second time. He said in al-Siraj: it is the more apparent, and al-Kamal inclined to it. The summary: there is disagreement on this issue, and therefore they did not count it among the nullifiers in the texts. His statement: 'and if one takes the trouble, etc.' flows from the preceding disagreement.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage discusses the third nullifier (in the matn's enumeration): water reaching most of one foot inside the khuff. The matn initially states it as a nullifier according to the correct view, requiring removal and washing. However, the commentary reveals a significant ikhtilaf based on the nature of the concession (rukhsah) for wiping over khuffs. There are two views: (1) Rukhsat tafrih (concession for ease): wiping is a lighter alternative but the original duty (washing) remains valid and can be performed. On this view, if water reaches the foot, one should remove the khuff and wash because the washing is still possible and combining washing and wiping should be avoided. (2) Rukhsat isqat (concession of abrogation): wiping replaces washing entirely, so if water reaches the foot while the khuff is on, it is not considered a valid washing because the foot is still covered and the hadath is on the khuff. Therefore, the wiping remains valid, and the water contact has no effect. If one later removes the khuff or the period expires while not in a state of hadath, the foot is considered pure and must be washed again. The commentary notes that al-Siraj considers the second view (that it does not nullify) more apparent, and al-Kamal inclined to it. Due to this disagreement, many matns (texts) do not list this as a nullifier. This lesson is a critical refinement showing that the ruling is not settled, and the student should be aware of the ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
رخصة ترفيه (rukhsat tafrih): A concession that provides ease, but the original duty remains permissible and can be performed alongside the concession.
رخصة إسقاط (rukhsat isqat): A concession that abrogates the original duty; the original becomes invalid when the concession is used.
الحدث (al-hadath): Ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, specifically the hadath that is 'suspended' on the khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which view is described as 'azhar' (more apparent) by al-Siraj?
A) The tafrih view (water nullifies).
B) The isqat view (water does not nullify).
C) The view that one must remove the khuff immediately.
D) The view that water is always considered a nullifier.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on water reaching the foot under the khuff is disputed within the Hanafi school; the isqat view that it does not nullify wiping is considered more apparent by later authorities.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Wiping Over Headgear and Gloves is Invalid
Ruling that wiping is not valid on turbans, caps, face veils, or gloves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over headgear and gloves, and identify the exception for the turban when moisture reaches the head.

Core Idea
Wiping over any headgear or gloves is invalid; the concession of wiping is exclusive to khuffs.

In wudu, wiping a quarter of the head is obligatory. However, many Muslims cover their heads with turbans, caps, or veils. This lesson clarifies that simply wiping over such coverings does not fulfill the obligation, unless the water penetrates to the skin. The same applies to gloves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the items prohibited for wiping
List the four items mentioned: turban (عمامة), cap (قلنسوة), face veil (برقع), and gloves (قفازين). Note that each is a covering that prevents water from reaching the skin.
These are not khuffs, which are the only exception in wudu.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The ruling of wiping (maskh) is an exception to the base rule of washing, established only for khuffs by textual proof. It cannot be extended by analogy to other coverings.
Qiyas ma'a al-fariq: the difference is that khuffs are specifically mentioned in the Sunnah.
3
Recognize the exception for the turban
Wiping over a turban is valid if moisture from the hand penetrates to the head and covers at least a quarter of it. This is how the hadith of the Prophet wiping his turban is interpreted.
The moisture must reach the skin; simply wetting the turban is insufficient.
4
Note the definitions and scope
The text defines each item: gloves are stuffed with cotton, caps are head coverings, veils have eye holes. The ruling covers all similar coverings.
The exception does not apply to caps or veils because they are not typically removed during wudu and moisture usually doesn't penetrate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( لا يجوز أي لا يصح المسح على عمامة وقلنسوة وبرقع وقفازين) لأن المسح ثبت بخلاف القياس فلا يلحق به غيره والقفاز بالضم والتشديد يعمل لليدين محشواً بقطن له أزرار يزر على الساعدين من البرد تلبسه النساء ويتخذه الصياد من جلد اتقاء مخالب الصقر والقلنسوة بفتح القاف وضم السين المهملة مكان المجوزة والبرقع بضم الباء الموحدة وسكون الراء المهلمة وضم القاف وفتحها خرقة تنقب للعينين تلبسها الدواب ونساء الأعراب على وجوههن. قوله : (أي) لا يصح) دفع به ما يتوهم أنه يصح مع الحرمة . قوله : (المسح على عمامة) إلا إذا نفذت البلة منها إلى الرأس وأصابت مقدار الفرض وعليه حمل ما ورد أنه مسح على عمامته كما في السراج . قوله : ( وقفازين) ويتصور مسحهما بأن يأمر غيره به وهو لا يجوز. قوله : (مكان المجوزة) وفي شرح السيد هي ما تلف عليه العمامة كطربوش، وطاقية ولعل مراد الشرح بالمجوزة ما يسمى بالمقلة التي يلبسها أهل الفضل قوله : ونساء الأعراب) الأولى ما تستر به المرأة وجهها فإنه لا يخص نساء الأعراب، ولعله إنما خص نساء الأعراب لكونهن اللاتي ابتدأن لبسه ويجعل للدواب إتقاء للذباب .
(It is not permissible, i.e., it is not valid to wipe over a turban, a cap (qalansuwah), a face veil (burqa'), and gloves (qafazain), because wiping is established contrary to analogy, so nothing else is attached to it. Al-qafaz (with damm and tashdid) is made for the hands, stuffed with cotton, with buttons to button on the forearms against cold; women wear it, and the hunter uses it from leather to protect against falcon's claws. Al-qalansuwah (with fatha on qaf and damm on the important sin) is the place of the triangular cap. Al-burqa' (with damm on the single ba, sukun on the important ra', and damm and fatha on qaf) is a cloth with two holes for the eyes worn by animals and Bedouin women on their faces. His statement: 'that is, it is not valid' – it rejects the misconception that it might be valid along with prohibition. His statement: 'wiping over a turban' – unless the moisture from it penetrates to the head and reaches the amount of the obligatory (part). Upon this is based what is reported that he (the Prophet) wiped over his turban, as in al-Siraj. His statement: 'and gloves' – and it is conceivable to wipe them by commanding someone else, but it is not permissible. His statement: 'place of triangular cap' – and in the commentary of al-Sayyid, it is whatever the turban is wound around, like a tarbush or a skullcap. Perhaps the commenter meant by 'triangular cap' what is called the muqalla worn by virtuous people. His statement: 'and Bedouin women's' – the correct term is what shields the woman's face, as it is not specific to Bedouin women; but he specified Bedouin women perhaps because they were the first to wear it. And it is made for animals to protect against flies.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage states the ruling that wiping over a turban ('imamah'), a cap (qalansuwah), a face veil (burqa'), and gloves (qafazain) is not valid. The reason given is that the ruling of wiping (i.e., substituting wiping for washing) is established only for khuffs due to textual evidence and by way of exception to the general analogy that requires washing. Therefore, it cannot be extended to other coverings. The commentary then defines each item: al-qafaz are gloves stuffed with cotton used by women and hunters; al-qalansuwah is a cap around which a turban is wound; al-burqa' is a face veil worn by Bedouin women and animals. An exception is mentioned: if moisture from the turban reaches the head and covers the obligatory part of the head (i.e., a quarter of the head), then it may count as wiping the head itself, and the report that the Prophet wiped over his turban is interpreted in this light. The commentary also notes that commanding someone else to wipe over one's gloves is theoretically possible but impermissible. The passage emphasizes that the ruling is about validity (sihhah), not just permissibility; it is invalid to perform such wiping. This lesson clarifies the limits of the concession for wiping.

Key Terms
عمامة ('imamah): A turban wrapped around the head, often over a cap.
قلنسوة (qalansuwah): A cap worn under the turban or alone, typically conical or rounded.
برقع (burqa'): A face veil with openings for the eyes, worn by Bedouin women or placed on animals.
قفاز (qafaz): Gloves stuffed with cotton, buttoned on the forearms.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on wiping over a cap (qalansuwah) during wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Valid if the cap is thin.
B) Invalid, because wiping over headgear other than khuffs is not allowed.
C) Valid for men but not women.
D) Valid only if the cap is made of leather.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over any headgear or gloves is invalid; only if moisture reaches the skin can it count, and that exception applies solely to the turban.

Introduction to the Jabirah (Splint) in the Hanafi School
Beginning the section on rulings for medical splints and bandages

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define the term jabirah, identify its types, and state the condition that it must be applied on a place of necessity.

Core Idea
A jabirah is any medical covering placed on a wound for necessity; its use permits wiping over it in wudu.

In this lesson, we begin the chapter on the jabirah (splint). The opening sentence defines what a jabirah is and gives examples of materials that may be used. Understanding this definition is crucial because the legal rulings for wudu and ghusl depend on whether a covering qualifies as a jabirah applied for necessity. We will unpack the definition and its conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal term
Note that the passage introduces a 'fasl' on 'jabirah'. This is the technical term for a splint or bandage used in purification rulings.
2
Recognize the defining characteristic
The text states 'كل ما يوضع على موضع الضرورة' – everything placed on a place of necessity. This is the core defining feature: the jabirah must be applied due to a medical need.
3
List the examples
The text gives four examples: cloth (khirqah), glue (ʿilk), medicine (dawa'), and a piece of gall bladder (jildat mararah). These illustrate that many materials can qualify, as long as they serve the purpose of healing.
4
Note the pending conditions
The phrase 'بشرطه' (subject to its conditions) signals that further requirements will be detailed later, such as that the covering cannot be removed without harm.
5
Connect to purification rulings
The relevance of this definition is that if a wound covering qualifies as a jabirah, then during wudu or ghusl one may wipe over it instead of washing the injured area. This is a key dispensation (rukhsah) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الجبيرة ونوعها من كل ما يوضع على موضع الضرورة كخرقة وعلك ودواء وجلدة مرارة بشرطه
Chapter on the splint (jabirah) and its types: everything that is placed on a place of necessity, such as a cloth, glue, medicine, and a piece of gall bladder, subject to its conditions.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This brief passage introduces the chapter (fasl) on jabirah (splint or bandage). It defines the jabirah as any material placed on a wound, fracture, or other area of necessity for healing. Examples include a simple cloth (khirqah), gum/glue (ʿilk), medicinal substances (dawa'), and even a piece of animal gall bladder (jildat mararah). The ruling (to be detailed in the following pages) will be subject to conditions (bi-shartih). As this is only the opening sentence, the lesson serves as an anchor for the upcoming rulings. In the Hanafi school, jabirah rulings concern whether one may wipe over such coverings during wudu or ghusl when removing them would cause harm. This lesson provides the definition and anticipates the conditions.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabirah): A splint or bandage placed on a wound or fracture to keep it stable and protected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an example of a jabirah as defined in this passage?
A) A wristwatch
B) A cloth bandage on a broken arm
C) A decorative ring
D) A sock

Key Takeaway
The jabirah is defined as any material placed on a wound for necessity; its use in wudu is a dispensation conditioned on the covering being necessary and not removable without harm.
