The Prohibition of Wiping Over Headgear and the Effect of Nullifiers on Khuff Wipe
Explanation of nullifiers and prohibition of wiping over headgear

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over non-khuff coverings and explain the rational proof (dalil aqli) that prohibits extending the concession to other items.

Core Idea
The wipe over khuffs is a concession outside analogy; it cannot be extended to turbans, caps, veils, or gloves.

In this passage, the author clarifies two connected issues: the effect of three nullifiers (removing the khuff, wetting most of the foot, and expiry of the period) on the validity of the khuff wipe, and the absolute prohibition of wiping over any headgear or hand cover. The core legal reasoning is that the permission to wipe over khuffs is a deviation from the normal qiyas (qiyās) of washing the feet; therefore, it is a restricted concession that cannot be analogically applied to other coverings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three nullifiers of the khuff wipe
The passage states that after removing the khuff, wetting most of the foot, or the expiry of the period, the wipe is invalidated. You must be able to list these three events.
The nullifiers are specific to the khuff wipe, not general nullifiers of wudu.
2
Determine the consequence of the nullifiers
After any of these three events, only the feet need to be washed; the rest of the wudu remains intact if it was performed before. This is because the previous hadath (impurity) was only on the feet.
This is a specific ruling that applies only to the khuff wipe scenario.
3
State the prohibition of wiping over other items
The author explicitly states that it is not permissible (lā yajūz) to wipe over a turban (ʿimāma), cap (qalansuwa), face veil (burquʿ), or gloves (quffāzayn). The ruling is one of invalidity (lā yaṣiḥḥ).
The prohibition covers any covering that is not a khuff (or, by extension, a similar foot covering like a sock in some cases).
4
Understand the rational proof (dalīl ʿaqlī)
The proof is that the permission to wipe over khuffs is thābita bi khilāf al-qiyās (established by departure from analogy). Since it is an exceptional concession, it cannot be extended to other items by qiyas. This is a principle in Hanafi uṣūl: a concession that contradicts qiyas cannot be analogically applied.
This is a rational proof, not a textual one. It relies on the nature of the ruling as an exception.
5
Apply the exception for moisture reaching the head
The commentary notes an exception: if the moisture from wiping over the turban actually penetrates to the head and covers the obligatory area (at least a quarter of the head), then it may be considered a valid wipe of the head itself, not a wipe over the turban. This explains the hadith of the Prophet wiping over his turban.
This nuance is important for interpreting reports that appear to allow wiping over a turban.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعضها أو عطبها من البرد فيجوز له المسح حتى يأمن وظاهر المتون بقاء صفة المسح وفي معراج الدراية يستوعبه بالمسح كالجبائر (وبعد الثلاثة الأخيرة) وهي نزع الخف وابتلال أكثر القدم ومضي المدة (غسل رجليه فقط وليس عليه إعادة بقية الوضوء إذا كان متوضئاً لحلول الحدث السابق بقدميه ( ولا يجوز أي لا يصح المسح على عمامة وقلنسوة وبرقع وقفازين) لأن المسح ثبت بخلاف القياس فلا يلحق به غيره والقفاز بالضم والتشديد يعمل لليدين محشواً بقطن له أزرار يزر على الساعدين من البرد تلبسه النساء ويتخذه الصياد من جلد اتقاء مخالب الصقر والقلنسوة بفتح القاف وضم السين المهملة مكان المجوزة والبرقع بضم الباء الموحدة وسكون الراء المهلمة وضم القاف وفتحها خرقة تنقب للعينين تلبسها الدواب ونساء الأعراب على وجوههن. قوله : إن لم يخف ذهاب رجله الخ) ظاهره أنه لا ينتقض المسح، وليس كذلك للزوم. مسحه كالجبيرة، ودفع هذا بأنه مرتبط بمحذوف تقديره فيجب عليه نزع خفيه، وغسل رجليه إن لم يخف الخ. قوله : ( حتى يأمن الخ) أشار به إلى عدم التوقيت بمدة . قوله : (وفي معراج الدراية هو المعوّل عليه قوله : (يستوعبه) وقيل : يكفي مسح الأكثر على الخلاف في الجبيرة قوله : (غسل رجليه فقط) وفاتته الموالاة وهي ليست بشرط في الوضوء قاله في الشرح وبقي من النواقض الخرق الكبير وخروج الوقت للمعذور قاله السيد، والخرق الكبير الحادث بعد المسح داخل في حكم النزع ، وخروج الوقت للمعذور داخل في انقضاء المدة فلذا والله أعلم لم يذكرهما المصنف. قوله : (أي) لا يصح) دفع به ما يتوهم أنه يصح مع الحرمة . قوله : (المسح على عمامة) إلا إذا نفذت البلة منها إلى الرأس وأصابت مقدار الفرض وعليه حمل ما ورد أنه مسح على عمامته كما في السراج . قوله : ( وقفازين) ويتصور مسحهما بأن يأمر غيره به وهو لا يجوز. قوله : (مكان المجوزة) وفي شرح السيد هي ما تلف عليه العمامة كطربوش، وطاقية ولعل مراد الشرح بالمجوزة ما يسمى بالمقلة التي يلبسها أهل الفضل قوله : ونساء الأعراب) الأولى ما تستر به المرأة وجهها فإنه لا يخص نساء الأعراب، ولعله إنما خص نساء الأعراب لكونهن اللاتي ابتدأن لبسه ويجعل للدواب إتقاء للذباب .
And [the ruling on] some of it or its being damaged from cold: then it is permissible for him to wipe until he is safe. And the apparent [meaning] of the texts is that the description of wiping remains. And in Miraj al-Diraya, he must cover it entirely with wiping like splints. (And after the third [thing]), which are: removing the khuff, wetting most of the foot, and the passing of the period. (He washes only his two feet, and he is not required to repeat the rest of wudu if he was in a state of wudu because the previous hadath occurred with his feet). (And it is not permissible, i.e., it is not valid, to wipe over a turban, a cap, a face veil, and gloves) because wiping is established by departing from analogy, so nothing else is joined to it. Al-qafaz (glove): with damm and tashdid, it is made for the hands, stuffed with cotton, with buttons buttoned on the forearms from cold, worn by women, and the hunter takes it from leather to protect from the claws of the falcon. Al-qalansuwah: with fatha on the qaf and damm on the sin, is the place of the mujawwazah. Al-burqu': with damm on the ba and sukun on the ra, and damm or fatha on the qaf, a cloth with a hole for the eyes, worn by animals and Bedouin women on their faces. [Then the commentary:] His saying: "If he does not fear losing his foot etc." Its apparent meaning is that the wipe is not invalidated, but it is not so because it is necessary to wipe it like a splint. And this is repelled by it being connected to an omitted phrase, the estimation being: it is obligatory upon him to remove his khuffs and wash his feet if he does not fear etc. His saying: "until he is safe" indicates the lack of a time limit. His saying: "and in Miraj al-Diraya, it is the relied-upon thing" His saying: "he covers it entirely" and it is said: the majority suffices, following the difference in splints. His saying: "he washes only his feet" and he missed the muwalat, but it is not a condition in wudu, as stated in the sharh. And among the nullifiers that remain: a large tear and the exit of time for the excused, as said by al-Sayyid. And the large tear occurring after the wipe is included in the ruling of removal, and the exit of time for the excused is included in the expiry of the period, so the author did not mention them. His saying: "i.e., it is not valid" repels what might be imagined that it is valid though sinful. His saying: "wiping over the turban" except if the moisture from it penetrates to the head and reaches the obligatory amount, and based on this is interpreted what is reported that he wiped over his turban, as in al-Siraj. His saying: "and gloves" and their wiping is conceivable by ordering someone else to do it, but it is not permissible. His saying: "place of the mujawwazah" and in the sharh of al-Sayyid: it is what the turban is wound around, like a tarbush and a taqiya, and perhaps the intention of the sharh by mujawwazah is what is called al-muqalla which the virtuous people wear. His saying: "and Bedouin women" the first is what a woman veils her face with, for it is not specific to Bedouin women, and perhaps he only specified Bedouin women because they were the ones who first wore it, and it is made for animals to protect from flies.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi deals with two issues: the effect of the three nullifiers of the wipe on the khuff (naz' al-khuff, wetting most of the foot, and expiry of the time) and the prohibition of wiping over headgear such as turbans, caps, face veils, and gloves. The author first clarifies that after the occurrence of any of these three, the wudu is not entirely invalidated; rather, only the feet need to be washed, and the rest of the wudu remains intact if it was performed before. Then, he firmly states that wiping over a turban, cap, face veil, or gloves is not valid (la yasihh). The reason given is that the permission to wipe over the khuff is an exception established contrary to analogy (thabata bikhilaf al-qiyas), meaning it is a concession that cannot be extended by analogy to other coverings. The commentary then addresses various nuances: the condition that if the moisture from the turban reaches the head and covers the obligatory area, it may be considered as wiping the head; the possibility of wiping gloves by having someone else do it, but this is also not permissible; and the definitions of the items mentioned. The author also notes that the large tear of the khuff and the exit of time for a excused person are included in the nullifiers but were not mentioned by the original author.

Key Terms
عمامة (ʿimāma): A turban, a head covering that is wound around the head.
قلنسوة (qalansuwa): A cap or hood, often worn under the turban or separately.
برقع (burquʿ): A face veil with a hole for the eyes, worn by women.
قفازين (quffāzayn): Gloves stuffed with cotton, worn for warmth or protection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it not permissible to wipe over a turban (عمامة) in wudu according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because it is not mentioned in the Quran.
B) Because the ruling of wiping over the khuff is established contrary to analogy, so it cannot be extended to other items.
C) Because the Prophet forbade it.
D) Because the turban is not a covering for the feet.

Key Takeaway
The permission to wipe over khuffs is a restricted concession that does not apply to headgear or gloves; the only exception is if moisture from the headgear reaches the head itself.

8 min
Ruling on Wiping Over Splints (Jabeera)
Definition and ruling of wiping over a splint

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a splint, identify the evidence and its epistemological weight, and explain the distinction between fard and wajib in this context.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is wajib once, not fard, because the proof is ahad and does not yield certainty.

This lesson examines the topic of wiping over splints (jabeera) for those with wounds or fractures. We will define the jabeera, state the ruling, explore the evidence, and understand the subtle distinction between fard and wajib within the Hanafi school. The passage also addresses the scope of wiping and the conditions that make this concession applicable.

Guided Path
1
Define the jabeera and its conditions
Identify what constitutes a jabeera: any material placed on a wound or break out of necessity. Note the condition: the wound cannot be washed or wiped directly without harm.
The definition includes rags, gum, medicine, etc.
2
Identify the ruling and the internal dispute
State the correct opinion (sahih) that wiping is wajib once. Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is fard, while Abu Hanifa says wajib. Understand why this distinction matters for the validity of prayer.
The dispute hinges on the epistemological weight of the evidence.
3
Examine the proof
Analyze the primary evidence: the hadith of the Prophet wiping on his bandage and ordering Ali to wipe on splints. Also note the Quranic principle of removing hardship (5:6). Recognize that the hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
The proof is used to justify the rukhsa (concession).
4
Understand the epistemological basis
Explain why Abu Hanifa holds it as wajib not fard: fard requires qat'i proof; ahad hadith gives zann, so it obliges action but does not invalidate prayer if omitted without excuse.
This is a key usul principle applied in fiqh.
5
Resolve the ikhtilaf and identify the mufta bihi
Review the positions of later scholars: al-Hidayah leans towards once; al-Tatimmah gives fatwa on the view of the two (fard) as precaution. Understand al-Razi's distinction: if the wound can be washed if exposed, wiping is fard; if not, it is not obligatory at all.
The practical fatwa often follows the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) for caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

العضو) بماء بارد ولا حار وقيل لا يجب استعمال الحار ولا يستطيع مسحه وجب المسح على الصحيح مرة واحدة في الصحيح وقيل : يكرر إلا في الرأس واستحباب رواية وقيل : فرض لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يمسح على عصابته ولما كسر زند علي رضي الله تعالى عنه يوم أحد، أو يوم خيبر أمره النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن يمسح على الجبائر ويمسح على أكثر ما شد به العضو) هو و لئلا يؤدي إلى فساد الجراحة بالاستيعاب وكفى المسح على ما ظهر من الجسد الصحيح آحاد إتفاقاً، الآتي، والجبيرة فعيلة من الجبر بمعنى الإصلاح كما في المصباح سميت بذلك تفاؤلاً كما سمي موضع الهلاك مفازة. قوله : (تلف بورق) أي مثلاً قوله: (وقيل لا يجب إستعمال الحار) جزم به في السراج دفعاً للمشقة. قال في البحر والظاهر الأول. قوله: (ولا يستطيع مسحه) قال في البدائع : إن كان المسح على عين الجراحة لا يضرّ بها لا يجوز المسح إلى على عين الجراحة، ولا يجوز المسح على الجبيرة لأن جوازه للعذر ، ولا عذر اهـ. قوله: (على الصحيح أي عن الإمام فتجوز الصلاة بدونه لأنّ الفرض إنما يثبت بدليل قطعي والمروي خبر وهو إنما يفيد العمل دون العلم فحكمنا بوجوب المسح عملاً، ولم نحكم بفساد الصلاة بتركه لغير عذر لأن الحكم بالفساد يرجع إلى العلم، وهذا الدليل لا يفيده واختاره في الفتح، وفي الشرح وعليه الإعتماد قوله: (وقيل يكرر إلا في الرأس) فإنه لا يكرر مسحه . والأولى أن يزيد الشرح لفظ مرة ليقابل قوله وقيل يكرر وإن بقي من الرأس قدر الربع مسحه، وإلا ، مسح على العصابة أفاده السيد، وقد يقال : لماذا لم يتعيّن مسح الصحيح وإن قال، ويتمم الفرض بالمسح على العصابة قوله : (وقيل) الفرض هو قولهما، وفي الإيضاح الفتوى على قولهما احتياطاً، وفي البحر وحاصله أنه اختلف التصحيح في إفتراضه ووجوبه، ولم أر من صحح إستحبابه على قوله : وفصل الرازي ، فقال : إن كان ما تحت الجبيرة لو ظهر أمكن غسله فالمسح واجب لأن الفرض متعلق بالأصل، فيتعلق بما قام مقامه كمسح الخف، وإن كان ما تحتها لو ظهر لا يمكن غسله فالمسح عليها غير واجب لأنّ فرض الأصل قد سقط، فلا يتعلق بما قام مقامه كمقطوع القدم إذا لبس الخف، وهذا يفيد أن المراد بقوله : فالمسح واجب الفرض لا الواجب المصطلح عليه .اهـ. وقال الصيرفي : هذا أحسن الأقوال اهـ وإذا علمت ما ذكر تعلم أن نسبة الوجوب إلى الصاحبين ليست على ما ينبغي قوله: (لأن النبي الخ) دليل لأصل المسح كما في الشرح قوله : (كان يمسح على عصابته ) حين رماه ابن قميئة يوم وما ورد في هذا الباب من الأخبار ضعيف يستأنس به وفي الحلبي ولا يضر ضعف الحديث بالنسبة إلينا بعد ما أجمع عليه المجتهدون رحمهم الله تعالى بالدليل الواضح، وهو قوله تعالى : ما يريد الله ليجعل عليكم من حرج) [المائدة/ ٥] .اهـ. قوله: (هو الصحيح) وفي التتمة يفتى وفي الخلاصة، وعليه الفتوى وإليه جنح صاحب الهداية واختار في الكنز الاستيعاب .
Chapter on the splint and its types. From everything placed on the place of necessity, like a rag, gum, medicine, a piece of gallbladder skin, with its condition. (If he is wounded or his limb is broken, and he binds it with a rag or a splint), it is sticks from palm branches, wrapped with leaves, and tied on the broken limb, and he cannot wash the limb with cold or hot water (and it is said that hot water is not required), and he cannot wipe it, then wiping becomes obligatory, correct opinion: once, in the correct opinion, and it is said: repeat except on the head, and a narration recommends, and a saying: it is obligatory because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم used to wipe on his bandage, and when the forearm of Ali was broken on the day of Uhud or Khaybar, the Prophet ordered him to wipe on the splints. And he wipes on most of what the limb was bound with, so as not to lead to ruining the wound by covering it all, and it suffices to wipe on what appears of the healthy body. Al-jabeera is a feminine noun from jabr meaning repair, as in al-Misbah, named so for optimism, just as a place of destruction is called mafaza. His saying: "wrapped with leaves" i.e., for example. His saying: "and it is said that hot water is not required" he decided it in al-Siraj to avoid hardship. He said in al-Bahr: and the apparent is the first. His saying: "and he cannot wipe it" he said in al-Bada'i': if wiping on the wound itself does not harm it, then he must wipe on the wound itself, and it is not permissible to wipe on the splint because its permission is due to excuse, and there is no excuse. His saying: "correct opinion" i.e., from the Imam, so prayer is valid without it because the obligation is established only by categorical proof, and the narrated report is ahad, which only necessitates action, not knowledge, so we ruled that wiping is obligatory in practice, but we do not rule that prayer is invalid for leaving it without excuse because the ruling of invalidity depends on knowledge, and this proof does not provide that. And he chose this in al-Fath, and in the sharh it is relied upon. His saying: "and it is said repeat except on the head" for he does not repeat wiping on it. And it is better that the sharh add the word 'once' to contrast with the saying 'repeat', and if there remains from the head the amount of a quarter, he wipes it, otherwise he wipes on the bandage, as stated by al-Sayyid. And it may be said: why is it not determined to wipe the healthy part and complete the obligation by wiping on the bandage? His saying: "and a saying" the obligatory is the saying of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and in al-Idah the fatwa is on their saying as a precaution. In al-Bahr: the gist is that there is a difference in declaring it fard or wajib, and I have not seen anyone declaring it recommended. And al-Razi said: if what is under the splint could be washed if exposed, then wiping is wajib because the obligation is attached to the original, so it attaches to what stands in its place like wiping the khuff. If what is under it cannot be washed if exposed, then wiping on it is not wajib because the obligation of the original has fallen, so it does not attach to what stands in its place like a person with a cut foot who wears a khuff. This indicates that by 'al-mash wajib' he means obligatory in the sense of fard, not the technical wajib. He said: al-Sayrafi said: this is the best of statements. When you know what is mentioned, you learn that attributing wujub to the two companions is not appropriate. His saying: "because the Prophet" is a proof for the principle of wiping, as in the sharh. His saying: "he used to wipe on his bandage" when Ibn Qumay'a threw him on the day of Uhud. What has been reported in this chapter are weak hadiths that are used for seeking comfort. In al-Halabi: the weakness of the hadith does not harm us after the mujtahids have agreed upon it by clear evidence, which is His saying: "Allah does not intend to make hardship for you" [5:6]. His saying: "it is the correct opinion" and in al-Tatimmah it is given for fatwa, and in al-Khulasah it is the fatwa, and the author of al-Hidayah leaned towards it, and in al-Kanz he chose covering entirely.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi introduces the chapter on al-jabeera (splint). It defines the splint as any material placed over a wound or break, such as a rag, gum, medicine, or animal skin, used when washing the limb is not possible with cold or hot water, and wiping the wound directly is also not possible. The ruling is that it is obligatory to wipe over the splint once, according to the correct view (sahih), with evidence from the Prophet's practice: he used to wipe on his bandage and ordered Ali to wipe on the splints when his forearm was broken. There is a difference of opinion on whether the wipe should be repeated, but the relied-upon position is once. The commentary clarifies that the obligation is based on a hadith which is ahad, so it obliges action but does not make the prayer invalid if omitted without excuse. The discussion also covers the extent of wiping: it should be over most of the splint, not all, to avoid harming the wound. The author presents a subtle distinction by Imam al-Razi: if the wound could be washed if uncovered, then the wipe is obligatory (fard) because the obligation transfers to the splint. If it cannot be washed, then the obligation falls away, and wiping is not required. This resolves the apparent contradiction in attributing wujub to the two companions. The ultimate proof is the Quranic verse on removal of hardship.

Key Terms
جبيرة (jabīra): A splint or bandage placed on a wound or broken limb, made from sticks, rags, etc.
عصابة (ʿiṣāba): A bandage or wrap used on a wound, synonymous with jabeera in this context.
عصائب (ʿaṣāʾib): Bandages (plural of 'isabah) i.e., the cloth used to bind the splint.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on wiping over a splint (jabeera) when the wound cannot be exposed or washed, according to the correct opinion (sahih) in the Hanafi school?
A) It is obligatory to wipe over it once.
B) It is recommended but not obligatory.
C) It is not valid; one must perform tayammum instead.
D) It must be wiped three times.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is a valid substitute for washing, wajib once due to ahad hadith and the principle of hardship removal, with internal Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether it is fard or wajib.
